How to Display Help Topics

                                            [F1] = Help

Any time help is needed in RICS press the [F1] key to display the help topic for the current screen.
To use Help, select the Contents button at the top of the RICS Help window. The Help Topics window
displays three tabs: Contents, Index, and Find.
Select the Contents tab to display a list of topics available in RICS Help. Topics are organized in books laid
out much in the order of the screens in RICS. To open a book, double-click it. Continue opening books until
you find the topic you want to read. Click the page icon to display the topic.

In Navigating the Menu, or any topic overview section you can also click on the option key of header menu
to jump to the help topic for that option.

To search for a specific topic or word in Help:
Select the Search button at the top of the RICS Help window. The Help Topics window displays with three
tabs: Contents, Index, and Find. Search using the following options:

     1) Select the Index tab to look up a keyword or phrase in the online index. Browse through the index or
          type the term you're looking for and the list automatically finds the word or phrase you are typing.
          When the search phrase is found (or something comparable), double-click the phrase to display the
          associated help topic associated.

     2) Select the Find tab to search for each instance of a word or phrase throughout RICS Help. Each
          listed topic has the keyword or phrase being searched. Double-click the topic

Colors & Fonts in RICS Help:

Green Underlined Jumps link to another topic. When double-clicked, it jumps to that help topic.

[Bold black text in brackets] refers to a key to press, or text to type in the indicated field.

[Red Text in Brackets] refers to a button to click in RICS.

Burgundy Text refers to either a question or option that would be on the RICS screen for that selected Help
Topic.

Blue Text refers to either a question or option that is shown in an Example used for that selected Help Topic.

To print a RICS Help Topic:
From the page to be printed in the help file, click the Print button, or use the right mouse button to click inside
the Help window, and then click Print Topic.

To print a group of related topics, click a book in the Help Contents and then clicking Print.

To return to the previously viewed topics:
In the Help topic window, click the Back button to return to the previously viewed topics.

To view a list of previously viewed topics:
In the Help topic window, click Options, click Display History Window. This displays all previously viewed
topics since the last time the Help program was opened.

Getting Technical Support

We'll Get You Started Off Right: Your first 60 days are free! That's right--to make sure you get up and
running quickly on RICS, we offer 60 days of support available free of charge to our new clients. Whenever
you have a question just call and one of RICS support specialists will happily assist you!

For Technical Support or to register RICS, call 1-800-654-3123 or (515) 270-8182 during normal office

hours of Monday- Friday 8am to 5pm CST. Messages are taken on weekends and holidays and calls are
returned however no one is usually in the office on these days. Fax us anytime at 515-270-1006. If you
would prefer to handle your support issue by email, you can also email us at help@csi-rics.com. One of the
RICS support specialists will reply to your question just as soon as possible.

Our address is:

                 CSI Services
                 4725 Merle Hay Road, Suite 101
                 Des Moines, IA 50322

To ensure uninterrupted support after your 60-day warranty period has lapsed, we offer an annual support
and upgrade program, where you will receive quality technical support from trained support professionals. As
you use your software to manage your business, we can continue to help you thru our technical staff.

Getting Started - New to RICS

                                                     What to do before you start
After RICS is installed you should experiment with the "practice" data that is installed with RICS. The best
way to learn how RICS works is to practice. Each time you go into an option press [F1] (Help) to display the
Help topic for the current screen. Make sure have read

Navigating the Menu (on page 6) before continuing. Enter "practice" data into RICS. DO NOT enter

your entire inventory. Right now, practice using RICS. Remember, "practice" data will be deleted so you
can't hurt anything. When entering in your "practice" data remember to [Save] the information before you
enter the next item, after you saved an item you can do a Lookup to see the item you just created. You can
also ADD new SKUs, vendors, etc. on the fly when you do a Lookup and select the [ADD] option. If you
have any questions call Support at 1-800-654-3123

Printers
Before starting setup the printer(s). Setup the printer in Windows if it is not setup already. See Printer Setup
in Windows (on page 17) for more information. Next, inform RICS about your printer in Company Setup
under the Printer Setup option (on page 216) also in Labels in the Setup Stock Labels option (on page 82).

Start with File Setup

     · Enter the Store information (on page 141).
     · Locate fifteen or twenty different items in the store. These items are going to be used to setup

          categories, departments, size types, and vendors.
     · Enter six or eight Categories. (on page 145) (DO NOT enter all of your data.)
     · Enter three or four Departments. (on page 144)
     · Define two or three Size Types. (on page 147)
     · Enter five or six Vendors. (on page 153)
     · Enter those fifteen or twenty stock numbers on the SKU's Setup screen. (on page 154)
     · Enter three or four Sales People. (on page 106)

You should now have a good cross section of information entered into RICS. Next, you want to practice
      receiving, ordering, and reviewing these stock numbers.

                           2
Next in Stock Maintenance
     · Use Enter Manual Receipts (on page 66) and receive some "practice" inventory into RICS. (Note:
          This option will be used later to enter your beginning inventory quantities.)
     · Use the option Inventory Inquiry, (on page 70) and view the on-hand quantities of some of the SKUs
          just entered. Get comfortable using this option; minimize this window to keep it active while doing
          more data entry.
     · Use Enter Manual Returns (on page 66) and take some quantities out of inventory. Again, use the
          option Inventory Inquiry.(on page 70)

Enter Purchase Orders
     · Enter three or four orders in Enter Purchase Orders.(on page 56)
     · Receive those orders in Receive Purchase Orders.(on page 57). Receive some of the purchase
          orders in full, and some receive only partially.

Print Labels
     · Stock labels are printed using the option Print Stock Labels. (on page 83)
     · Practice receiving more merchandise and printing stock labels again. Repeat this several times.

Move on to Sales
     · Enter sales on the main computer using Enter Sales (on page 28). Please review the Ticket Overview
          (on page 21) section carefully. Don't just enter a few sales, enter quite a few, and practice with the
          different types of transactions.
     · Print Sales Journals (on page 44) and Post Sales to Inventory (on page 45) are the final steps in the
          inventory cycle.
     · Practice Backup Data,(on page 184) and Backup Files for POS, (on page 176) on this computer and
          then Restore Data from Main on the POS computer.

You will also need to collect your store data information. Make a list of the Departments, Categories,
    Size Types, Vendors, SKUs, and Employees for your store(s) to be entered later.

Continue to practice all the above steps until you are comfortable with every step before going on to
Entering New Store Data. (on page 4)

                        YOU MUST DELETE PRACTICE DATA!!

Contact Technical Support for help deleting the "practice" data information entered on the computer, before
entering your real data.

                                                                                           3
Entering New Store Data

                                                  Before entering your "real" data
You should have the information you collected earlier to enter your Department, Category, Size Type, Vendor,
SKU, and Employee data. Initial setup of any system is always the most time consuming part, but once your
data is all entered you'll find you may seldom need to change anything other than new SKUs. You don't need
to enter every record immediately because with RICS you have the ability to Add on the fly, but it may be
easier to enter many records at once. It's also a good idea to enter as much data as you can before you start
entering the inventory. The best way to enter your data is in the order as listed below.

Start by Setting up your Company Preferences -
Once these options are set up, your preferences would very rarely ever change.

Company Setup -Information on your company preferences (on page 214).
Mail List Setup -Information on your mail list preferences for customers (Optional- on page 218).
Season Setup -Information on your season preferences for SKUs (Optional- on page 218).

Then do File Setup
Once these files are setup, they would seldom change, expect for new SKUs.

Store - Information on your Stores, Tenders, and Taxes (on page 141).
Categories - Information on your Categories (on page 145).
Departments - Information on your Departments (on page 144).
(Optional) Groups - Information on your Groups (on page 145).
Size Types - Information on your Size Types (on page 147).
Vendors - Information on your Vendors (on page 153).
SKU's - Information on your SKUs the heart of the system (on page 154).

Depending on how you plan to setup your system, you may not want to create a SKU for all items you have in
the store. You may want to create Dump SKUs for older items, discontinued items, departments, or for
vendors. Or you may want to create some Dump SKUs to track sales until you get all your SKUs entered in
the system.

Sales People - Information about your Salespeople is entered in the Sales People Menu (on page 106).

Next step is to enter your inventory in Stock Maintenance
Have a plan on how you'll enter your inventory, either by vendor, category, etc.

Enter Manual Receipts ­ (on page 66) to enter your beginning inventory quantities for each SKU. If printing
stock labels it is recommended that you do not enter your entire inventory at once, instead enter several
SKUs, or maybe one vendor at a time, print those labels, then label those SKUs and repeat, otherwise it may
be difficult to locate all the SKUs with all the labels printed out at once.

Print Stock Labels. - Stock labels are printed using this option, and then label all items. (on page 83)

Backup Files for POS, on this computer and then Restore Data from Main on the POS computer. (on page
176)

Enter your Sales at the POS, Close the Batch of Sales, Copy Sales to Diskette at the POS, and then at the
main computer Copy from POS Diskette. Remember you must Print Sales Journals and Post Sales to
Inventory for the sales to be deducted from inventory, and credited as sales.

                                                                                           4
Logging into RICS

Enter a valid User ID and Password and click [Login].
To train employees on Entering Sales, login as a user that would normally login to this terminal (Ex: POS) and
click [Practice Sales]. After clicking the button, the user is prompted to copy current RICS data files to a
practice directory. This login will allow the person being trained to enter practice sales without disturbing the
live sales file.

                                                                                           5
Navigating the Menu

The RICS Main Menu has two parts: The Top Portion is the Main Menu Options, and the Bottom Portion
is the Choices for the Active Main Menu Option.
Notice the menu above. The Sales option is highlighted in the top portion of the menu which indicates the
menu is active, so the available menu option Choices for Sales are then displayed below.
To select a Main Menu Option you can (1) click on the option, or (2) use your [Tab] or arrow keys to highlight
and press [Enter] to activate or (3) Select the option and choice from the Options menu on the top of the
screen [Alt] + [O].
To select a Choice (1) click on the choice, or (2) use your [Tab] or arrow keys to highlight and press [Enter]
or (3) Select the option and choice from the Options menu on the top of the screen [Alt] + [O].
Underlined Options (i.e. Post Sales to Inventory) can be linked together with other Underlined Options
and can be put into a Job List to run together. Data entry type screens (i.e. Enter Sales) cannot put in the job
list.

                                                                                           6
Report Options

                                                      Selecting Options/Reports
Report Options will vary from report to report to report, and may be as simply as one line asking for
Stores:_____ or it could be a series of folders, where you would may have many different options in each
folder.
How you select the options and choose the Criteria or Wild Cards (on page 8) will change how the report will
appear, you can basically custom format any report this way.
Depending on the report options chosen, you may not be able to choose other options on the same report,
you can then un-check some options, or clicking [Clear Selections] or press the [Alt] + [L] keys at the same
time will clear the current entry that was displayed.
Any Underlined Report/Option will have a line for a Report Comment:____, when you enter a comment
you can then Save Current Selection which is that report's layout to run again later. By setting the report
comment to "DEFAULT", the next time you run this report, the selection screen will display the default options
you selected. If no default report selection exists the last report options are selected.

Once saved, you can then Retrieve Saved Selection to run that report/option layout again and again, without
re selecting the report options or criteria. This is a great way to run routine reports such as end of the week
reports, or options such as to call stores.

Underlined Options can be linked together with other Underlined Options and can be put into a Job List to
run together or to create a Super Job.(on page 189)

                                                                                           7
Criteria / Wild Cards

                                           Selecting Information Criteria for Reports
Before running a report, you determine what information should or should not print. When selecting most
reports, a criteria option will display the same choices as the last time you ran that report. The new report
may be run the same way, or you may change any of the selections for a different report. Wild Card
selections may be entered for all reports. Following are some of the Criteria choices available when printing a
report:

INCLUDE INFORMATION: To PRINT ALL leave that selection BLANK. To print selected information,
separate ranges with a hyphen "-", and individual choices with a comma ",". For example: Categories 100-
199,250-260, 350, 500 If entering a numeric range, separate the beginning and ending values with a hyphen
"-" , this must be numeric only and also must be the same number of characters. For example: 2000-2999
will print all 4 digit numeric entries from 2000 to 2999. But if you entered 2-35 this will not print entries from 2
to 35. Instead, this will select all entries of any length or are alpha numeric that the entry begins with any
characters between 2 and 35. For instance 22135 and 29/BLK would also be included in this selection.

EXCLUDE INFORMATION: All report selections allow for exclusions ("< >" less than sign followed by the
greater than sign). This means you can run all of a selection except certain selections. For instance, you
can print a report for all vendors except NIKE, all categories except 400-449, all stores except 3 and 10, all
seasons except 8, etc. For example: < >NIKE would include ALL vendors EXCEPT NIKE. < >400-449 would
include ALL categories EXCEPT 400 through 449. < >3, < >10 would include ALL stores EXCEPT 3 and 10.

KEYWORD CONSIDERATIONS: When selecting Keywords, it may desirable to have an SKU's keywords
match all of the selected keywords, rather than just 1. If the first selection in the keyword field is an addition
sign [+], only SKUs meeting ALL the selected keyword criteria will be included (or excluded) in the report.

Wild Cards

            Selects Multiple or Similar Characters

All reports also allow you to make selections using wild cards. A wild card is a method that allows the

computer to select multiple, similar entries using certain characters. A question mark "?" in an SKU selection

indicates that any character can occupy that position.  For example: SKUs

???37,12??,12???,??10????,10000-25000 This would print SKUs that are 5 characters long and end with

37 or SKUs that are 4 or 5 characters long and begin with '12' or SKUs that are 8 characters long that have

10 for the 3rd and 4th characters of the SKU and SKUs between 10000 and 25000.

An asterisk "*" in the selection will select all entries with any characters after the "*" if it is the last character in
the selection or any character before the "*" if it is the first character in the selection. For example: 58* would
select all entries of any length that begin with the number 58 and are followed by any character of any length.
For instance 58, 5872BLK, and 589999999 would be included in this selection. *BLK would select all entries

            8
of any length that end with "BLK" and begin with any number of combination of characters. For instance
MARY/BLK, 5872BLK, and JILL5-BLK would be included in this selection.

If you are selecting an individual entry to print such as 100-120, and that entry (such as an SKU or a mail list)
has a hyphen in the entry, you must specify that the hyphen in this instance is not specifying a range. To do
this precede the hyphen with a Exclamation point "!" or [Shift] +[1] . For Example: 100!-120 Would select
ONLY the SKU number "100-120" and not all entries between 100 and 200.

To get to a DOS Prompt you must be at the desktop, follow these steps exactly in this order:

     1. Select "Start" by clicking the mouse on "Start" from the Desktop
     2. Select "Programs"
     3. Select "MS-DOS Prompt"
     4. You will then be at C:\WINDOWS> type in CD\ and press [Enter], you will then be

         at the C:\> prompt.

To get to a RICS prompt, from the DOS Prompt or C:\> prompt type in cd\ricswin and press [Enter].

icon you may access the records for that field, these fields would include SKUs, Customers by Account
#'s, Customers by Name, Family Members, Stores, Vendors, Departments, Categories, Size Types,
Groups, and Users.

     1. Click on the Look up icon

the same time.

10
Clear, Save, Delete, Copy, Exit, Exit RICS

In all data enter or function screens the [Clear] button appears. Clicking the [Clear] button, or pressing the
[Alt] + [C] keys at the same time, clears the current entry that was displayed.

In all report screens the [Clear Selections] button appears. Clicking the [Clear Selections] button, or
pressing the [Alt] + [L] keys at the same time, will clear all information entered and reset them to the default
report selections.

In all data entry or function screens, the [Save] button appears. Clicking the [Save] button, or pressing the
[Alt] + [S] keys at the same time, saves the current entry that was displayed.

In all data entry or function screens, the [Delete] button appears. Clicking the [Delete] button, or pressing the
[Alt] + [D] keys at the same time, deletes the current entry that was displayed.

In all data entry or function screens, the [Copy] button appears. Clicking the [Copy] button, or pressing the
[Alt] + [O] keys at the same time, copies the current entry that was displayed.

Click the [Exit] button, or pressing the [Ctrl] + [X] keys at the same time, exits the current screen. You may
also exit by clicking Help at the top of the screen and choosing Exit, or exit by clicking the X Box at the top
right hand corner of the current screen.
Press the [Ctrl] + [M] keys at the same time to return to the Main Menu without exiting the current screen.
You may also return to the Main Menu by clicking Help at the top of the screen and choosing Main Menu.

Click the [Exit RICS] button, or pressing the [Ctrl] + [X] keys at the same time, to close all screens and exit
RICS. You may also exit by clicking Options at the top of the screen and choosing Exit.

Or you may also exit by clicking the [X] (Exit) Box at the top right hand corner of the current screen.

                                                                                          11
Reading Reports

                                                      The Key to your Business
With the many different options in the RICS reports you should be able to obtain any key information you may
want to know about your inventory or customers, but the key to any report is to review the information and not
just run the report.

(Best Sellers Report in order of ROI%)

A very simple way to tell how any item is doing in your store is to compare it to your store average this should
be your key indicator as to what items, categories, or vendors are above or below your store average. On
any report look at the store average for either GP%, Turns, or ROI%, with ROI% being the key number. Any
items above that number are performing better, and any items less than that number are the poor performers,
these items should be looked at very carefully for ways to improve their performance. Remember the old 80-
20 rule, At any given time of the year, about 80% of the business is done with about 20% of the
inventory.

ROI% (Return on Investment Percentage) - Sometimes known as GMROI (Gross Margin Return on
Investment) is a combined measurement of how quickly your inventory sold, and how profitable it was. The
ROI% is always annualized regardless of what period is being analyzed.
It is strongly recommended that you use ROI% as part of your inventory review, because it is the best
overall indicator of performance.

Key Reports to Run
Sales Analysis: (on page 88) When running a Sales Analysis for week-to-date or month-to-date totals you
may only want to run the report using a department, vendor, or category summary to see areas that may be
strong and/or weak against your store average at a glance, and then run this report again by SKU detail for
those selected areas, this should be a smaller and easier amount of data to review.
Week-to-Date: to get weekly totals, and review, before you close the week.
Month-to-Date: to get monthly totals, and review, before you close the month.
Year-to-Date: to get yearly totals, and review, before you close the year. You will probably want to run this
several different ways such as by SKU detail, Vendor summary, and category summary.
8 Week Trending: when ever you want to know the trends of how items are selling. This is very important
when reordering, or considering markdowns.

Best Sellers Report: (on page 93) This report can be used to print your best/worst selling SKUs, sorted by
quantity sold, dollars sold, dollars profit, ROI%, or turns.
Before Reordering: To check the best selling items for reorders.
Before working with a Vendor: It's a good idea to run this just by the vendor to show them how their items
are selling by ranking them from best to worst, you can also show them GP%, turns, and ROI%. This will also
show them how they performed over all. You may also want to run this by selecting Best by Vendor to show
them how they rank against your other Vendors. At least once a year every line should be appraised on their
performance based on it's ROI%, Sales, Turns and Markdowns, before Buying for Next Season, Before a
Promotion, Special, or Markdowns: It's a good idea to run this report by worst by to see your slow movers,
or by

Recommended Transfers: (on page 79) This report can help you balance your inventory between stores you

                                                                                          12
may want to run this quite often, and before reordering. This allows the following options Print based on:
Selects the method to report by. Uneven on hand (doubles) prints SKUs that have two or more on hand of
a size at one store and none at another. Selecting High turnover variance of at least prints SKUs that are
selling at a faster % rate (regardless of size) at one store than they are at another. Example: 500% would
print any SKU selling 5 times faster at one store than another.

Size Type Analysis: (on page 99) The key to this report is timing. It should be run periodically during the year
and at the end of the season before any large-scale markdowns. The intent is to determine which
columns/rows are selling at the best rate and which columns/rows are over or under stocked. You can also
check next season's future orders to see if you ordered the right sizes by running on-order (Future) quantity.
Check by color and size (i.e. white shoes on order), to compare with a previous report to see if on order
quantities reflect previous sell thru %.

Employee Analysis: (on page 111) Allows you to measure individual employee productivity and compared
them to other sales people and to store averages. Whether you pay commissions or not, these reports
generate the information to reward excellent performance or critique poor performance, and provide
guidelines on areas to improve selling behavior.

Sales by Time: (on page 41) This report will show sales amounts and quantities sold for each hour of
business. This report may be useful for scheduling purposes, and the two date ranges allows you to do
comparisons.

Marketing Tools

                              To Get the Most Out of Your "Preferred Customer" Mail List
Direct Mail if properly prepared and executed can be the most effective and least costly form of advertising.
Getting customers on your list can be done several different ways, whether you simply ask for the information,
have the customer fill out a card, or take the information off their check. One of the easiest ways to obtain
information is by using a Frequent Buyer Plan (on page 201), which gives the customer a incentive to get on
your list because you reward them for making purchases in your store. You can also run reports or lists for
Frequent Buyers customers by Plan #, Quantity, or Dollars spent.

Any of the following options can be printed to labels to stick on cards, or envelopes, exported to a file to work
with your word processor to create personalized cards, letters, or envelopes, it can be copied to a diskette to
give a mail processor, or printed as a list to hand write letters/cards or to be used as a phone list to call your
customers. You can run these options for the entire company, or select by Store, Vendor, category, or
individual salesperson. These are just a few ideas and how to run them.

New Customers: To run a list of all new customers under Sales Criteria enter in the Added to the
computer from __ to __ the date since you last ran this option, this should be done within two weeks of
when the new customer made their first purchase and followed up with a thank you card, letter, or phone call.

Old Customers who haven't purchase: To run a list of old customers under Sales Criteria enter in the Date
of last purchase from __ to __ the date since you last ran this option, this is a great way to contact

Thank You Cards Simply send a follow up thank you card or letter to the customer for making their purchase
in your store. Customers appreciate and remember this extra contact with them. To run a list of recent
customer purchases under Sales Criteria enter in the Date of last purchase from __ to __ is the date since
you last ran this option, this should be done within two weeks of the purchase.

PT's (Personal Trade): Under Mail List Setup (on page 218) create a field for the Salesperson's name, then
all your salespeople can see who the customer's personal salesperson is. You can then also select mail list
options for the selected salesperson.

Top Spending Customers: To run a list most Dollar purchases under Sales Criteria enter in the PTD, YTD,
or TTD the amount range in dollars (i.e. 500-99999) this example would print any customer who purchased
from $500 to $99,999.

                                                                                          13
Check Size Reminder Cards (Children): To run a list for size reminders under Sales Criteria enter in the
Date of last purchase from __ to __ for the date range you want, if this is also for selected categories under
Detail Criteria enter in the Category.

Birthday Cards: To enter birthday information select [Family] when entering Mail List information there is an
area for the birthday information. To print select Print Mailing List (Family) (on page 126) then choose Family
Criteria and enter the Birth Date from __ to __ and select the Birth Month.

Gender: To enter gender information select [Family] when entering Mail List information there is an area for
the gender information. To print, select Print Mailing List (Family) then, Family Criteria and enter the Gender
information.

Special Size Promotions: First run a Size Type Analysis to locate the sizes that you need to move. Then
under Detail Criteria enter in the Column/Row information. This type of promotion is best setup as a
Personalized Letter to the customer.

Personalized Letters: Select the report to run as a Export comma-delimited file and give it a name, then in
your word processor create your form letter, and then mail-merge with this file.

Trunk Shows / Vendor Promotions: To run a list of customers who purchased from a selected vendor or
category use Detail Criteria and enter in the selected Vendor or Category.

Phone List: Select your criteria and run your report as either a Wide or Narrow Report.

Customer Detail Records: To enable you to give the customer better service, by knowing what, and when
they have purchased in the past, plus comment areas, this can be printed at the POS.

Top Performance

         To get the most out of RICS be sure you're using some key features to enter data quicker,
                                         focus your reporting, and staying on budget

Eliminate entering the same sizes by setting up Case Packs, (on page 161) which are a preset group of
quantities you create for selected columns and rows. They are used in any option that allows size entry, to
speed up the entering of data. To use case packs, you would enter the case pack number and the quantity
would be automatically displayed. Create your own case packs for sizes you normally carry in your store
(such as a 24 pair size run in N, M, W).

Quit entering Job after Job to run, by combining Jobs together in a Super Job (on page 189), to run again
and again without re-entering any of the information. A must for calling stores, or End of the Month reports.

Stop typing the same information over and over by creating Macros.(on page 205) A macro is a single
keystroke that represents a series of keystrokes. The best time to use a macro is when the same information
is typed continually. This is a great tool for entering the same information such as a City, State & Zip code.

Never again select criteria for reports or options that you run again and again by entering a Report
Comment. (on page 7) Once saved, you can then Retrieve Saved Selection to run that report/option layout
again and again, without re-selecting the report options or criteria. This is a great way to run routine reports
such as end of the week reports, or other options such as to call stores.

For each report, you can create a default job by typing [DEFAULT] in the Report Comment field and save
(or add the job) to save the report settings. The next time the selection screen is pulled up for that report, the
DEFAULT job is loaded even if different settings for this report were used on the previous (LAST) job.

Creating Model Quantities can make Reordering Easy for selected SKUs and then running Automatic
Purchase Orders. (on page 59)

Focus Reports and Make Easy Price Changes by setting up Seasons (on page 218) and creating
Groups.(on page 145)

                                                                                          14
Stay on Budget with an Open-to-Buy Plan (on page 158) and Buy the Right Sizes and Quantities by using
Order Worksheets. (on page 61)

Easily Receive Merchandise or Check Late Deliveries buy creating Purchase Orders. (on page 56)

Contact Customers by using the Marketing Tools.(on page 13)

POS Equipment/Setup

                                                   To install your POS equipment
This is only applicable if you purchased your POS equipment from CSI Services. Contact your hardware
supplier for equipment purchased elsewhere.

WARNING: DO NOT connect/disconnect anything to/from your computer while your computer has the
power turned on.

CONNECTING RECEIPT PRINTER
Install the ribbon and receipt paper according to the printer's instructions. Connect the printer cable to the
back of the printer. The other end of the cable will connect to the back of the computer.

Before using your printer be sure you have (1) Setup the printer in Windows, (2) RICS Printer Setup and (3)
Manager's Options. The Manager's Options screen is displayed the VERY FIRST time you use the POS
software, or by pressing [Manager Options] from the Ticket Header section of the sales screen.

CONNECTING CASH DRAWER
Your cash drawer will connect via a "telephone-style" cable to the back of your receipt printer. Your
receipt printer will have a black plug over the cash drawer connection, remove the plug and insert the
cable. You need to indicate in RICS where your cash drawer is connected in Manager's Options

CONNECTING the BAR CODE READER

You bar code reader will already be programmed if purchased from CSI, and should work without doing
anything "special" in RICS, or to the bar code reader. Keep any information that was sent with the scanner
for future reference.

PSC 6000 Decoded Scanner
A "Y" shaped cable will interface the laser between your keyboard and the back of your computer.

     1. With the computer turned off, disconnect the keyboard cable from your computer.
     2. Plug the small male plug of the "Y" cable to the keyboard port (connection) on the computer.
     3. Attach the keyboard cable to the female plug of the "Y" cable.
     4. Turn on the computer.

If the connections do not fit your computer just switch the adapter to the other side of the connector.

Percon Power Wedge 20, PSC Undecoded Scanner, & Credit Card Reader
A "Y" shaped cable will interface the Power Wedge 20 Decoder to the back of your computer.

     1. With the computer turned off, disconnect the keyboard cable from your computer.
     2. Plug the 25 pin connector of the cable in the back of the Percon PW20 marked Host Input.
     3. Plug the small male plug of the "Y" cable to the keyboard port (connection) on the computer.
     4. Attach the keyboard cable to the female plug of the "Y" cable.

                                                                                          15
5. Attach the laser scanner to the front of the Percon PW20 mark Input 1.
6. Set the Percon PW20 power switch to the ON position.
7. Turn on the computer.

Credit Card Reader
The device that reads the magnetic stripe on a credit card for account information to automatically be
processed for a credit card transaction. Attach the credit card scanner to the front of the Percon PW20 mark
Input 2.

TESTING YOUR BAR CODE READER
Test you reader by scanning some UPC bar codes from a DOS Prompt; 12 digits should appear on the
screen, if not contact Technical Support.

POS Platform

              Neatly organizes your keyboard, printer, monitor, and Pole Display
                          to fit on top of the cash drawer and hides cables.

Customer Pole Display
Shows the customer information about the transaction that includes the description of the product, quantity,
price and change from the transaction. It may also be used for marketing or other information, allowing two
lines of up to 20 characters per line to be displayed. The pole display will connect to the serial port in the
computer; contact Technical Support on how to setup messages.

Modems

To perform communications between your main computer and POS computers, we strongly recommend
using either a Hayes Accura or Zoom external 56K modem. Many internal modems that are purchased with
computers are sometimes not totally Hayes compatible, or are often poorer quality modems, which causes
more communications problems. External Hayes Accura or Zoom are the only Modems CSI recommends.
The modem is connected thru a serial or com port on the back of the computer. The phone line is then
connected to the back of the modem in the line jack outlet; a phone can also be attached to the modem thru
the jack outlet marked phone.
Make sure you have no other devices on this phone line that will answer calls, such as a fax or answering
machine. For more information see Communications File Setup (on page 161) and Communications Setup.
(on page 214)

Printer Setup in Windows / Bar Code Printer

                                           To Setup or Change a printer in Windows
For RICS to know about your printer it must first be setup in Windows 95/98. To perform this setup, follow
these steps exactly in this order:

From the Windows Desktop:
      1. Select "Start" by clicking the mouse on "Start"
      2. Select "Settings"
      3. Select "Printers" to open the printers folder.
      4. Click the mouse ONCE on the selected printer you plan to use in RICS:
          (If there are no printers to select from on the screen, use Add Printer to add your printer driver see
          Add Printer below.) Do Not use the Printer Driver diskette that may have come with your printer.
      5. Select "File"
      6. Select "Properties"
      7. Select the "Details" tab.
      8. Select "Port settings" and the small configure LPT port box will appear.
      9. Click ONCE on "Spool MS-DOS print jobs" to remove the check mark
     10. Select "OK"
     11. Select "OK" again
     12. Close the job by clicking on X in the upper right hand corner

Now your system should return to the Windows 95 Desktop and be ready for the Printer Setup in RICS.

To Add a Printer
Follow steps 1-3 as shown above only in step 4 select Add Printer as your choice, and the Add Printer
Wizard will appear.

     4A. Select "Next" to begin installing the printer.
     4B. Select "Local Printer" and click "Next" to continue.
     4C. Highlight you choice from the Manufacturers List on the left and the Printers listed on the right.

          Select "Next" to continue.
     4D. Highlight the port (usually LPT1) from the list of Available ports and select Configure Port.
     4E. Configure the port as shown in steps 9 & 10 above.
     4F. The configure port box will close, select "Next" to continue.
     4G. Enter the printer name and select "Next" to continue.
     4H. Select "Finish" to complete the installation.

If using a separate bar code printer it is recommended that you have a 2nd Parallel Printer Port installed in
your computer, or purchase a USB Parallel Printer Adapter which allows you to connect a Parallel printer

format 1.25"X1.00"), with the option of custom formats on all labels.

The printer must be setup in both Printer Setup and Stock Label Setup.

Portable Bar Code Reader_ Percon PT2000

                To scan a physical inventory, PO receipts, manual receipts, and transfers
                                               This section describes how to use the Percon PT2000 portable bar
                                               code reader (loaded with CSI APP Software Program). It is used to
                                               scan bar codes on your merchandise, to enter physical inventory
                                               counts, manual receipts, manual returns, PO receipts, and/or transfers
                                               between stores. Before using the Percon unit for actual counts,
                                               experiment with scanning bar codes, manually entering counts and
                                               getting familiar with the different keys on the reader.

                PERCON KEYPAD
                The PT2000 keypad has three types of keys: data keys, function keys,
                and action keys. Each key produces an audible beep when you press
                it.

                Data Keys: Data keys are used to enter letters, numbers, and several
                other characters. Each key has two modes: normal and alpha. You
                use the [Alpha] key to switch between the modes. (See Alpha key
                below).

                Function Keys: There are four function keys, F1 through F4, at the
                top of the keypad. When pressing the Alpha key, these keys change to

F5 through F8.

Action Keys: There are four action keys: I/O, Alpha, BKSP, and ENTER.
     I/O: Press this key to turn the PT2000 on and off.

Alpha: Press the Alpha key to toggle between the normal and alpha modes. When in the Alpha
mode, a caret ( ^ ) appears at the cursor position in the display screen. The PT2000 remains in the
alpha mode until you press a function key, enter a quantity, or press the Alpha key again.

BKSP: This is the backspace key. Press it to move the cursor one place to the left and delete the
character there.

     ENTER: Press this key to enter the current data string and move to the next area.

The following screen is the first menu you see then the unit is turned on:
PERCON PORTABLE
10:06:10 (Current Time)
01/11/97 (Current Date)
F-KEY=CONTINUE
Press any of the Keys F1 -F4 to continue

The next screen will then be displayed:
PERCON CSI APP
F2=WEDGE
F3=COLLECT DATA
Select one of the options:

F2=WEDGE is used to setup the PT2000 as a keyboard wedge to attach a scanner to a PC to scan directly
into the computer. Contact CSI before using this option.

F3=COLLECT DATA is to use the PT2000 as a portable bar code reader use this option to do inventory,
transfers, receipts or returns.

                18
Press the F3 Key to continue and the following
MAIN MENU is displayed:

F1=ENTER DATA
F2=SEND FILE
F3=ERASE
F4=EXIT

         SCANNING INVENTORY

F1=ENTER DATA (COUNTS): Press the [F1] key
and the following DATA Screen is displayed:

STORE NUMBER Physical Inventory: Enter a 2-digit store number (i.e.: 01, 02, etc.)

When Scanning Transfers, Receipts or Returns, YOU MUST enter store number as "00"!

The appropriate transfer or receiving store numbers are entered on the computer when you select "Post Data
from Portable Reader".

Press Enter after entering the store number and the
following UPC Screen is displayed:

To Change a Store Number: Press F3 = REV (Review), Press F5 = 1st(1st Record), Press F7 = MOD
(Modify), Enter the new Store Number, Press Enter.

In the UPC Screen, just scan the bar code for each item you want counted. When a bar code is scanned, and
a good read has taken place, the PT2000 will beep, the screen will clear, and you may then scan another bar
code. There is nothing to enter, just scan bar codes one after another.

The F Keys (Function Keys) Used when entering data are as follows:

F1=SKU   to manually enter an item by the SKU#, COL, ROW, and quantity.
         (In the SKU Mode, F1=UPC will take you back to UPC mode)
F3=REV   Takes you to the REVIEW MODE
F4=EXIT  Takes you back to the MAIN MENU.

                                                REVIEW MODE

When the reader is in the REVIEW MODE the following keys are available. If you forget what function keys
are available in the REVIEW MODE, press F8=HELP. Then press any function key (F?=CONT) to return to
REVIEW MODE.

F1=PREV Displays the Previous Record
F2=NEXT Displays the Next Record
F3=DEL Deletes Current Record on the screen
F4=EXIT Returns you to Enter Data Mode
F5=1st Takes you to the 1st Record in the file
F6=FIND Finds a UPC or SKU record
F7=MOD Allows you to modify the quantity for a count
F?=CONT Press any function key to continue in REVIEW MODE

Entering PO Receipts
When entering or scanning PO receipts into the portable reader, at the SKU Screen, enter the PO number
being received in the SKU field. Then enter REC for the COL (column) and PO for the RW (row), press
ENTER, then press the F1 key (F1=UPC) to scan UPCs. The following entries will be used as quantities
received for that PO number. If you wish to enter receipts for another PO, again enter the new PO number as
SKU, REC as column, and PO as row.

                                                     19
Transferring the counts from the Reader
Make sure the computer is ready to receive data from the portable reader by selecting F5) Physical
Inventory, C) Get Data from Portable Reader. Connect the "direct connect" cable to the bottom of the
PT2000 and to the serial port on the computer. (If you are not attaching to COM 1, you will need to contact
CSI to change the configuration.) From the Main Menu on the PT2000, press the F2 key (F2=SEND FILE),
and the following screen will appear:
Press the F2 key (F2=CONTINUE) and the counts will
be transferred to the computer. [Next run F5) Physical
Inventory, D) Post data from portable reader.]
Deleting ALL Counts from the Reader
All counts need to be deleted after the counts have been successfully transferred to the computer and you
have successfully ran F5) Physical Inventory, D) Post data from portable reader. From the Main Menu, Press
the F3 key (F3=ERASE), the following screen will appear:
Press the F3 key (F3=ERASE). The reader has now been cleared and can be used for more counts.

PT 2000 Fixes

No beam comes from the scanner:
Take off battery cover on the back and remove the batteries, then replace the batteries, this will reset the unit.
Unit is frozen, no keys work:
Take off battery cover on the back and remove one of the batteries, hold down both the Enter and the Alpha
keys keep hold these keys down and replace the battery while holding down these keys, this will do a
complete system reset.
The data in the unit will be lost while doing this.

Overview             SSAALLEESS

          For Entering Sales Screens and Tickets

Before entering sales you must setup certain options that will appear on your sales ticket screen, how and
were you want receipts printed.
Managers Options - Set Options for Sales Tickets.
Additional Sales Ticket Options - (Optional)
Currency Options - (Optional)
All sales are grouped to together in a batch, the complete sales cycle would consist of:

     1. Start a Batch of Sales - to start entering tickets.
     2. Enter Sales Tickets - enters Sales and Customer information.
     3. Close a Batch of Sales - ends the current batch of sales
     4. Copy Sales - From the POS/Register to the main computer.
     5. Print Sales Journal - Prints the daily sales transactions.
     6. Post Sales to Inventory - Posting Sales will deduct the items sold from inventory.

Manager Options

                                                   Sets Options for Sales Tickets
The Manager's Options screen is displayed the very first time Enter Sales is selected, or by clicking [Manager
Options] when in the Batch Header or Ticket Header section of Enter Sales. If no Password exists, you
will be at:
Beginning Receipt Message - Ending Receipt Message
Up to five lines of text can be printed at the beginning and end of each sales ticket. These lines could be
used to print store name/address and your return policy. Each line can be formatted to print with a different
style of text, check the _ Bold and/or _ Large box or leave un-checked for normal print. Note: Any line with
bold and/or large print is not displayed on the screen any differently. A "large" line can only have half the
number of available characters. For example, a 40 column receipt can only print 20 characters in large print.
[Center Messages] will automatically center your messages.
The following screen determines basic functionality for the sales screen, and shows a normal setup for
equipment purchased from CSI.

# Lines on receipt and # Lines to print: Leave blank for pre-printed/perforated receipts, indicate the #
lines on receipt/to print (6 lines per inch).
Default tender type: Enter a number for the default tender type to display on the sales screen, (i.e. 1 for
cash) or leave blank for no default tender type. See Tender Types.
Default transaction: Enter a number for the default transaction type to display on the sales screen, (i.e. 1 =
regular sale).
Auto # receipts: Checked on for the receipts to number consecutively, automatically or left un-checked
allows the receipt number to be entered before each transaction.
Allow perks $: Checked on will display a field that allows perks to be entered with each sales transaction,
left un-checked no field is displayed. Perks can also be set up for each SKU's.
Allow discounts: Checked on will display a field that allows a discount percentage to be entered left un-
checked no field is displayed for discounts. The price can always be over-ridden whether this is checked on
or not.
Automatically Post: This should be left unchecked. If you have a network, contact your support person for
more information.
Receipt Format: This option is for your printer and should be set for 40 Column. (For printers purchased
from CSI)

                                                                                          22
There are three choices of pricing information that will print on the customer's receipt, select one.
Net Price Only: The price the item sells for is the only price (Net) that is printed on the receipt.
Retail & Discount: Both the retail price and discount amount are printed, but not the net selling price.
Retail, Discount & Net: All three of the prices are printed on the receipt.

                                                                                          23
Cash Drawer:
No Cash Drawer if no cash drawer is used.
Com Port if the cash drawer is connected to COM Port, it will then ask for the COM PORT #.
Attached to Printer if the cash drawer is connected to a printer, it will then ask for the Printer Codes. These
are the decimal codes that are sent from the printer to the cash drawer in order to make the cash drawer
open.

                     If you have a STAR receipt printer purchased from CSI, enter 07 in the first box and make
                           sure the other boxes are blank.

                     If you have an EPSON TM series receipt printer enter 27, 112, 0, 25, 250 in each box,
                           respectively.

                     If you have a different printer, consult your printer manual.

# of Receipts to print should be set to 1. If you want to always print multiple receipts, enter the number of
receipts in this field.

[Cash Totals] This brief report is a Sales Recap broken down by transaction type, a Cash Drawer Recap
broken down by tender type and a Void Summary. You may also [Print] these Cash Totals.

[Open Drawer] This will open the cash drawer.

Sales Ticket Options

Required Account Numbers for Selected Transaction Types.
Required Account Numbers for Selected Tender Types.
Automatically Reprint Sales Tickets.
Additional Ending Messages for Selected Transaction Types.
Additional Ending Messages for Selected Tender Types.

Contact Customer Support for more information about implementing or changing any of these
features.

Required Account Numbers for Transactions: RICS will allow the user to set options to require Account
Numbers to be entered for selected transactions types. You may want to have account numbers required for
all layaway sales & payments, special order deposits & pickups and all house charge payments.

Required Account Numbers for Tender Types: RICS will allow the user to set options to require Account
Numbers to be entered for selected tender types. You may want to have account numbers required for all
house charge, store credits or all refunds.

Reprint Sales Tickets: RICS will allow the user to set options to automatically reprint sales tickets for
selected transactions types. The system will be preset to reprint layaway sales, layaway payments, and
special order deposits. You may also configure RICS to manually reprint sales tickets on demand.

Additional Ending Messages: RICS will allow the user to create special messages to print after your normal
ending receipt message for the following:

     · All sales tickets.
     · Selected transactions types (such as special orders and layaways).
     · Tickets tendered by House Charges.
     · Refund tickets with a negative total.

These messages could be your store refund policy, layaway policy, special order policy, or a signature line for
refunds or House Charges.

                                                                                          24
Currency Options

Displayed only if it is setup in the RICS.CFG file. Contact Technical Support for more information on setting
up this option.

When you go into Enter Sales Batch Header click on the [Currency Options] button or press [Alt] + [C] to get
to the following screen:

Enter your Conversion Factor (exchange rate), check on/off Print Foreign Currency Total on the Receipt
and enter the number of Decimals on Receipt (0-4).
Currency Tender: When tendering a sales ticket in foreign currency you will have two columns for tender, the
left hand column is for dollars and the right hand column is for the foreign currency with the description above
it, and the calculated exchange rate entered. You can enter the tendered amount in either column depending
on the currency given, and you then also have the option to select how to Give Change in ___ by check on
the option below, the exchange rate is also displayed.

Start New/Close a Batch of Sales

                                        Sales Tickets are grouped in a Batch of Sales
Start a Batch of Sales: This screen is used to start a new batch of sales. It is displayed when you go to
Enter Sales and the previous batch of sales has been closed, if this screen does not come up when Enter
Sales is selected, you have not closed the previous batch of sales. Any time sales are entered for a different
store and/or date, you should Start a New Batch of Sales. After all sales for a given store and/or date are
entered you should close the current batch of sales. A Batch of Sales needs to be transferred from a
POS/register to the main computer by Copy Sales to Diskette, or by a modem Call, where the sales need to
be Printed on a Sales Journal and Posted to Inventory before they actually take effect.

                                                                                          25
Store: Enter the store number of the sales being entered and the last ticket # used will appear.
Last ticket #: It is best to let this number increment each day, if you do not change this number your
tickets will continue to increment from the last time you entered sales. It is not recommended to restart at
ticket number one (1) each day. The first ticket number will be one number higher than this number. For
example: a -0- will start the tickets at 1. If you don't want users to be able to change the last ticket number in
RICS, change the RICS.CFG entry Sales Screen, Item ChgTicket, to have a value of 'N',
Date: This is the date of the sales being entered. Leave blank to use the current date/time.

Close a Batch of Sales

                                          This screen is used to close batch of sales
You go to this screen from the Ticket Header screen by using [Close Batch] or [Alt] + [C]. This screen will
let you balance the cash in the cash drawer with the computer's total of the cash, and show a Sales Recap.
Password: if used enter the Manager's Password.
Cash Count (Deposit): this number is used to determine the over/short amount. (Optional)
[Cash Totals] or [Alt] + [T] will display a small report showing the Sales Recap, a Cash Drawer Recap, and
Void Summary you may also print this report which can be used to balance the drawer. (Optional)
[Close Batch] or [Alt] + [C] you will be prompted - Are sure you want to Close the Batch?
[Salesperson Summary] or [Alt] + [S] will print a Salesperson Summary report. (Optional)
[Open Drawer] or [Alt] + [O] will open the cash drawer.
[Count Money] or [Alt] + [M] will list cash and other Tender Types counted to balance the cash drawer.
(Optional)
The Starting Cash Drawer Amount field is a stored amount from the Ending Cash Drawer Amount of the
last closed batch. If there is a difference in the Starting and Ending Cash Drawer Amounts, then the Total
Cash is adjusted by the difference, affecting the Cash Count (Deposit). This is an optional feature that
allows you to make corresponding G/L Summary entries when there is a difference and the deposit is
affected.

Count Money

                                              Count out your cash at the end of day
When you close your batch you can use the Count Money screen to help you keep track of tender types for
your daily sales. On the screen shot below, notice the tender types are Cash, Check, MC/VISA, Discover, and
American Express.

                                                                                          26
Double click a tender type to count that tender. The following screen shot shows a tender type treated as
cash, this one happens to be Cash. You can enter change and bills. As you do, your total is affected and
shows the difference between the computer total based on tendered sales for this tender type and your count.

                                                                                          27
The following screen shot shows a tender type not treated as cash, this one happens to be Check. Enter the
value of each check you received for this batch. As you do, your total is affected and shows the difference
between the computer total based on tendered sales for this tender type and your count.

The Count Money screen also has an entry for Ending Cash Drawer Amount. Here you can count your
drawer and if there is a difference between the beginning cash drawer amount and the ending cash drawer
amount, the drawer difference adjusts the cash deposit on the Close Batch screen. The following screen shot
shows a Starting Cash Drawer Amount is a stored amount from the Ending Cash Drawer Amount of the
last closed batch. If there is a difference in the Starting and Ending Cash Drawer Amounts, then the Total
Cash is adjusted by the difference, affecting the Cash Count (Deposit).

Enter Sales

                                                      Entering Sales ­ Overview
Sales consists of three separate screens all which must be entered:
Ticket Header to enter Cashier, Transaction and Customer information
Ticket Detail to enter SKU/Column/Row, Quantity, Price and Discount information.

                                                                                          28
Ticket Tender to Tender out and end the sale.
Use the mouse or press the [Enter] or [Tab] keys to move the cursor from one field to the next within the
current section of the sales screen. To move backwards use the mouse, or the press [Shift] + [Tab] keys to
move backwards one field.
The section of the sales screen you are in is displayed on the "status line" at the top of the screen. Each of
the three sections of the sales screen will have different options that are displayed at the bottom of the
screen.
Transaction Types are:
1 - Regular Sale
2 - User Defined
3 - Special Order Pickup
4 - Layaway Sale
5 - Gift Certificate Sale
6 - Charge Payment
7 - Special Order Deposits
8 - Layaway Payment
Once a transaction type has been saved, you cannot change it, you must void the ticket and then enter a new
ticket to change it.
Other Options within Sales Tickets are:
Manager Options sets Options for Sales Tickets.
Ticket Review will allow you to change items already entered on a Sales Ticket.
Reclaim Ticket will allow you reclaim/undo a voided ticket.
Reprint Ticket will allow you to reprint a Sales Ticket.
Pay Outs are used to record cash taken from the cash drawer.

                                                                                          29
Sales Ticket Header

To Enter Transaction Types, Customer, and Salesperson information

Enter the Cashier and Transaction numbers if you don't know the numbers, Click on the Lookup icon ,
or hold down the [Ctrl] key and press the [P] key at the same time. See Look Up for more information.
(Cashier will default to the last number used. Transaction will always default to 1- Regular Sale.)
Customer account numbers can be optional or required based on how RICS is configured. Contact Technical
Support for more information.
Discount__% - You have the option to give an automatic discount on the entire sale if you have Discounts
setup in the Manager Options.
Promotion Code This is where the cashier can assign a promotion code to the sale. Promotion codes are
assigned in Promotion Code Setup. A promotion code may also be assigned in the ticket tender screen.
[Save/SKU Detail] or [Alt] + [S] will save the Ticket Header portion and take you the Ticket Detail portion of
the sales screen.
Other Options on this screen are:
Mail Detail
Manager Options
Payouts
Close Batch

                                                                                          30
Reclaim Ticket
Reprint Ticket
Mail List

Sales Ticket Detail

                       To enter SKU/Column/Row, Quantity, Price and Discount information

There is no limit to the number of items you can sell on a single ticket.
Note: UPC field will not be displayed unless UPC bar codes are used. Discount% and Perks may or may not
be displayed, depending on how you set up the Manager's Options.

Entering a SKU:
Scanning UPC bar codes: With the cursor at the UPC field simply scan the bar code. The SKU, Column
(Size), Row (Width), Qty (quantity will default to 1) and Price will be entered for you. The SKU description,
style/color and Price Extension will also be displayed. You may change any of the fields.

WITHOUT Scanning UPC bar codes: Press [Enter] past the UPC field (if field is displayed). Type in the
SKU, Column (Size), and Row (Width). The Qty (quantity will default to 1) and Price will be entered for you.

If you need to lookup the SKU #, click on the lookup icon  or hold down the [Ctrl] key and press the [P]
key at the same time.

31
Changing Quantities when scanning: When scanning an item the cursor defaults to the Price field. Use
your mouse to click on the quantity field or hold down the [Ctrl] key and press the [Tab] key at the same time
to move backwards to the field.

Discount% and or Amount may or may not be entered.

If the customer is purchasing another item:
Simply scan the next item or:
[Save/Next SKU], [Alt] + [S], or [F4] will save the displayed SKU, allowing another item to be sold. Each
time an item is saved, the SKU section clears and the cursor goes back up to UPC field, the saved item then
appears in the SKUs already entered on ticket portion of the screen.

When you are ready to collect the customer's money press:
[Save/Tender], [Alt] + [T], or [F5] will save the displayed SKU and, the Ticket Tender screen becomes
active.

Other Options from this screen are:
[Void], or [Alt] + [V] will void the current sales ticket. (You can setup passwords to be required before
allowing anyone to void a ticket.) For more information see Change Sales Passwords
[Clear], or [Alt] + [V] will the clear only the displayed SKU. Items already entered on ticket will not be cleared.
[Mail Detail], or [Alt] + [D] will display the purchase history information of the account number entered for the
current sales ticket. For more information see Mail Detail
[Change Header], or [Alt] + [H] will take you back to the ticket header. For more information see Ticket
Header
[Next Price], or [Alt] + [N] will enter the next price that has been setup for the displayed SKU. If no other
prices are setup for the SKU the price will not change
[Review], or [Alt] + [R] will take you to the Ticket Review screen to look at, modify, or delete items that have
already been entered for this sales ticket.
[Reverse Qtys], or [Alt] + [Q] will reverse the quantity of the SKU you have entered. This is an easy way to
change a sale into a return.

Comment A comment may be added to each SKU for readability on the sales receipt. This is ideal for
special order deposits to describe the merchandise.

Return Code, if displayed, is a code to determine why an item is being returned. The code may be entered or
the lookup option may be used.

Discount %, if displayed, is the % discount entered without the decimal point. For example, a discount of
10% should be entered as 10, not .10. Amount is the dollar and /or cents amount of the discount.

Tax will appear as setup in the Store File. You may un-check the box to make individual items non-taxable. If
your tax rate is already zero, it does not matter if the sales tax boxes are checked or not.

Salesperson will default to the cashier number, but can be changed to any other salespersons number to do
split sales on the same sales ticket. You can have multiply salespeople on the same sales ticket but only one
per line item.

Family Member will allow you to keep mail list detail for more than one person on the same mail list account
number. Entering a Family Member will enter the detail in that members file. You can have multiply Family
Members on the same sales ticket but only one per line item.

                                                                                          32
Sales Ticket Tender

                                         To Enter Tender Types and End Sales Ticket

Tender is used to record how a customer is paying for the merchandise. It will default to the total sale
amount. If a default tender type was selected in Manager Options, then that tender will also be entered.
If you want to continue the payment to another ticket, you can use a tender of '99'. This will force the next
ticket to be for the same customer. The tickets are then joined as a 'continued' ticket. If any part of a
continued ticket is voided, the entire transaction will be voided. This allows the cashier to ring up a gift
certificate sale and a regular sale and only collect payment once from the customer.
Four different Tenders are available for recording a split tender. (i.e. both cash and check are used.)
Tender Total cannot be less than the sale. All Sale Must Be Fully Tendered.
Change will be displayed if the amount of the tender is greater than the total due.
Tax can be changed or overwritten here.
Other Charges is used to record charges for services such as freight or delivery. The Total due will change
accordingly.
Ticket Comment is not required. It could be used to record information on why a item was returned, a check
number, or a credit card expiration date. Any information entered here will print on the customer's receipt,
added to the customer's Mail Detail, and print on the sales journal.

                                                                                          33
Other Options from this screen are:
[Mail Detail], or [Alt] + [D] will display the purchase history information of the account number entered for the
current sales ticket. For more information see Mail Detail

[End Sale], or [Alt] + [E] will save the rest of the ticket. The receipt will print and cash drawer will open. You
will then be back at the Ticket Header, ready to enter a new ticket.

[Void], or [Alt] + [V] will void the current sales ticket. (You can setup passwords to be required before
allowing anyone to void a ticket.)

[Add More SKUs], or [Alt] + [A] will take you back to the ticket detail to add more SKUs or you can change
other information. For more information see Ticket Detail

[Clear], or [Alt] + [C] will the clear the tender amount entered and will default back to the total sale amount.

Note: If a sales ticket has been ended with the wrong tender entered, and you want to correct this to balance
for your deposits, you can enter a new sales ticket with nothing sold (the amount due is -0-), in ticket tender
enter the incorrect tender type and that amount as a negative, then enter the correct tender type and that
amount as a positive (the total tendered for the ticket is still -0-, but the tender's totals for the day will then
change when the ticket is saved).

Ticket ­ Review, Reclaim, Reprint, Refunds

                                         Allows you to change items already entered
From the Ticket Detail screen [Review], or [Alt] + [R] will take you to this option. The screen will display any
item already entered for this sales ticket. You cannot review previous sales tickets that have already been
ended.

[Remove Item], or [Alt] + [R] will remove or delete the highlighted item from the Sales Ticket.

[Modify SKU], or [Alt] + [M] will enter the highlighted item back in the Ticket Detail so you can make any
necessary changes to the item and then save the changes.

Ticket - Reclaim

                              Allows you reclaim/redo a voided ticket in the Current Batch
From the Ticket Header screen [Reclaim Ticket], or [Alt] + [R] will take you to this option. The screen will
display only voided sales ticket in the current batch of sales that can be reclaimed. You cannot reclaim sales
tickets from a previous batch of sales, from tickets that were voided after completion, or from voided
continued ticket sequences.

[Select], or [Alt] + [S] will enter the highlighted Ticket back to the Ticket Header so you can make any
necessary changes to the Ticket and then save the changes.

Ticket - Reprint

                                  Allows you Reprint a Sales Ticket in the Current Batch
From the Ticket Header screen [Reclaim Ticket], or [Alt] + [E] will take you to this option. The screen will
display any sales ticket in the current batch of sales. You cannot reprint sales tickets from a previous batch of
sales.

[Select], or [Alt] + [S] will reprint the highlighted Sales Ticket.

Ticket - Refunds

                  To Enter Customer Refunds/Returns

                  34
When a customer returns merchandise, enter all information just as you would a regular sale only change the
quantity to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT change the price to a negative number. (You can setup
Sales Passwords to be required before allowing anyone to enter a Return).

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 1 Regular Sale and a Customer Account number if
entered on original sale.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, and row, only change the quantity
to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT change the price to a negative number.

To tender a return the amount will show up as a negative amount. Enter the tender type of the refund and
the amount of the refund as a negative amount. If you are giving the customer a Store Credit enter tender #11
Store Credit.

You Can Require Account Numbers for All Refunds

Ticket - Credit Slips, Void, Pay Outs

                                Credit, Due Bill, Store Credit, Customer Credit, Credit Slip
No matter what you call them, they fit under tender type # 11 Store Credit. When using store credits Always
Enter an Account Number, this will track the balance of Store Credits for the customer.

Enter Ticket Header Section and Ticket Detail Section as you always would.

In the Ticket Tender Section, enter the Tender Type #11 Store Credit and the amount of the Store Credit
being redeemed.

[Mail Detail], or [Alt] + [D] will display the Store Credit Balance and purchase history information of the
account number entered for the current sales ticket. For more information see Mail Detail

If the customer makes a purchase with a store credit and the credit is for more than the purchase, enter the
tender (# 11 Store Credit) for just for the amount of the sale, and RICS will keep track of the balance of the
store credit under their account.

You Can Require Account Numbers for All Store Credits

Ticket - Void

                                     Voiding a Sales Ticket before it's been completed
[Void], or [Alt] + [V] will void the current ticket. You will be asked if you are sure you want to void the ticket.
If a void password was set up in the Change Sales Passwords, you will be asked for the password. If a ticket
is voided it can be Reclaimed later, (if it is in the current batch of sales), this would the same as putting the
ticket on hold until your ready to complete it.

Pay Outs

                                    Are used to record cash taken from the cash drawer
You might enter a pay out, for example, if you take $2.50 out of the drawer to pay the postman for a postage-
due letter.

Enter the Cashier.

If the RICS.CFG entry ValidatePayouts in the Sales Screen section is N, then a line is available to enter a
Description of the Payout transaction. If the ValidatePayouts entry is not in the RICS.CFG, or is entered as a
Y, then you are required to select from the list of payout transaction descriptions.

Enter the Amount.

[Save] or [Alt] + [S] will save the information.

[Open Drawer] or [Alt] + [D] can be used to take money out of the drawer.

[Exit] or [Alt] + [X] will take you back to the sales screen without saving any information.

The cash totals (sales recap) can be printed when you close a batch of sales, this will print the total of all Paid
