Special Order ­ Overview, Deposit

Overview

Special Orders consist of two separate types of transactions, the Special Order Deposit #7 and the Special
Order Pickup #3 both parts must be done to track special orders properly.

A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.

Special Order Deposit is done if the customer is going to put a deposit down or pay for an item you do not
have in stock. This is only a deposit. The item is not taken out of inventory, nor does it become a sale until
a special order pickup is done.

Special Order Pickup is done when the item is picked up. This is when the item is taken out of inventory and
is counted as a sale in the system

Print Special Orders will print Special Orders Transactions from a selected range of store(s) and date(s)

Special Order Reports from Print Mail List will print a report on Special Orders allowing criteria selections.

You Can Require Account Numbers for All Special Orders

Special Order - Deposit

Special Order Deposit is done if the customer is going to put a deposit down or pay for an item you do not
have in stock. This is only a deposit. The item is not taken out of inventory, nor does it become a sale until
a Special Order Pickup is done. A salesperson does not get credit for the sale until a Special Order Pickup is
done. (A special order deposit does not necessarily need to be done if the customer is paying in full and the
SKU is VALID you may just want to make a Ticket Comment to mail out when in, or PAID will pickup when in.)

A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 7 Special Order Deposit and a Customer Account
number.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, and row.
If the SKU entered is a valid SKU previously entered in RICS, then the description and price will display on
the screen.
If the SKU entered is NOT A VALID SKU currently in the system, RICS will allow you to enter an invalid
SKU number, Column/Row (Size/Width) and Price. The system will not display a description. A description,

                                                                                          36
color or other information about the SKU may be entered in the Ticket Comments. Whatever SKU is entered

will NOT be recorded as a sale. It is just used to print a sales ticket showing the item(s) being ordered, the

total of the ticket, the amount paid, and the balance that will be due when the special order is picked up. The

sale  is  recorded  when  you                           enter  S.O.  Pickup.

In the Ticket Tender Section enter the Tender Type and the amount of the deposit another line will show the
Balance Due, this will also print on the customer's receipt.

You Can Require Account Numbers for All Special Orders

Special Order ­ Pickup, Refund, Print

Special Order - Pickup

A Special Order Pickup is done when the customer is going to pick up an item they had already paid a
Special Order Deposit on. You MUST ENTER CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBERS to track special orders.
You Can Require Account Numbers for All Special Orders

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 3 Special Order Pickup and a Customer Account
number.
In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, and row.
The SKU Must be a valid SKU previously entered in RICS, then the description and price will display on the
screen.
In the Ticket Tender Section a line will show the amount Previous Paid, this amount will be taken off from
the total due, enter the Tender Type and the amount to fully tender the sale.

Special Order - Refund

If a customer is returning a special order that has already been picked up you can do a regular Refund on the
item.

When a customer needs a refund on a Special Order Deposit, enter all information just as you would on the
Special Order Deposit, only change the quantity to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT change the price to
a negative number. A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.

You Can Require Account Numbers for All Special Orders

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 7 Special Order Deposit and a Customer Account
number.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, and row, only change the quantity
to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT change the price to a negative number.

In the Ticket Tender Section enter the Tender Type and the amount of the deposit (Previous Paid) as a
negative amount, another line will show the Balance Due. This should also be a negative number. These
numbers should be the same as the original numbers only negative.

Print Special Orders

                                          For a selected range of store(s) and date(s)
Stores is used to enter the store(s) that you wish to have Special Orders printed for. If you only have one
store, or you want all stores printed, leave stores blank. Each store will print separately.

Print from ___ to___ is used to enter the date range that the Special Orders should be printed for.

                                                                                          37
Select from posted sales, when checked any Special Orders that occurred in the specified date range that
have been posted will print. For more information, see Post Sales to Inventory.

Select from unposted sales when checked you can use a date range. It is recommended to leave the
beginning date and ending date blank. This will ensure that all unposted Special Orders are printed. Only
Special Orders from sales that have NOT yet been posted will print. If sales have been posted, or your date
range is incorrect, nothing may print.

Check both Select from posted sales and Select from unposted sales to choose ALL Transactions.

You may also use Mail List, Print Mail List to print out all Special Orders regardless of date.

Layaway - Overview, Payment, Pickup

Overview

A layaway is done when the customer puts a down payment on merchandise that the customer wants you to
"hold". The customer would then make payments on the merchandise to pay off the balance owed. Layaway
sales are taken out of inventory and credited for the complete sale when the item is first put on layaway.
Layaways consist of two separate types of transactions, the Layaway Sale #4 and the Layaway Payment #8
both parts must be done to track Layaways properly. A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to
track special orders. You Can Require Account Numbers for All Layaways

Layaway Sale is done when the customer first is going to put a deposit down on an item. This is their
deposit. The item is then taken out of inventory, and it becomes a sale.

Layaway Payment is done when the customer is going to make a payment or the item is picked up.
Print Layaways will print Layaway Transactions from a selected range of store(s) and date(s)

Layaway Reports from Print Mail List will print a report on Layaways allowing criteria selections.

Layaway - Payment

Layaway Sale or Deposit is done when the customer first puts a deposit down for an item. This is their
deposit. The item is then taken out of inventory, and becomes a sale. A salesperson then gets credit for the
sale. A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.
You Can Require Account Numbers for All Layaways

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 4 Layaway Sale and a Customer Account number.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, and row.
The SKU entered must be a valid SKU previously entered in RICS, then the description and price will
display on the screen.

In the Ticket Tender Section enter the Tender Type and the amount of the deposit another line will show the
Balance Due, this will also print on the customer's receipt.

Layaway - Pickup

Layaway Payment is done when the customer is going to pay on or pick up an item they had already put in
Layaway. A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.
You Can Require Account Numbers for All Layaways

                                                                                          38
In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 8 Layaway Payment and a Customer Account number.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter Payment on Ticket # - this would be the original Ticket # when the item
was put in Layaway it will then show you the Originally Due, Less Paid and the Balance. Enter the Amount
of the payment, it will then show you the New Balance.

If you don't know the Original Layaway Ticket # [Mail Detail], or [Alt] + [D] will display the purchase history
information of the account number entered. For more information see Mail Detail

In the Ticket Tender Section will show the amount to be paid this amount will be taken off the balance. If
you need to change the amount of the payment entered, press [Change Amount] or [Alt] + [A].

Layaway ­ Refund, Print

If a customer is returning a Layaway that has already been picked up (Paid for) you would do a regular
Refund. A CUSTOMER ACCOUNT NUMBER IS REQUIRED to track special orders.
You Can Require Account Numbers for All Layaways

When a customer needs a refund on a Layaway Deposit, enter all information just as you would on the
Layaway Sale, except change the quantity to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT change the price to a
negative number.

In the Ticket Header Section enter Transaction - 4 Layaway Sale and a Customer Account number.

In the Ticket Detail Section enter SKU - Enter the SKU number, column, row, and price just as it was
entered on the original Layaway Ticket, except change the quantity to a negative number (i.e. -1). DO NOT
change the price to a negative number.

In the Ticket Tender Section enter the Apply Layaway Balance to Ticket # this is the original Layaway
ticket this will then show the amount Originally Due, Less Paid and Balance, another line will show the New
Balance, this should be a negative number. Enter the tender type and amount, press enter and the New
Balance, will recalculate this should now be -0-.

If you are charging the customer a layaway fee you can [Tab] back to Other Charges and enter in the
amount.

If you don't know the Original Layaway Ticket # [Mail Detail], or [Alt] + [D] will display the purchase history
information of the account number entered. For more information see Mail Detail

Print Sales Journal

                                                Prints the Daily Sales Transactions
This journal will show a detailed listing of selected daily sales transactions. This report will print separate
journals for each day, store, and register.

You must Print a Sales Journal and also Post Sales to Inventory for your inventory to be accurate,
regardless if the sales were entered on the main or POS. A sales journal must be printed before you post
sales. DO NOT post sales for a selected store and/or date unless all the sales are printed successfully and
everything is correct. Review and keep your sales journals. You can print a sales journal as often as
necessary before you post sales. The sales will post only once. But once you post sales you can no longer
get a sales journal for those sales.

Stores is used to enter the store(s) that you wish to have Sales Journal printed for. If you only have one
store, or you want all stores printed, leave stores blank. Each store will print separately.
Print from ___ to___ is used to enter the date range that the Sales Journal should be printed for. It is
recommended that the 'Print from' and 'Print to' date ranges be left blank to ensure that all unposted
items will print on the sales journal.

Printing and Posting Using the Date Range: When you print and post your sales you will have the ability to
enter a date range. This date range is used as a "filter" to decide if your sales should be printed and posted.

Print Sales Ticket Time: The time of each sales ticket can be printed on the Sales Journal. This can make it
easier to research specific sales transactions. To print the time for each sale, perform the following:

     1. At the RICS Main Menu select Utilities 2
     2. Under Section select SALES SCREEN, and for Item(s) for selected Section select JOURNALTIME
     3. Change the Entry for selected Section and Item to 'Y'.

Printing: For example, assume you have sales for three different days on your computer. The days are:
11/15/98, 11/16/98, and 11/17/98. The date range on your sales journal screen is 11/01/98 through 11/15/98.
Any sales that have occurred in the specified date range that have not yet been posted will print. The only
sales that will print are those that occurred from 11/1/98 thru 11/15/98.

Posting: Using the above example, when you post sales to inventory, the date range on your screen is
11/01/98 through 11/30/98. The only sales that will post are the sales that occurred 11/15/98. Why? Because
only the sales that have been printed on a sales journal can be posted. What happens to the other two days,
Nothing, and they are not lost. Just print a sales journal for those sales, by changing the date range, and then
you can post them. To prevent a problem similar to this example, leave the date range blank.

When a Sales Journal is printing, it is possible for errors to occur. Below, is an example of an error message
that can occur.
{bmc JournalError.bmp}

In the example above, SKU 2617 has either been deleted or discontinued. If that SKU really should exist, it
would need to be added into inventory using File Setup - SKUs. Otherwise, you would need to void the ticket
using Sales - Void a Ticket. If you void the ticket, all items on that ticket are NOT deducted from inventory or
credited as sales. You would need to start a batch of sales on the MAIN COMPUTER and re-enter the ticket
correctly.

                                                                                          44
Post Sales to Inventory

                                 Posting Sales will deduct the items sold from inventory
This option will post your sales tickets. Posting sales will deduct the items sold from inventory and the sales
dollars and quantities will increase. It is a good idea to post sales every day.

If you try to post sales before you Print a Sales Journal, those SALES WILL NOT POST. Instead, you will get
a message stating all of your sales are not posted.

Stores is used to enter the store(s) that you wish to have Sales Posted for. If you only have one store, or you
want all stores printed, leave stores blank. Each store will print separately. This screen will also show you The
current month and year that the system is set for.

Post from day___ of the current month to day___ of the current month is used to enter the date range
that the Sales should be posted for. It is recommended that be left blank to ensure that all unposted
items will be posted for the current month.

Print negative on-hand report when checked on it will print a negative on-hand report which can help make
you aware of items and/or sizes that were sold that you did not have entered in the computer. Knowing this
information may help you correct your inventory on a more timely basis.

Printing A/R Detail - If not doing Accounts Receivable, leave this unchecked.

IMPORTANT: At the start of a new month, sales can not be posted for that month until the previous month is
closed out. For example, sales can not be posted for March until February is closed out. For more
information, see Close/Clear - Close Month/Season/Year.

NOTE: If the following notice is displayed when you are done posting sales, DO NOT ignore it. It means all
of your sales are not posted.

Reasons sales might not have posted:
1. The sales you tried posting have not been printed on a sales journal.
2. The sales occurred for a different store than the store selected. Check the store number on the sales

        journal. Post the sales again, this time leave stores blank, or select the proper store.
3. The sales occurred for a date that is not included in the selected date range. Make sure the date range

        includes the date of your sales. If you still cannot determine why you have sales that are not posted, do
        the following:

1. Print a Sales Journal but click the      or press the [Alt] + [L] keys at the same

time before running. This will clear the current entry that was displayed.

2. Repost the sales but click the           or press the [Alt] + [L] keys at the same time

before running. This will clear the current entry that was displayed. .

There may be times that you do not want all sales posted. Some reasons may be that you have sales that
occurred in two different months the sales for the next month can not and should not be posted until you

                                        45
closed out the previous month. Your months are on a weekly not monthly basis. Another reason is that you
have sales on the computer for multiple stores and/or days. You notice a problem for one of the stores and/or
one of the days. So, you select a store number and/or date range that does not include the sales in question.
If you have sales for a month before the current month as indicated in the Company Setup, you will receive
the following message. It is recommended you click Yes which post the sales into your current month.
Contact Technical Support for additional options.

If you have sales after the current month, you will receive the following message warning you that there are
sales that are for a month after. An example of this message is entering sales on the first day of the month
without closing the previous month's sales. Close the month and re-post the sales.

If you still can not determine why you have sales that are not posted, or how to get rid of them, please call
Technical Support .

Print Sales Tax Recap

                         Summarize your sales and taxes collected by the customer's state

This report will show your sales and taxes summarized by the mail file state of the customer. This report is
ideal for mail order or catalog departments, where sales tax payments may have be made to multiple states.
Stores is used to enter the store(s) that you wish to have the recap consider. If you only have one store, or
you want all stores printed, leave stores blank. Each store will print separately.
Date Range from ___ to___ is used to enter the date range whose sales the Recap will use.
Select from posted sales, when checked any sales that occurred in the specified date range that have been
posted will print. For more information, see Post Sales to Inventory.
Select from unposted sales, when checked any sales that occurred in the specified date range that have
been unposted will print. For more information, see Post Sales to Inventory.
Check both Select from posted sales and Select from unposted sales to choose ALL Transactions.
Print Store/State Report, Print State/Store Report options will print the report in the selected order, You
may print both reports at one time.
Select from unposted sales, when checked any sales that occurred in the specified date range that have
been unposted will print. For more information, see Post Sales to Inventory.
Another choice is where to get the sales and tax figures from, either the ticket totals or ticket detail lines.
If the ticket detail lines are selected then the sales tax calculated is the line item tax amount calculated for that
line of the ticket. The collected tax is the amount that was collected for each sale. This could be different from
the calculated tax if there are multiple line items. Each line individually could have a remainder of a cent. The
collected tax is the line item tax for each line added together and then rounded. The difference is the amount
collected at the sale and the total of the line item tax.
An example is 2 separate line items at $10.95 each. A tax of 8% makes each line item tax $ 0.876. The sales
tax for the ticket shows $ 1.75. The individual line items are $ 0.88 each. In this example the calculated tax is
$ 1.76 and the collected tax is $ 1.75.

Void a Ticket - After the Sale

                                      Voiding a Completed, but Unposted Sales Ticket
This option is used to void a ticket that has not been posted. It may be necessary to void a ticket because of
a problem on a sales journal, or because the ticket was entered incorrectly. Once a ticket is voided it will still
print on the sales journal, but it will not post. It still prints on the sales journal as a record of the transaction,
and a void summary will show the number of voids, amount of voids, and % of net sales voided.
To Void a Ticket:
Listed will be all unposted sales sorted by Store#, Date, and Ticket #, this will also show the transaction
type and account # for each ticket. Select (highlight) the ticket you want voided and click [Void] or press the

                                                                                          51
[Alt] + [V] keys at the same time.

Change Sales Passwords

                                To Create a New or Change an Existing Sales Passwords
This screen is used to set up and change passwords that are used on the sales screen. These passwords
can be set up any time and will take affect immediately after being saved.
Manager Password is used to prevent people from Closing a Batch of Sales, changing Manager's Options,
and issuing a Payout unless they know that password. If a password is not set up, you would not be
prompted for a password on those screens.
Ticket Password is used to prevent people from Voiding a Ticket unless they know that password. If a
password is not set up, you would not be prompted for a password when a ticket is voided. The ticket
password can also be used to prevent: a return, a change in price, a perk from being entered, or a discount
percentage or amount. For more information about setting these options call Technical Support.
Setting New Passwords If a password has not been created enter pass the current password, then Enter
New Password, then Enter New Password Again and click [Save] or press the [Alt] + [S] keys at the same
time.
Changing Passwords - If a password has been set up before, Enter Current Password, then Enter New
Password, then Enter New Password Again and click [Save] or press the [Alt] + [S] keys at the same time.
You can change any of these passwords at anytime. It does not matter if you have already started a new
batch of sales.

Inventory Inquiry

                Look at SKU's On-hand, On-order, Sales, quantities and other SKU information
Enter a SKU number and press [Enter] (You may use or [Ctrl] + [P] to display a list of existing SKUs.).
Enter a Store number and press [Enter] (You may use or [Ctrl] + [P] to display a list of existing Stores.)
Row is used only for certain Display options for a selected row of an SKU that has multiple rows.
This will display the SKU Description, and information on the Category, Vendor, Vendor SKU, Style/Color,
Size Type, and Last received date for this SKU. Displayed in the upper right corner of the screen will be the
Retail Price, Markdown 1, and Markdown 2, along with the Average Cost, Current Cost and List Price for
this SKU. Sales totals for Qty, Net, Markdown, Profit, for the period Week, Month, Season, and Year are
displayed below that.
The lower half of the screen will display the size grids based on the Display Options selected.
Options- This option will allow you to change the displayed quantities. Click Options or press [Alt] +
[O] to display the list of Options A menu similar to the following will be displayed:

Hint: To quickly change the display, press the appropriate function key [F1] through [F12], or shift and the
appropriate function key. [Shift]+[F1] or [Shift]+[F2]
[F2] On Hand is the quantity and sizes on hand in the system.
[F3] On Order (Current) is the quantity and sizes on At Once Orders.
[F4] On Order (Future) is the quantity and sizes on Future Orders.
[F5] Model Quantities is the model quantity and sizes entered in the system

                                                                                          53
[F6] Short Quantities is the model quantity less the on hand quantity. If short is a positive number, on-hand
inventory is greater than the model. If short is a negative number, on-hand inventory is less that the model.
[F7] Month-to-Date Sales is the quantity and sizes sold Month to Date.
[F8] Season-to-Date Sales is the quantity and sizes sold Season to Date.
[F9] Year-to-Date Sales is the quantity and sizes sold Year to Date.
[F11] Column only displays the quantity on hand, on order, model, short and MTD, STD and YTD sales for
an SKU that does not have rows or for a selected row on an SKU that has multiple rows.
[F12] All stores on hand display the quantity on hand of all stores for an SKU that doesn't have any rows, or
for a selected row of an SKU that has multiple rows.

[Shift] + [F1] All stores-1 row displays the quantity on hand, on order, and MTD, STD and YTD sales of all
stores for an SKU that doesn't have any rows, or for a selected row of an SKU that has multiple rows.
[Shift] + [F2] All stores-summary displays the total quantity on hand, on order, and MTD, STD and YTD
sales of all stores for an SKU, with no column or row information.
[Shift] + [F3] Max Quantities is the max quantity and sizes entered in the system.

[Shift] + [F4] Reorder Quantities is the reorder quantity and sizes entered in the system.

Process in Store Order - When this option is selected (a checkmark appears to the left of the option) and
you click the [Prev] or [Next] buttons, the items are shown in Store, SKU order showing you all SKU's for 1
store, then when the store changes it starts with the first SKU. When this is not selected and you click the
[Prev] or [Next] buttons, each store is display before getting to the next SKU.

Print Directly to Printer (if possible) - When this option is selected (a checkmark appears to the left of the
option) and you click the [Print] button, the screen is printed directly to the printer, if possible. Otherwise it is
printed to a screen spool file.

[Prev] or [Alt] + [P] - This option will display the previous SKU#.
[Next] or [Alt] + [N] - This option will display the next SKU#.
[UPCs] or [Alt] + [U] - This option will display the UPC codes for this SKU.
[POs] or [Alt] + [S] - This will display outstanding PO's of the selected SKU. A display box similar to the
following will be displayed:

[Trend] or [Alt] + [T] - This option will display the eight week trending information for the selected SKU. For
more information, see Eight Week Trending.
[Info] or [Alt] + [I] - This option will display additional information for the selected SKU/Store.

     Additional information displays the Season, Label Code, Group Code, Date 1st Received, Date Last
Markdown, Perks, and Comments. Also displayed is the Last 12 Months Sales for Qty and Sales $ listed
by Month and also Total. Included on this screen is G.P.%, ROI, and TURNS for the SKU/Store by M-T-D,
S-T-D, and Y-T-D.
[Detail] or [Alt] + [D] - This option will display detailed Inventory Change Detail to see when you have

received, returned, transferred, or physically adjusted the inventory of the selected SKU.
[Print] or [Alt] + [R] - This option will print the current screen.

Inventory Change Detail

From the Inventory Inquiry screen, click the [Detail] button to view transaction for this SKU including, Manual
Receipts, Returns, Purchase Order and Purchase Order Receipts, Transfers In, Transfers Out, and Physical
Inventory Adjustments.
The information displayed is Store Number, Transaction Date, Transaction Type, Quantity, Cost, and any
comments. The comments are Bill To/Ship From store information and Purchase Order numbers, and RMA
numbers for returns.
The information is displayed in store order with most recent activity shown first.
You can [Print] the page by clicking the button.
Check the Detail check box to view size detail. Remove the check to show summary activity.
Check the Show All Stores check box to view all store activity for this SKU. If you selected an All Stores
option from the Inventory Inquiry screen this option is not available and all store activity for this SKU is shown
summarized.
If you want more detailed information, run the Inventory Detail Report.

Enter Purchase Orders

                            Create a New, or Look at /Change an existing Purchase Orders
PO Number - Enter a new number, or accept the default, which is one number higher than the last PO
number. You can use any combination of letters and numbers in a PO number. However, a PO cannot start

with the letters 'A' or 'V'; they are reserved for Automatic and Direct Sale Purchase Orders respectively.
or [Ctrl] + [P] will display a list of existing PO numbers. If you use letters in your PO number, the system may
not be able to automatically increment to the next PO number.

Enter the Bill-to Store and Ship-to Store number(s). Enter the Vendor number. If you are not using EDI, the
cursor will skip Order Type, which will default to RO - Regular Order. If using EDI you will have the options
RE for At Once Order, and SA for Future Order and an Option box for Export will appear. Click "on" or "off"
the option for Storing Labels, or press [Alt] + [L].

                                               You then have two folder options Header Info and SKU Info. Start with
the Header Info. You may then enter a Confirmation #. The Account #, Terms, and Ship-Via- fields
defaults to information setup in the Vendor file. Any of this information can be changed. Backorder & Split
shipment- can be Click "on or "off", If you leave either field blank, that information will not print on the PO.

Order, Ship, Cancel, and Pymt dates should be entered. Ship dates are used to determine if the order is an
At Once or Future Order. It is also used in the Open-to-Buy, Purchase Order Reports, and Open POs by
Month Report. Payment date is used to calculate, and print a cash payments projection at the end of the
Purchase Order Report. The current date on the computer is the default order date. Program Code is used
only when entering some EDI purchase orders. Comments or special instructions can also be entered on the
purchase order.

SKU Info - A purchase order can have as many SKUs as necessary. An SKU must be set up before you can
enter it on a purchase order, if an SKU is not yet set up simply click [Add] in the SKU Lookup After an SKU
number is entered, the description and style/color are displayed from the inventory screen. The Retail Price
and Current Cost are also displayed; and you can change these values (Changing the values here will also
change them in the master file unless you choose to change a RICS.CFG entry).

Casepacks: If you enter a casepack number, the sizes set up for that casepack will automatically be
displayed. X__ can be used to order more than 1 casepack for that SKU. A casepack must be set up before
you can enter it on a purchase order, if a casepack is not yet set up simply click [Add] in the Casepack
Lookup . The casepack number will print on the Purchase Order.

Enter the quantities that you want to order. After entering quantities for a SKU click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S]
to save. The SKU will clear and the cursor will go back to SKU. You can then enter another SKU and its
quantities. You would click [Save] after each SKU and its quantities are entered.

Click [Save & Print PO] or press [Alt] + [a] after the last SKU is entered for that PO. The purchase order will
print and the screen will clear, which will allow you to enter another Purchase Order.

When looking at an existing PO, click or press [Ctrl] + [O] to view all the SKUs on this PO. Click [Next
SKU] or press [Alt] + [N] to see the next SKU on that PO.

Display the SKU or PO you wish to delete. Click [Delete] or press [Alt] + [D] to delete, the screen will then
ask if you want to delete the entire PO, [P] or the current SKU, [S].

Modifying quantities on order
Display the SKU you wish to change and enter the new quantity you wish to order. Do not enter the
plus/minus difference. For example, you have 5 on order, and you need to have 6 on order. Enter a 6. That
will become you new on-order quantity then [Save].

Discount % would be for a volume discount and would lower the entered cost per item.

Under Receiving an SKU If you do not receive an SKU in full, the following message will be displayed:

[Yes] will cancel the on-order balance, [No] will leave the balance as a backorder.

                                                                                          57
SKU NOT on a PO An SKU not entered on the PO can be received. However, the SKU will not be added to
the PO unless an in-transit Purchase Order is being received. These SKUs should be received under the
correct PO# or receive them using Stock Maintenance - Enter Manual Receipts.

                                                                       Over Receipt of an SKU in Error - Re-enter the SKU
                                                                       that was over-received and enter a minus quantity to
                                                                       offset the mistake. For example: four of a size were
                                                                       received when three of that size should have been
                                                                       received. Enter a quantity of a minus one. That entry
                                                                       will take the item out of inventory and put it back on the
                                                                       Purchase Order. However, four labels will print instead
                                                                       of three.

                                                                       Other Purchase Order Information - After a purchase
                                                                       order is received in full, it is not immediately deleted
                                                                       from the system. Purchase Orders received in full will
stay in RICS until you close out the month. If a PO is NOT ever received in full, it will stay in RICS until it is
received in full, or deleted. It is your responsibility to delete any purchase orders that are no longer valid. The
Purchase Order Reports could be used to locate those past due purchase orders by printing a ship date
range with a blank beginning date, and the ending date being the last day of last month.

After a purchase order has been received, either in full or partial, if you display that purchase order in Enter
Purchase Orders it will display the original quantities ordered. The purchase order WILL NOT display just
what is left on order. To view just what is left on order you have two choices. 1. Run a Purchase Order
Reports PO format (open quantities) 2. View the purchase order on this screen.

Purchase Orders Reports

                                          Reports on existing Open Purchase Orders
You can use the Report Options to:

Sort by: The options are to sort by Store, PO#, by Store, Vendor, or by Store, Ship Date. The report will
also show category totals and cash payments projection.

Po's to Print: The options are to print All PO's, At Once PO's, Vendor, or Future PO's.

Report to Print: The options are to print:

    Complete PO (Report format) will print POs showing the original amount ordered, the amount received,
        and the open balance.

    PO Totals will print PO Totals showing the original amount ordered, the amount received, and the open

                                                                                          58
        balance.
    Store Totals will print the Total of POs by Store, showing the original amount ordered, the amount

        received, and the open balance, by category.
    PO format (order quantities) will print your original POs with the original on-order quantities. You'll also

        have the option to Print Cost on and/or Print Retail Price on PO's.
    PO format (open quantities) will print your original POs with the remaining on-order quantities (to use

        when checking back orders). You'll also have the option to Print Cost on and/or Print Retail Price on
        PO's.

You can use the Criteria to select normal criteria selection but you may also:

      Print a list of all past due open orders, or a list of all orders due to arrive next month, by selecting Ship
      date from ___ to ___, Order date from___ to ___, Cancel date from ___ to ___, Date Last Received
      from___ to ___.

Open P.O. by Month Report

                                       Reports on existing Purchase Orders by Month
This report can be used to view, spread out by the next 12 months, what and when orders are due to be
received.

You can use the Report Options to:

Sort by: The report can be summarized by Vendor, or by Category.

Data to Print: The options are to print the Open Quantity on order, the dollar amount on order Open at Cost
or the dollar amount on order Open at Retail.

Date by: This report will print a summary of the open purchase orders by Ship Date, Cancel Date, Payment
Date, or spread out between Ship/Cancel Date Spread.

Detail to Print: The options are to print the SKU Detail or Category/Vendor subtotals.

PO's to Print: The three options are to print All PO's, At Once PO's, or Future PO's.

Use Vendor from: The normal default is the SKU File. The Purchase Order File is used if you are buying
from someone other than the original vendor. Example: You are buying Nike from both Nike and also a
Jobber, you could then have orders for the same SKU from two different vendors. This option would allow you
to separate who the vendor is that the orders are placed with, where as if you if you ran it by SKU File all the
orders would show up as Nike

Combine Stores: Leave unchecked to separate store totals.

Export as comma delimited file checkbox allows you to export the sales analysis report to a comma-
      delimited file specified in the Export Filename text box. The Export Filename must have a file extension
      of ".TXT" or ".CSV".

Generate Automatic Purchase Orders

This option will create purchase orders for stores based upon model, on-hand, and on order quantities. For
each store, if the on hand quantity plus the order quantity for an SKU is less than the model quantity, the
amount short is added to an Automatic Purchase Order.

Before running Automatic Purchase Orders you need to Enter Model Quantities. The model quantity for each
store-SKU-column-row combination is the quantity of that item you would like to have on hand. Before running
this option you should have entered, printed, and posted all sales transactions so that the on hand quantity for

                                                                                          59
your stores is current. All Automatic Purchase Orders start with the letter A, and are considered AT-ONCE
orders.
If you have entered maximum quantities in your model quantities, the order quantities generated will bring you
to that maximum quantity. Otherwise, the order quantities will bring you to your model quantity. If you have
entered reorder amounts in your model quantities, the order quantities generated will be the multiple of that
reorder quantity that will bring you up to or over the applicable minimum or maximum quantity.
P.O. Options

Choose whether you want to make purchase orders for selected Stores or Vendors. For more information
      about selecting see Criteria or Wild Cards.

Bill-to-Store is a required field. This is the store that will be listed on the PO as the bill-to store.
Combine to Store ­ acts as a warehouse or central distributing store for companies with multiple stores. If
the Combine to Store is used, the total need is gathered from all selected stores based on the highest model
of the selected stores. The on hand amount from the Combine to Store is then subtracted from total quantity
short from all of the stores used to get the quantity ordered. This creates a single purchase order for the
Combine to Store.
Backorder & Split shipment - can be on or off.
Ship, Cancel, and Payment dates should also be entered.
Automatically Generate Labels should be checked if you want labels printed.
Hint: You can use Enter Purchase Orders option to manually adjust the automatically created PO.
Criteria

                                                                                          60
Choose whether you want to order a particular portion of your inventory by selecting Categories, Seasons,
SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting see Criteria or Wild Cards.

Replicate Purchase Orders

                                     Copy a Purchase Order to multiple ship-locations

Enter the Purchase Order you wish to replicate in the Replicate PO# field.
(The Bill-to Store, Order date, Ship date, Cancel date and Payment date fields will be filled in with the

                                                                                          61
Enter a 5 character prefix that will be assigned to each new purchase order. All the purchase orders that are
replicated will contain the 5 character prefix and the ship-to store. For example, if the prefix '02AUG' has a
purchase order created for store 12 the purchase order number will be '02AUG012' (notice that the store
number has is padded with zeroes to 3 places).
Enter the store or range of ship-to stores you want to replicate the purchase orders to.
Note: If a purchase order number that would be created is already on file, that purchase order will NOT
created.

Merge In-Transit Purchase Orders

                       Combines multiple In-Transit Purchase Orders into a single shipment

Enter the Purchase Order you wish to merge the in-transit purchase orders into. The 'Available Purchase
Order' list box will be filled with all unreceived in-transit purchase orders which are going to the selected
purchase order's ship to-store and from the selected purchase order's bill-to store.

                                                                                          62
Double-clicking on a purchase order will move it to the other list box.

The [Unselect All] button will unselect all the purchase orders in the appropriate list box.
Click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S] to merge the orders, or Click [Save & Print] or press [Alt] + [a] to merge the
order and print a copy of the newly merged order.
Note: The orders the have been merged will no longer exist. All the order quantities will have been combined
into the selected purchase order. Once merged, the purchase orders cannot be reclaimed.

Order Worksheet

                                              To prepare your sizes for Future Buys
By using an order worksheet you can ensure you are buying the correct sizes, quantities and Retail $ Dollars
you need for your store before you Enter Purchases Orders. By planning ahead you can greatly improve your
ROI% by investing your Open-to-Buy in the right sizes. A key to using Order Worksheets is running Size
Type Analysis.
Enter the Store#, Category#, Size Type, Season, Total Order Quantity (Total # of pairs) and Total Order
at Retail (Total Retail $Dollars).
Next enter in the Projected Sales by Sizes (The total of all percentages must equal 100). Then click on the
[SKU] or [ALT] + [S] and enter in the SKU # (the SKU does not need to be created to do a worksheet this is
only a reference), Retail Price, and Month to be shipped in (number from 1-12), and [Save].
When you select [Totals] a report will appear similar to the one below.

Receive ASN Cartons

                                       Receive entire carton with single barcode scan
Receive an entire carton from a vendor by scanning the carton barcode. The barcode is created by the
vendor for the carton. The barcode and items in the carton are sent to the store via EDI. When the carton is
received at the store, the store scans the barcode and each item in the carton is received. The store also has
the option to create a label for each item in the carton.

                                                                                          63
To edit the ASN Carton, see ASN Carton Maintenance.

ASN Carton Maintenance

                                                 Create, Delete, or Modify Cartons
The ASN Carton Maintenance screen is used to modify the ASN Carton. This should be used with caution
because when the ASN Carton is received, the items and quantities of the received items come from the ASN
Carton.
To add a new item to the carton, click the [New] button. To edit an existing entry, click the [Edit] button. To
delete an item from the carton, click the [Delete] button.

See also Receiving ASN Cartons

Reset Future Orders

                           Recalculate your Purchase Orders to Future or At=Once Orders

RICS determines whether your Purchase Orders are At-Once or Future based on whether the difference in
the entry date and the ship date is greater than the number of days you determine in RICS.CFG under section
[Purchase Orders] items DyFut. The Purchase Orders are also optionally realigned when you close your
month. This job afford the user the opportunity to realign orders in the middle of the month or just to change
change the criteria that determines how many days in advance a future order is.

Enter Manual Orders

                                     Enter orders without generating a Purchase Order
Use this option to enter manual orders. Both manual orders and purchase orders will update the on-order
amounts in the inventory files. However, with manual orders you do not have the other information stored with
a PO such as order dates and due dates of specific SKUs so orders are much easier to track if you Enter
Purchase Orders. You probably will not use this option very often.

Enter Manual Receipts

                                       Receive merchandise not on a Purchase Order
Use this option to receive merchandise NOT on a purchase order. You would also use this option to enter
inventory in RICS for the first time. When this option is used to receive merchandise, it will also update the
"date last received" that is displayed in Inventory Inquiry.
Enter the Store, and the SKU, this will then display the SKU description, Category, Vendor, Vendor SKU,
and Style/Color. You may also change the Retail Price and Cost.
Case packs: If you enter a casepack number, the sizes setup for that casepack will automatically be
displayed. To enter multiple case packs of the same SKU, use the X__ field.
Click Storing Labels, or press [Alt] + [L] to toggle the option to store labels for received items.

Enter the quantities received. After all of the quantities are entered for a SKU click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S]
to save this information. The SKU will clear and the cursor will go back to SKU. You can then enter another
SKU and its quantities. You would click [Save] after each SKU and its quantities are entered.
Click [UPC] or press [Alt] + [U] to display a UPC line to scan manual receipts into the computer.

Click [Change Store] or press [Alt] + [G] to clear the SKU and store and the cursor will go back to Store.
You can then enter a different Store #.

Enter Manual Returns

                                    Decrease on-hand quantities, or returns to vendors
Use this menu option to decrease the on-hand quantities of selected SKUs. For example, defective items that
should to be returned to the vendor. The numbers entered here will reduce the on hand amounts in your

Enter the Store, and the SKU, this will then display the SKU description, Category, Vendor, Vendor SKU,
and Style/Color. You may also change the Cost.
Case packs: If you enter a casepack number, the sizes setup for that casepack will automatically be
displayed. To enter multiple case packs of the same SKU, use the X__ field.

Enter the quantities received. After all of the quantities are entered for a SKU click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S]
to save this information. The SKU will clear and the cursor will go back to SKU. You can then enter another
SKU and its quantities. You would click [Save] after each SKU and its quantities are entered.
Click [UPC] or press [Alt] + [U] to display a UPC line to scan manual receipts into the computer.

Click [Change Store] or press [Alt] + [G] to clear the SKU and store and the cursor will go back to Store.

Click [On Hand] or press [Alt] + [O] to show the On-hand quantity for this SKU. You may make changes to

Enter Price Changes

                                Change prices immediately or make future price changes
This option provides a way to: Immediately change prices, enter a price change to take place at some future
date, enter a price change to take place at some future date and revert back to the current price at a later
date, and to use different prices for different locations (contact CSI for more information). You may also use
the option File Setup, SKUs to change prices.

Date to change price: To immediately change the price of a SKU, use the default of today's date as the date
to change price. To enter a future price change, enter the date the price is to change (RICS will inform you of
the # of days until the price change is to take effect). The price change then takes effect when you click
[Save] or press [Alt] + [S] to save this information.

Date to change price back: If left blank the Price Change becomes "PERMANENT". You can include a
date to automatically have the prices revert back to their pre-sale values after the sale by entering that date
(Optional). RICS will inform you of the # of days after the price change is to take effect until it reverts back to
the current price.

SKU: Enter the SKU (use or [Ctrl] + [P] to lookup a list of existing SKUs) you want to change the price
on. It displays the description and current pricing for this SKU.

Click on the current price option (Retail Price, Markdown 1, and Markdown 2) of the desired price or enter
the new price. Each of the current price options display the G.P. % based on the current cost.

You can make multiple price changes for the same SKU. For example, you could enter a reduced price for a
SKU effective March 1, another price reduction effective April 1, and yet another price reduction effective May
1.

You can use File Printouts, Print SKU File, to print a list of future price changes.

Each morning, when someone logs into RICS, the computer will check to see if any "future" price changes
should be made today. If so, the following is displayed:

If you click [Yes], the computer will then post the price changes for today. If you press [No], the computer will
ask the above question each time someone logs in, until the price changes have been posted (or the file is
deleted).

Change Average Cost

                                     Changes the average cost associated with an SKU
RICS will automatically calculate the average cost of a SKU for each store, or all stores whenever needed. If
necessary, you can manually adjust this amount using this option.

                                                                                          67
Enter the Store, (Enter zero [0] for all stores) and the SKU. This will then display the SKU description. You
can then change the Average Cost.
IMPORTANT: Average cost is used to compute your gross profit. If you receive SKUs at the wrong cost,
changing the current cost under File Setup, SKUs will not correct the average cost. You must also change
the average cost.
If you enter sales and post sales for SKUs with the wrong average cost, an incorrect gross profit is calculated.
When the average cost is corrected it does not retro-actively correct the past gross profit on sales of the
corrected SKU. You must first reverse the sale (as a return) with the incorrect average cost and then post the
sale. Then correct the average cost, re-enter the sale, and then print and post the sales.

Enter Model Quantities

                                             Setup or change your Model Quantities
Model quantities can be setup for each store/SKU/column/row. A model can be either the desired quantity to
maintain on hand or it can be the minimum level reorder point. Model quantities are used in both Automatic
Transfers and Automatic Purchase Orders. When printing the Stock Status Report, you have the option to
print only those SKUs that are short. This means the quantity on hand has fallen below the model quantity.
Entering models is an optional feature. Many RICS users create models only for faster moving items, or basic
stock that would require fill in orders. You don't have to create models for all SKUs.

Enter the SKU, and the Store (Enter zero [0] for all stores. To set model quantities for all stores, except for
selected stores such as a warehouse, call CSI.), this will then display the SKU description, Category,
Vendor, Vendor SKU, Style/Color, Current Cost, Average Cost and date Last Received.

                                                                                          68
Case packs: If you enter a casepack number, the sizes setup for that casepack will automatically be
displayed. To enter multiple case packs of the same SKU, use the x __ field.

If you want to enter or adjust the model quantities for multiple stores with one entry, enter the first store to
update as "Store __", and then enter the other stores (either individual or ranges, i.e. _2,5-8,11,14 ) as
Additional stores to copy the model to. You will have to click in the text area to get into this field.

Enter the Model Quantities that you want. After all of the quantities are entered for a SKU click [Save] or
press [Alt] + [S] to save this information. The SKU will clear and the cursor will go back to SKU. You can then
enter another SKU and its Model Quantities. Click [Save] after each SKU and its Model Quantities are
entered.

In addition to model quantities, RICS supports Maximum (Max) and Reorder Quantities. If a max quantity is
entered, RICS will treat all quantities with on-hand below the model quantity as short by the amount it is below
the max quantity. Using max quantities is optional and allows you to order or transfer quantities up to the max
quantity amount. This can reduce the amount of fill-in orders and transfers needed to replenish stock. Reorder
quantities allow Automatic Purchase Orders to order multiple quantities. This can be useful for items like
socks that must be orders in groups of 3 or 6.

RICS will always show the model, max, and reorder quantity amounts of the current size. Click [Max] or press
[Alt] + [A] to enter max quantities. Click [Reorder] or press [Alt] + [R] to enter reorder quantities. Click
[Model] or press [Alt] + [M] to enter model quantities. When either of the [Max], [Reorder], or [Model]
buttons are clicked, focus remains on the same size. Click [Copy], or press [Alt] + [O], to copy the Max,
Reorder, or Model quantities to another type of quantity for the current SKU.

Discontinue SKUs

                                           Discontinue or change an existing SKU #
This option can be used if the vendor changes the SKU number of an item, or to combine (discontinue)
several SKUs into a single SKU. For example: at the end of a season you decide it is no longer necessary to
track the history of several SKUs (perhaps they can no longer be ordered) and it's no longer important to
compare how one performed vs. another. You DO NOT want to delete these SKUs and lose the totals on your
reports.

Enter the Store (Enter zero [0] for all stores), under the column Item being discontinued enter the SKU #,
this will then display the Vendor, Vendor SKU, Category, Size Type, Group, Description, Style/Color,
Season, Current Cost, Retail Price, Markdown 1, Markdown 2, and Perks. None of these items can be
changed here.

Under the column Item retaining information, enter in the new SKU #, This SKU # can either be an
inventory item that already exists (in which case the discontinued SKU information is added to this existing
SKU) or it can be a brand new item (in which case the item will be added with the discontinued SKU
amounts).and press [Enter]. This will display the SKU information Vendor, Vendor SKU, Category, Size
Type, Group, Description, Style/Color, Season, Current Cost, Retail Price, Markdown 1, Markdown 2,
and Perks. You may change any of these items, plus the Current Pricing.

Click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S] to save this information after everything is filled in properly. All information
about the discontinued SKU (on hand quantity, on order quantity, quantity sales, dollar sales, etc.) will be
transferred into the new SKU number with one exception: Model Quantities of the SKU being discontinued will
not be added to the new SKU if the new SKU already has activity. When any discontinued SKU is on an
Open Purchase Order, the PO will be changed to reflect the new SKU# as still on order.

Before using this option to combine SKUs
Decide which of the following information is important for you to track: Sales information by vendor, Sales
information by category, Sales information broken down by size, all of that information, or none of
that information. The more information you track, the more hash (discontinued) SKUs you will have in RICS.

                                                                                          69
For example, if none of that information was important to keep, you would have one hash SKU to combine
everything. If it were important for you to track sales information by vendor broken down by size, you would
have a SKU for every vendor/size type combination. If it were important for you to track sales information by
just category, you would have one SKU for every category. If all the information was important for you to
track, you would have one SKU for every category/vendor/size type combination.
Other important information
Because much of the SKU history is stored by size and width, the SKU being discontinued, and the SKU
retaining the information must have the same size type. There is one exception to this rule: if you no longer
care about the individual column/row amounts, you can discontinue an SKU with a size type into an SKU with
a zero or no size type. The information for all the sizes and widths will be added together and only the totals
will be saved.
Hint: It is sometimes convenient to define a category 999 and/or a vendor ZZZZ just for discontinued items.
Then, when printing reports indexed by category and/or vendor, the discontinued items will appear at the end
of the report and will not be added into other sub-totals.

                Look at SKU's On-hand, On-order, Sales, quantities and other SKU information
Enter a SKU number and press [Enter] (You may use or [Ctrl] + [P] to display a list of existing SKUs.).
Enter a Store number and press [Enter] (You may use or [Ctrl] + [P] to display a list of existing Stores.)
Row is used only for certain Display options for a selected row of an SKU that has multiple rows.
This will display the SKU Description, and information on the Category, Vendor, Vendor SKU, Style/Color,
Size Type, and Last received date for this SKU. Displayed in the upper right corner of the screen will be the
Retail Price, Markdown 1, and Markdown 2, along with the Average Cost, Current Cost and List Price for
this SKU. Sales totals for Qty, Net, Markdown, Profit, for the period Week, Month, Season, and Year are
displayed below that.
The lower half of the screen will display the size grids based on the Display Options selected.

[O] to display the list of Options A menu similar to the following will be displayed:

Hint: To quickly change the display, press the appropriate function key [F1] through [F12], or shift and the
appropriate function key. [Shift]+[F1] or [Shift]+[F2]

Enter Price Discounts

                                 Changes Retail Prices by a Percentage or fixed Amount.
This option works like Enter Price Changes, only this option will allow you to markdown or markup all items in
the store, or for selected SKUs, categories, vendors, seasons, colors, or groups in a simple process by a
selected percentage or by a fixed dollar amount. You can also force them to end in a set cent (such as .95 or
.99). This is an ideal tool for running specials such as $10 off all Dexter, or 20% all running shoes.
HINT: This program may change the prices for many SKUs, and there is no way to reverse these price
changes if you change your mind or select the wrong SKUs. Always make a backup of your data first, and
you may want to print a Preview report of those SKUs to change to review first.

Effective date of change price: To immediately change the price of an SKU, use the default of today's date
as the date to change price. To enter a future price change, enter the date the price is to change (RICS will
inform you of the # of days until the price change is to take effect).

                                                                                          73
Date to revert to original price: If left blank the Price Change becomes "PERMANENT". Optionally, you
can include a date to automatically have the prices revert back to their pre-sale values after the sale, by
entering that date. (RICS will inform you of the # of days after the price change is to take effect until it reverts
back to the current price).
for Stores: Enter the Stores the price charges will take effect for. This option is only displayed when you
have different prices at different stores.
Decrease by: Determine whether the discount will be by a Percentage, a fixed Amount, or Reset Original
Retail Price.
Decrease prices by: The percentage or amount of the discount. (If you want to increase prices, enter a
negative number)
Force the price to end in : If you are discounting a Percentage, you have the option to force the resulting
changed price to end in a specified decimal amount. Entering -1 in this field will cause RICS to round the price
to the nearest decimal amount. This option is used to make all the new prices conform to the pricing
conventions of the store. For example, if an item priced 69.99 is going to be discounted by 25%, the new price
would be 52.49. However, by entering '99' in the force price field, the resulting price will be 51.99 or 52.99,
depending on the rounding method chosen.
Change master file also: This option is only available when you have different prices at different stores. If
check, this will update the default prices in the SKU file to the new prices.
Only change SKUs priced at the original retail price: This option will prevent any items currently at a
markdown price from being effected by the price discount changes.
Compute discounts from the original retail price (not current price): This option will cause the discount
to be calculated from the original retail price (not a markdown). This enables the user to have items 10% off
retail, 20% off retail, and 30% off retail without having to calculate discounts of discounts.
Change Perks allows you to set a new dollar amount for the perks.
Rounding Method allows the user to choose how to round the changed price. The choices are to Round to
the nearest cent/dollar, Always round up or Always round down. Normally, the rounding will be to the
nearest penny, but if the Force the price to end in option is chosen, the rounding will be done to the nearest
amount ending in the decimal chosen.
Place new price in: You may choose to place the new price in the current price (retail or markdown) being
used in the first available markdown price. (If all the available markdown price slots are in use, the new
price will be placed in the last markdown bucket)

                                                                                          74
Criteria: Enter your selections for SKUs, Categories, Vendors, Seasons, Style/Color, Groups, or
Keywords.
Click [Process] or press [Alt] + [R] to save or process the price changes.
YOU MUST MAKE A BACKUP OF YOUR DATA BEFORE PROCESSING.
Click [Preview] or press [Alt] + [P] to preview the price changes before you process them.

inventory), this job will create a transfer from a warehouse or brick and mortar store to the Internet store,
zeroing out the inventory

The system will always keep this report to the screen spool file, even if you print directly to the printer.

Enter Manual Transfers

                                         Transfer inventory from one store to another
This option is used to transfer inventory from one store to another. The quantity on hand for both stores is
updated immediately. The system does not track transfers in transit between stores. A journal will be printed
and these transfers will also appear on the Transfer Summary report.

Enter the From Store, To Store, and the SKU. This will then display the SKU description, Category, Vendor,
Vendor SKU, Style/Color, Current Cost, Average Cost, and Last received date for this SKU. When sizes or
quantities are entered the system will total them as they are entered.

Click [UPC] or press [Alt] + [U] to display a UPC line to scan manual transfers into the computer.

Click [Change Store] or press [Alt] + [G] to clear the SKU and store and the cursor will go back to Store.
You can then enter a different Store #.

[Transfer All] or press [Alt] + [A] to default the screen with all of the on hand quantity of the "from" store.

[Show On-Hand] or press [Alt] + [O] to display the "from" store's on hand quantities for the selected SKU.

After entering transfers between stores, an option is available to print a transfer pick list on 8 1/2 by 11"
paper, sorted by store. With this option, you can enter all transfers to and from any store, in any order, and
when completed, a transfer pick list will sort the entries and print all transfers grouped by each store. This
report can then be sent or faxed to each store to instruct them with which items to ship to each other store. If
you answer "N", you can enter more transfers at a later time and all transfers will be sorted and printed
together.

Generate Automatic Transfers

                          Automatically transfer inventory from the warehouse to the stores
This option is for users who use a warehouse to receive all their merchandise and update their stores
periodically from this warehouse based upon model quantities. This option will calculate the SKUs and
quantities to transfer, print a pick list (or transfer journal), and will always print a transfer journal to the screen
spool file, and post the transfers to the inventory files. Before running Automatic Transfers you need to Enter
Model Quantities. The model quantity for each store-SKU-column-row combination is the quantity of that item
you would like to have on hand. Each day, you should have entered, printed and posted all sales transactions
so that the on hand quantity for your stores is current. Enter Manual Transfers to reverse any Automatic
Transfer transaction.

Sort Report by: Selects how the report will print by SKU, Vendor, Category, or Location (Store)

Enter the criteria for Vendors, Categories, Seasons, Groups, Keywords, SKUs, the Warehouse Store,
and the Transfer into stores and run.

Additionally, the transfers may be made into In-Transit Purchase Orders. These transfers will reduce the on-
hand levels at the warehouse but must be received at the stores in order to have the transfer completed. To
Reverse an Automatic Transfer made into an In-Transit purchase Order, the In-Transit Purchase Order must
be cancelled and the transfer amount placed back into the warehouse stores on-hand inventory, either by
Manual Receipts or as part of a Physical Inventory. Please contact Technical Support to find out more about
In-Transit Purchase Orders.

The lower numbered stores are transferred before the higher numbered stores ( i.e., all transfers to store 1
are computed, posted and printed, and then all transfers for store 2 are done, and so on). If you want to
transfer to stores in a different order, other than store number order, contact CSI.

To determine what is short in the warehouse, print the Stock Status report excluding the warehouse store,

                                                                                          76
and print only the short items (quantity on hand is less than the model quantity). This report will list the SKUs
that could not be transferred.
If multiple copies of this report are needed, either (a) use multi-part paper or (b) print from the screen spool
file. When viewing the report on the screen, any number of copies can be printed. The system will always
print the report to the screen spool file, even if you print directly to the printer.

Generate Balancing Transfers

             Generate Transfers that move inventory to stores based on ROI, Turns, or Sell Thru
This option is for users with multiple stores. Generate Balancing Transfers calculates the SKUs and quantities
to transfer based on ROI, Turns, or Sell Thru sending items from the lowest performing stores to the best
performing stores.

When using the Balancing Method Transfer SKUs Over/Under Models, only SKUs with a model setup are
affected. To setup models, see Enter Model Quantities. The model quantity for each store-SKU-column-row
combination is the quantity of that item you would like to have on-hand. Each day, you should have entered,
printed and posted all sales transactions so that the on hand quantity for your stores is current. Enter Manual
Transfers to reverse any Generate Balancing Transfer transactions. When this option is selected, SKUs
without a model setup are not included in the transfer. If the Transfer SKUs without models option is
selected, only SKUs without models are included in the transfer. The Transfer SKUs without considering
models option considers all inventory items that meet the selection criteria.
Sort Transfers by: Selects the sort order the report print: Category, Vendor, or SKU
Balancing Method selections allow you to choose which method to determine the quantities to transfer.
Transfer SKUs without considering models (default) and Transfer SKUs without models transfer single
items to stores that have zero on-hand in a store that is better than a store. Transfer SKUs
Transfer based on Sales Period allows you to select the sales period to calculate the ROI, Turns, and Sell-
Thru.
Transfer inventory based on allows you to select which performance monitor you want to base the transfer
criteria on (ROI, Turns, or Sell-Thru). The stores' priority is determined based on the selection made here. If
there is a decision the computer has to make to transfer the last item and there are more than 1 store to
transfer it to, When deciding to transfer inventory, give priority to stores with selection provides two
options. The first option is Turns/ROI/Sell-Thru ____ more than another store where the deciding factor to
transfer the item is based on the Turns, ROI, or Sell-Thru being X amount more than another store. The
second option is Turns/ROI/Sell-Thru ____ % higher than another store where the deciding factor to
transfer the item is based on the Turns, ROI, or Sell-Thru being X % more than another store.

                                                                                          77
Transfer doubles to lower priority stores is an option that when selected has higher priority stores send an
item to a lower priority store if the higher priority store has two or more on-hand and the lower priority store
has zero on-hand.
Transfer all inventory out of stores that have less than ____ sizes on-hand is an option that when
selected takes inventory out of a store that has less than the specified number of sizes on-hand. Those items
are then transferred to other stores.
You can preview the transfers without actually making the transfers by selecting the Print a journal of what
would be transferred without making the transfer option. This prints a report showing which items are
affected by running the Generate Balancing Transfers job with the options and criteria selected.
Make the transfers and print the journal option MAKES the transfers. The Make In-Transit PO's option
can be checked to make the transfers In-Transit purchase orders. When selected, you also have the option to
Print In-Transit PO's and if that is checked, the option to Print Columnar PO's is also available and when
selected does not print the purchase order in the size grid format, but lists each size and column on its own
line.

Enter criteria for Stores, Categories, Vendors, Seasons, Style/Colors, SKUs, Groups, and Keywords.
Click the eye to lookup any of the criteria options and add them to criteria. You have the option to Include
only SKUs at the original retail price or Include only SKUs at markdown prices to further limit the
quantity of items in the transfer. You also have the option include only SKUs with Perks.
Add the job to Job List by clicking either the Add Job and Run or Add Job and Continue buttons.
