                                    LLAABBEELLSS

Setup Stock Label Printer

A bar code label is a printed series of vertical bars that vary in width. Bar codes can be "read" and decoded
by a bar code scanner. A bar code contains no information about the SKU. The Bar code Cross Reference
refers the bar code # to a SKU#, column, and row. (Example: Bar code# 4 2724243415 5 refers to SKU#
47532 in Size 070 Width M). All information (prices, cost, etc.) then comes from what has been entered for
that SKU#.

To set up your Stock Label Printer

You only need to setup your printer once, unless you change printers. To setup a printer click: [Change
Printer], and select from the list of Printers Setup in Windows. Printers must be setup in Windows before they
will be listed here. Make sure you have answered the question "Automatically generate labels" in Company
Setup before hand.

Select the label type/size you are using for your printer.
Dot Matrix Printers: select either the 1" X 3 1/2 or 1" X 2 1/2 (1 across)
Laser Printers: select Laser or Ink jet (3X10 sheets) (Avery label #5160)
Zebra* (LP/TLP) Printers: Select Zebra (LP/TLP)
Barcode Blazer: Select Barcode Blazer

Select the font to use. The fonts listed are the fonts that you have in your computer. Recommended fonts in
both compressed and un-compressed are Courier New, Line Printer or Lucida Console. You may want to
experiment with some of the other fonts to get a different look to your labels.

Indicate how many copies of each label should be printed. The Number of labels to print will default to 1, but
can be up to 9.

*PLEASE NOTE: Zebra printers were formerly manufactured under the name Eltron. All settings and
instructions under either name are interchangeable with regards to appropriate model number.

Enter Stock Labels

                                        To generate labels without affecting inventory

Most people generate labels automatically when they are entering orders or receipts. You can, however, use
this menu option to generate labels to print without affecting either on-hand or on-order quantities.

If you use this option after you order or receive merchandise you run the risk of duplicating your labels. In
other words, if you were receiving merchandise and "Storing Labels", you DO NOT need to use this option to
generate stock labels. You need to answer the question How are labels to be selected: one of five ways.

#1- All SKU's one label for each item on hand is used to print labels for all SKUs on hand for selected
Stores, Categories, Vendors, SKUs, Groups, Keywords, Season, Date Last Received or Markdown, or
Pricing status (retail or markdown). For more information about selecting see Criteria or Wild Cards.

#2- Selected SKU's one label for each on hand is used to generate labels for a selected SKU/store. What
ever your on-hand quantity is for the selected SKU/store is the number of labels that will print for that SKU.
For example, if you selected SKU# 1234 for store 1, and its on-hand quantity was 10, 10 labels will print for
that SKU. You can change the default quantities.

                                                                                          82
#3- Selected SKU's user enters what labels to print is used to create labels for a selected SKU/store. You
select how many labels you want for each SKU/size. For example, if you selected SKU# 1234, you would
choose the quantity of each size that you wanted. This is ideal for an item returned by a customer with no
label on it, or when a label was ruined before it was put on the merchandise.

#4- Purchase Order SKU's one label for each item on PO is used to create labels for each item on a
Purchase Order. Choose whether you want to select/print a particular purchase order by Stores, Categories,
Vendors, SKUs, Groups, Keywords, Season, or Purchase Order. For more information about selecting
see Criteria or Wild Cards.

#5- Display labels SKU's one label for each SKU/Store is used to print 1 label for each selected
SKU/Store. You may select SKUs by Stores, Categories, Vendors, SKUs, Groups, Keywords, Season,
Date Last Received or Markdown, Pricing Status (retail or markdown), or seelct only SKUs that are
on-hand. For more information about selecting see Criteria or Wild Cards. This option is available to print a
custom label for a display rack. For more information, please contact CSI Services.

Print Stock Labels

                                              Prints labels currently in the label file

Label Type - A label code is assigned to each SKU created in File Setup - SKUs. Select the type of label of
label you want to print. Items in the label file with the selected code will print.

Label Indent - moves to the right the # of characters entered.

Print date - If checked the current date will print on the label. It will appear after the description in a coded
format: the last digit of the year followed by the month in reverse order. For example, March, 1999 would
appear as 930.

Printing Format
     · No Price on label: No price will not print on the label
     · Original Price on label: The original selling price of the item will print on the label. Even if the item is
          on sale, the original price will be printed.
     · Current Price on label: The current selling price of the item will print on the label. If the item is on
          sale, the sale price will be printed.
     · List Price (no price if List=0): Prints only List prices or no price if List is blank or 0
     · List Price (original price if List=0): Prints only List prices or the original price if the List price is
          blank or 0.
     · List Price (current price if List=0): Prints only List prices or the current price if List price is blank or
          0.
     · Current & List Price: The current selling price and the list price will print on the label.
     · Original & List Price: The original selling price and the list price will print on the label.

NOTE: List Price Label may be changed to SUGG, REG., COMP, OUR, etc., up to 4 characters.

Print UPCs - When checked, a UPC barcode will print on the label. RICS will automatically assign a UPC
number. DO NOT Change starting #.

      This is the choice of all new users who will print bar code labels.

Printing Labels - Check to make sure the labels are lined up in the printer properly. Click the [Test Pattern]
button to print a test label. This can be used to determine if the labels need to be moved up, down, left, or
right in the printer. It may be pressed as often as necessary. When the labels are lined up properly, click the
[Print Labels] button and all labels for the selected store and label code will print.

                                                                                          83
Laser Printer - A test pattern can not be done with a laser printer. Lasers can use a sheet of labels that is
partially used, it will then ask Start printing labels on row.

Deleting Labels - Click the [Delete Labels] button to delete all unprinted labels. A question will appear
confirming that all labels should be deleted.

Common Problems for all Printers:

Printer jams: Press [Esc] to cancel printing, adjust the forms and then start printing again. It will not print all
labels -- it should resume printing a few labels before the jam occurred. If all labels have been printed and
need to be re-printed, before trying to reprint the labels, click the [Restore Labels] button and then select
to print stock labels again and the last batch of labels will print again.

Labels will not print:
          1. Make sure the proper store and/or label code is selected.
          2. Make sure the printer is turned on and is on-line.
          3. Make sure the printer is connected to the computer properly.

Enter UPC Cross Reference

                                      Manually create or look at a UPC cross-reference

This option can be used to manually create a UPC cross-reference, or to look up an existing UPC cross
reference. A UPC number represents a single SKU/COLUMN/ROW.

Creating a UPC Cross-Reference - Type in the UPC number to be added to the cross-reference file. Enter in
the SKU/COLUMN/ROW that the UPC number represents. Click [Save] to save the information.

UPC Cross-reference Lookup: This will determine which SKU/COLUMN/ROW is assigned to a particular
UPC number. Enter the UPC number. The SKU/COLUMN/ROW it represents will be displayed. If no SKU
information is displayed, the UPC cross-reference has not yet been created for that number.

Import Vendor UPCs

                                        To get vendor UPCs from diskette or thru EDI
This option is used to read a UPC cross-reference diskette (GMAIC format) from the manufacturer, or thru
EDI. Before this option can be run, the NRF Codes and the Vendor SKU must be entered for the appropriate
size types and SKUs.

File Name - The complete file name is the drive letter, directory name, and file name with extension.

Example: C:\UPC\GMAIC.TXT

Drive letter = C:
Directory name = \UPC
File name = \GMAIC
Extension = .TXT

DO NOT read a file that has a ".zip" or ".exe" extension. Files with those extensions are "compressed" files
and need to be "de-compressed" before they are processed.

Drive letter - the disk drive containing the UPC cross-reference file. Valid choices are usually 'A', or 'C'. Use
the 'A' drive when the file is being processed from a diskette. Select 'C' when the file is on the hard drive.

                                                                                          84
Directory name - It is recommended that a directory be created for UPC files processed from the hard drive.
For example, a directory called UPC would be created at the DOS Prompt by typing [md\upc] and pressing
[enter]. DO NOT process files in the RICS directory.

File name - Is the name the vendor gave the file.

Extension - There are usually three different ways vendors provide the UPC cross-reference file: TXT, EXE,
or ZIP. The following is more information on each. Note: These directions are not exact; they are meant as a
reference.

1) TXT - The file can be read directly from the diskette. For file name, just indicate the diskette drive (i.e. A:)
      place the first diskette in that drive, and click [Add Job and Run].

2) EXE - The file is compressed in a self-extracting file. A file that is self-extracting usually has an "EXE"
      extension. In this instance the diskette is copied to the hard drive before it is de-compressed.

     For example, at the C:> prompt type [copy a:*.* \upc] and press [Enter]. This would copy the file(s) to
      the UPC directory in drive C (Note: The UPC directory must be created first). Change to the UPC
      directory once the copy is complete. For example, type [cd\upc] and press [Enter]. Type in the name of
      the file contained on the diskette with ".EXE". The file to be read in RICS will be "extracted" and
      renamed. The new file name will usually have a ".TXT" extension.

3) ZIP - The file is compressed using PKUNZIP. A file compressed with PKUNZIP usually has a "ZIP"
      extension. In this instance, while the file is unzipped to the hard drive it is un-compressed. For example,
      with the diskette in the diskette drive, from the A:> prompt, type [pkunzip upc_data.zip c:\upc] and
      press [Enter] to un-compress the file to a directory called UPC on drive C (Note: The UPC directory
      must be created first). The file to be read in RICS will be "Unzipped" and renamed. The new file name
      will usually have a ".TXT" extension.

If two different vendors use the exact same Vendor SKU number, RICS will use the vendor's qualifier and ID
from the vendor file to determine which SKU to reference the UPC to.

Note: Many vendors will send many more SKUs on their UPC diskettes than what retailers use in their store.
If an NRF code is not found, RICS will print an exception report of all invalid UPC entries. The report will print
the vendor's description and of that size to help explain or identify the exception. The system will
automatically print this sometimes lengthy report to the screen spool file, even if the printer preferences are
set to print to your local printer. Use Look at Screen Spool File to view this report.

You also have the option to Delete file after import, or to Re-import Bar codes that are already on file, by
checking the appropriate boxes.

Print UPC Cross Reference

                                                  Prints report on UPC bar codes.
There are two different types of UPCs. The Vendor UPCs where the Vendor gives you a cross-reference file
to read their bar codes either by a diskette or thru EDI, or user-generated UPCs where the UPCs are created
by the system when you print labels.

Report Options:
Include SKUs that have no Vendor UPCs?:
Yes will list All SKUs based upon the selected Criteria.
No will list ONLY SKUs with Vendor UPCs on file based upon the selected Criteria.
Only print SKUs with no Vendor UPCs will list ONLY SKUs with No Vendor UPCs on file based upon the

      selected Criteria.

Print Vendor UPCs when checked on will also print the Vendor UPCs to the selected report.
Print user-generated UPCs when checked on will also print the user-generated UPCs to the selected report.

                                                                                          85
Criteria: Choose whether you want to select/print a particular portion of your UPCs by Categories, Vendors,
      Seasons, SKUs, Style/Color, Size Types, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting
      see Criteria or Wild Cards.

Generate UPC Numbers

                                     Generate UPC barcodes for all items in the system
This option will create a UPC barcode for every SKU/Column/Row combination presently in the system. This
option would be used so any POS location could then print their barcode labels. If the POS location is not
going to print labels it is not necessary to run this option.

                             SSAALLEESS RREEPPOORRTTSS

Overview

Sales Analysis Report - Most commonly used report because of all its options.
Eight Week Trending - Will maintain and report on eight weeks of sales information.
Best Sellers Report -This report can be used to print your best/worst selling SKUs.
Sales History by Month Report -Reports quantities or dollars sold for the current month and each of the last
12 months.
Stock Status Report -This will print reports by Sizes (Column/Row).
Size Type Analysis Report -This will report Analysis by Sizes (Column/Row)
Open-To-Buy vs. Sales Report -This report compares the actual sales for the month and year with planned
sales.
Open-To-Buy Report -This report prints a 12 month open-to-buy projection.
General Ledger Summary Report -This report prints the monthly debit/credit totals.

The following are some of the headings listed on reports:

Qty - Quantity.
Retail - The Current Retail Price
Avg. Cost - The Average Cost
Curr Cost - The Current Cost
Mkdn Cost - The Markdown Cost
Value - Total Value of the Quantity at Retail or Cost
%-Str - Percent of store total
%-Rpt - Percent of Report total
Age - Number of days between the date last received and the current date
Sales - Total retail sales less markdowns and returns
Mkdwn% - The markdown percent (To determine markdown $, multiply the Sales x Mkdwn %.)
Profit ­ Profit (Sales less the cost of goods sold)
GP-% - Gross profit percent the percent of Profit (divided by) Sales
ROI% - Return on investment percentage. Sometimes known as GMROI (Gross Margin Return On

                     Investment) is a combined measurement of how quickly your inventory sold, and how
                     profitable it was. The ROI% is always annualized regardless of what period is being
                     analyzed.
        It is strongly recommended that you use ROI% as part of your inventory review, because it is
        the best overall indicator of performance.
Turns - Turnover rate is a measurement of how quickly your inventory is selling. Turnover is always
                     annualized even if the period analyzed is for a month or season.
V-SKU - Vendor SKU #
Weeks - The number of weeks supply on hand based upon current month sales

Sales Analysis Report

                               The most commonly used report because of all its options
The sales analysis report always prints the current On-Hand Inventory Quantity, inventory value amounts, and
the age of SKUs in addition to any sales information that may is requested.

Report Options:
Analyze by:

     · Category will list the report in order of the SKUs category
     · Vendor will list the report in order of the SKUs vendor code
     · Season will list the report in order of the SKUs season code
     · Group will list the report in order of the SKUs group code
Store Options:
     · Separate Stores will print each store separately
     · Compare Stores will print each store's information for each item. This method provides an easy

          comparison
     · Combine Stores will print each item's data for all stores at once
Type of Report:
     · SKU Detail prints individual SKUs sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option. Each SKU will be on a line by

          itself. If you select this report type you may summarize the data by SKU description by checking the
                                                box that will appear

     · Category Summary prints 1 category per line sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option. Department totals
          will also be printed

     · Department Summary prints 1 department per line sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option
     · Style/Color Summary prints 1 style/color per line as per the SKU file sorted by the 'Analyze by'

          Option
     · Vendor Summary prints 1 vendor per line as per the SKU file sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option
     · Price Point Summary allows you to analyze the price points within the 'Analyze by' option or Store

          Totals Only. You will be asked to determine the price points to analyze by entering a Beginning
          Price Point, a Price Increment, and an Ending Price Point.
     · Season Summary prints 1 season per line as per the SKU file sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option
     · Group Summary prints 1 group code per line as per the SKU file sorted by the 'Analyze by' Option.

                                                                                          88
Criteria:
Choose whether you want to select/print a particular portion of your inventory by Stores, Categories,
Vendors, Seasons, Style/Color, SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting
see Criteria or Wild Cards. Use the Lookup icon to insert a selection.
You may also choose to include only SKUs priced at the original retail price or SKUs prices at a
markdown price by checking the appropriate check box. Leave both unchecked to include SKUs regardless of
the current price. The other option is to include SKUs with perks which shows only items with a sales perk.

Values and Dates:
Show Percentages:
RICS can show you a percentage of each line item's on-hand value, sales, and profit as compared to the total

      of your choosing.
Percent of Store compares the line items to the entire store, even items not selected to print.
Percent of Report compares the line items to what has been selected to print for this store.
No Percents prevents any percentages from printing. Choosing this report will make your report run faster.
Value On-Hand Inventory at:
RICS can show you the value of your on-hand inventory in the following ways
Retail Price values your inventory by the current retail price of each SKU.
Average Cost values your inventory by the average cost of each SKU.
Current Cost values your inventory by the current cost of each SKU.
Markdown Cost computes market value of inventory that has been marked down from its original retail price.

      This figure is sometimes used as the inventory valuation for accounting purposes. If an SKU does not

                                                                                          89
      have a markdown retail price, then markdown cost will equal the current cost. Otherwise, the markdown
      cost is computed by taking the markdown price and dividing by the original retail price. That total is
      multiplied by the current cost. The result is markdown cost.

Retail Price and Average Cost or Retail Price and Current Cost will value your inventory by the current
      retail price and the average or current cost of each SKU. When running the report by one of these two
      options you will be able to select only one of the Printing Options.

Aging Options:
Date Last Received selects only those SKUs that have been last received in the specified date range.
Date First Received selects only those SKUs that have been first received in the specified date range.
NOTE: When comparing or combining stores, the date first received for an SKU will be considered the

      earliest date first received for any store and the date last received will be considered the latest date last
      received for any store. The SKUs data will be printed for all the stores or the SKU will not be printed at
      all. The dates an SKU is first and last received can be set by transferring merchandise if the user has
      selected to activate that option.
Age by allows you to age the merchandise by the date first received or the date last received. This option is
      only available when printing SKU detail.

Printing Options:
You may not select more than two of the Print Selections.
Week-to-Date prints the sales totals for Week-to-Date. You may not choose Prior Year or Inventory Summary
Month-to-Date prints the sales totals for Month-to-Date. You may not choose Inventory Summary.
Season-to-Date prints the sales totals for Season-to-Date. You may not choose Inventory Summary.
Year-to-Date prints the sales totals for Year-to-Date. You may not choose Inventory Summary.
Prior Year prints the prior year Month-to-Date, prior year Season-to-Date, or prior year Year-to-Date totals

      depending on which sales period you selected. If you are in the middle of a month and run a prior year
      report, the report will give you the totals through the entire month of last year. You may not choose
      Inventory Summary, On order amounts, or Last number of months when this printing option is selected.
Inventory Summary allows you to review the inventory activity for Month, Season, or Year to date, and by
      Quantity, At Costs, or At Retail (when run by month to date) showing Beginning Balance, Receipts,
      Sales, Returns, Transfers In, Transfers Out, Physical Inventory Adjustments, Markdowns, and Ending
      Inventory along with Sell Thru Percentages.
On Order amounts prints on order quantities and amounts with options for At-Once, Future, or In-Transit
      Orders. However, In-Transit Orders cannot be combined with any other type of purchase order on this
      report.
Last number of months requires you to answer the How many months (2-12) question. Enter the number
      of months from 2 to 12 that you want this report for. The current month is included in one of the months

                                                                                          90
      selected. For example, if the last 2 months were selected, this will print the current month and the last
      month combined.
Export as comma delimited file checkbox allows you to export the sales analysis report to a comma-
      delimited file specified in the Export Filename text box. The Export Filename must have a file extension
      of ".TXT" or ".CSV".

Trending Options:
This will give you the option to print the 8-week trending information for each line item when you check the
Include 8 week trending box.
If you are printing SKU detail you will also be able to select SKUs having a Weekly or Period sell thru %
Greater than or Less than ____% for ___ of the last ___ weeks. Example: You could run a report to show
any SKU with a sell thru percent that was greater than 15% for 3 of the last 4 weeks (up to 8 weeks). For
more information see Eight Week Trending. Note that when comparing or combining stores, the trending for
all stores are combined and then checked against the trending criteria before the SKU is printed. The SKUs
data will be printed for all the stores or the SKU will not be printed at all.

Eight Week Trending

                              Will maintain and report on eight weeks of sales information
RICS can maintain eight weeks of sales information (Current + the prior 7 weeks). You can view the total
number sold, inventory adjustments, sell thru percentages, and weekly supply on-hand. This information can
be printed in a Sales Analysis Report or "viewed" in the Inventory Inquiry for any SKU. It also provides you
with two types of sell through percentages (Weekly or Period) for the current week and the last seven
weeks. This information can be used to spot and adjust to trends in your sales and inventory.

IMPORTANT NOTE: You must always Close Week each and every week, on the same day each week for 8
week trending to track accurately. You may want to use Reminders to give you a reminder every seven days
to close out your week.

8-week trending format: Below is a sample format of what the eight-week trending may look like on the
Sales Analysis report, or from Inventory Inquiry.

                     7     6     5      4     3     2  1 Curr

              ----- ----- ----- -----         ----- ----- ----- -----

Avail/Week              - 34 28 23            32 27 85 75
Avail/Period
Rec/Tran/Adj            - 34 34 34            32 32 85 85
Sales
ST%/Weekly              - 34        -      -  14       - 63  -
ST%/Period
                        -     6     5      5     5     5 10 10

                        - 17.6 17.9 21.7      15.6 18.5 11.8 13.3

                        - 17.6 14.7 14.7      >15.6 15.6 >11.8 11.8

                                    91
The > (greater than sign) next to some of the period sell through percentages indicates that your period
"reset" on that week. An inventory adjustment (Rec/Tran/Adj) "resets" the period. A Period is the length of
time between inventory adjustments.
Avail/Week = Total Available On-Hand Inventory for Week (Weekly beginning balance + Rec/Tran/Adj for

                       that week)
Avail/Period =Total Available On-Hand Inventory for the Period (Period beginning balance + Total of

                       Rec/Tran/Adj for all weeks thru the current week)
Rec/Tran/Adj =Any receipts (PO or Manual), returns to vendors, transfers (In or Out), or inventory

                       adjustments (+ or -), but NOT A SALE or Customer Return.
Sales = All SALES, Lay-a-way sales, special order pickups, or Customer Returns (-).
ST%/Weekly =Weekly Sell through Percentage (The percentage of what sold that week (Sales) divided by

                       the Total Available On-Hand Inventory for that week (Avail/Week).
ST%/Period =Weekly Sell through Percentage (The percentage of what sold that week (Sales) divided by the

                       Total Available On-Hand Inventory for that period (Avail/Period).
Example: ST%/Weekly Calculation - In week 5 you sold a quantity of 5 (Sales) and Available inventory to
sell for the week is 28 (Avail/Week) 5 / 28 =17.9%
Example: ST%/Period Calculation - In week 4 you sold a quantity of 5 (Sales) and Available inventory to
sell for the period is 34 (Avail/Period) 5 / 34 =14.7%
Example: ST%/Period > Reset Calculation - In week 3 you have a beginning on hand inventory of 18
(Week 4 Avail/Week of 23 minus Week 4 Sales of 5, 23-5=18) you receive (Rec/Tran/Adj) a quantity of 14.
The Avail/Period week 3 is then rest to 32, (18+14=32)

Print Inventory value by:

Size Type Analysis Report

                                          This Analyzes by Size Types (Column/Row)

The key to this report is timing. It should be run periodically during the year and at the end of the season
before any large-scale markdowns. The intent is to determine which columns/rows are selling at the best rate
and which columns/rows are over or under stocked. If a sell thru percentage for the season is 10%, it would
be safe to say that particular column/row was overstocked. On the other hand, if the sell thru percentage was
100%, you might have been under stocked and losing potential sales. A key consideration is your size type
file. This report will only combine percentages on like size types. Therefore, the more different size types you
use, the more totals there will be on this report to analyze.

It can be used to determine the best selling columns/rows (sizes/widths, colors/size, waist/length, etc.) by
reviewing the sell thru percentage for each vendor or category. You can also check next season's future
orders to see if you ordered the right sizes by running on-order (Future) quantity. Check by color and size (ex:
white shoes on order), to compare with a previous report to see if on order quantities reflect previous sell thru
%.

Report Options:

Sort by:
     · Category - SKUs are sorted by their respective category
     · Vendor - SKUs are sorted by their respective vendor
     · Combine - prints the combined summary for all stores
     · Print SKU Detail - prints detail for each SKU (this could be a very lengthy report)

Criteria:

Choose whether you want to select/print a particular portion of your inventory by Stores, Categories,
      Vendors, Seasons, Style/Colors, SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting
      see Criteria or Wild Cards.

Printing Options:

Print:
     · On-Hand - prints the On-Hand Quantity and/or % of Total
     · On-Order (At-Once) - prints the At-Once On-Order Quantity and/or % of Total
     · On-Order (Future) - prints the Future On-Order Quantity and/or % of Total
     · On-Order (Total) - prints the Total On-Order Quantity and/or % of Total
     · Sales - prints the Quantity sold and/or % of Total sold, and/or Sell thru %. Sell thru percent is the
          percentage of your inventory that was available for sale that sold.
     · Available - prints the Available Quantity and/or % of Total. Available is the quantity that was on-
          hand at the beginning of the year plus all changes (i.e. receipts, transfers, returns).

                                                                                          99
Open-To-Buy vs. Sales Report

               This report compares the actual sales for the month and year with planned sales
This report compares the actual sales for the month and year with planned sales. It gives you a feel for
whether your planned sales have been accurate for the last several months. Using this information, you can
adjust your planned sales, which is important for the O-T-B report. You need to set up an Open-To-Buy Plan
before running this report.
You may select Stores and/or Categories for this report.
If you choose not to Include Category Totals, only department and store totals will be printed.

Open-To-Buy Report

                                   This report prints a 12 month Open-to-Buy projection
This report prints a 12 month open-to-buy projection based upon planned sales, turnover, and gross profit
percentage showing last years' sales, planned sales, required beginning of month inventory, on order, and
open-to-buy (at retail, cost and quantity). You need to set up an Open-To-Buy Plan before running this report.
You may select Stores and/or Categories for this report.
If you choose not to Include Category Totals, only department and store totals will be printed.
You may also select to combine Stores for this report.

General Ledger Summary Report

                                      This report prints the monthly debit/credit totals
This report prints the monthly debit/credit totals for the different accounts and can then be entered into your
general ledger system. These account totals include Cash, Non-Cash, House Accounts, Special Orders,
Layaways, Gift certificates, Sales Tax, Sales, Cost of Goods Sold, Other Charges, Payouts, and
Over/Short.
You may select only Stores for this report.
Export as comma delimited file checkbox allows you to export the sales analysis report to a comma-

      delimited file specified in the Export Filename text box. The Export Filename must have a file extension
      of ".TXT" or ".CSV".

Create NPD Export File

                                 Exports the Inventory On Hand and On Order Quantities
This job is used to output a file of SKUs with either monthly sales or on-hand quantities into a format that can
be read by the NPD Group. NPD is working with the NSRA to create compiled retail sales reports. In order to
run this job, you must have a NPD-assigned ID code. An audit file will also be generated in RICS to allow
you to verify the information being exported. The job is designed to be run at month-end. The following
options are available:

Export Options:
Export file name: This is the path and file name of the export file that will be created from running this job. If

      the created file has an extension of 'ZIP', the exported file will be called NPDFILE.TXT and will be
      compressed into the selected file name. Otherwise, the created file must have an extension of 'TXT'.

Criteria:
Choose whether you want to limit your export to a particular portion of your inventory by Categories,

      Vendors, Seasons, Style/Colors, SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting
      see Criteria or Wild Cards.

                                                                                         101
Export Inventory Quantities

                                 Exports the Inventory On Hand and On Order Quantities
This job will export your SKU information, including on hand and on order quantities into a Comma-delimited
file. This file can then be loaded into spreadsheets, database programs, or even to your internet store
provider for further processing.
Information exported:
Store, SKU, Size Row, Size Column, On Hand Quantity, On Order Quantity (Current), On Order Quantity
(Future), Current Selling Price, Vendor Code, Category, Vendor SKU, Vendor Color Code, Description, Style
Color, Season Code, Group Code, Size Type, UPC Code.

Export Options:
Export file name is the path and file name of the export file that will be created from running this job. If the

      created file has an extension of 'ZIP', the exported file will be called QUANTITY.TXT and will be
      compressed into the selected file name. Otherwise, the created file must have an extension of 'TXT'.
Combine Stores should be checked if the or hand and on order are to be to combined. Leaving this option
      unchecked will cause each store's data to be exported separately.

Criteria:
Selections: Choose whether you want to limit your export to a particular portion of your inventory by

      Categories, Vendors, Seasons, Style/Colors, SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information
      about selecting see Criteria or Wild Cards.

                                                                                         102
Export SKUs to HTML

                   This job exports SKU information (including pictures) into an HTML format
This job is used to output SKU information, including SKU pictures, into an HTML formatted document that
can be viewed with an internet browser. This is most often helpful when you need to view a number of SKU
pictures at the same time. The following options are available:

Export Options:
HTML File Prefix: This is an 8-character name that ALL the HTML pages that are created will start with. The

      files will be created in an 'HTML' subdirectory under your RICS data directory. Each prefix should be
      unique to avoid overwriting existing HTML pages.
Primary Sort: Sort the SKUs by Category, Vendor, SKU, or Season. If the primary sort is by Category,
      Vendor or Season, every new category, vendor, or season will trigger a new HTML page being created.
Secondary Sort: If you are not sorting by SKU, you can further sort the SKUs by Category, Vendor, SKU,
      Season, or Style/Color. This only affects the order in which the SKUs are displayed and will not cause
      any new HTML pages to be created on a change of sort value.

SKU Criteria:
Selections: Choose whether to select/print a particular portion of inventory by Categories, Vendors,

      Seasons, Style/Colors, SKUs, Groups, or Keywords. For more information about selecting see
      Criteria or Wild Cards.
Only process SKUs with pictures: Check this box to only show SKUs that you have assigned pictures on
      the HTML pages that will be produced. To find out how to assign pictures to SKUs, see File Setup -
      SKUs.

                                                                                         103
Stock Criteria:
Use Stock Criteria: Check this box to use stock quantity criteria to determine which SKUs will be processed.
Stores: Select which stores are used to determine whether the SKUs meet stock quantity requirements.
Include SKUs that: Check the appropriate box(es) to include SKUs that are On-Hand, On-Order(Current and

      Future combined), or have week, month, season, or year to date sales.

PO Criteria:
Use Purchase Order Criteria: Check this box to use purchase order criteria to determine which SKUs are

      processed.
Ship-to Stores: Select only SKUs on purchase orders shipping to the selected stores.
PO's: Choose only SKUs on selected Purchase Orders. For more information about selecting see Criteria or

      Wild Cards.
Ship Dates: Select only SKUs on purchase orders shipping in a selected range of dates.
Order Dates: Select only SKUs on purchase orders in a selected range of order dates.
Cancel Dates: Select only SKUs on purchase orders in a selected range of cancel dates.

                   SSAALLEESSPPEEOOPPLLEE

Enter Salespeople

Note: If the Time Clock is not turned on in RICS you will not see the Time Clock Options for salespeople.

Salesperson # - can be up to 4 characters (numbers and/or characters). This will be the # they will enter to
make a sale.

Name - the employee's name

Other Information - used to store a person's title, social security number, phone number, etc.

Commission % - based on sales or gross profit (If commissions are not paid you can leave this blank).

Time Clock Overview

The Time Clock System has several separate areas that you work with after the Time Clock has been turned
on. To Turn Time Clock On

Passwords - created in Enter Salespeople.
Log In or Log Out - entered in the Time Clock.
Time Clock Administration - Allows adjustments to Time Clock Data.
Print Time Clock Data - Prints a report on Time Clock Data.
Clear Saved Time Clock Data - Clears the Saved Time Clock Data.

If using the time clock option you will not be able to enter hours in the Enter Hours/Percs option, but you can
enter salesperson time adjustments in the Time Clock Administration. All employees and Passwords must be
created, and changes made at the main computer, and the information must be transferred to the POS
computer before they can take effect (unless you are using a Network). If using the time clock option in
RICS a Password is required for the employees in Enter Salespeople.

Salesperson hours will print at the end of Salesperson Summary at the POS, and also at the end of the Sales
Journal at the main computer. Salespeople cannot be clocked in for more than 24 continuous hours at a time.

When closing a batch of sales, coping sales to disk, or waiting for a call, the user will be notified if there are
salespeople still on the Time Clock. If the salesperson is not clocked out first they WILL NOT BE CREDITED
for their hours at the main computer, and a message like the below will appear. Simply clock out the
employees and then continue.

                                                                                         106
Passwords

In addition to the normal Enter Salesperson information you must enter Time Clock Options and Passwords
which will appear when the Time Clock option is turned on.
Password - any combination of numbers and/or letters up to 12 characters. If you do not want a
salesperson to be able to clock in/out on their own DO NOT GIVE THEM A PASSWORD, (leave
password blank). A password can be changed for an existing ID.
After entering a password for an employee the following two options may be checked:
This salesperson is allowed to be a time clock administrator ­ when checked, a time clock administrator
can make adjustments to existing hours.
This salesperson may access time clock functions only for themselves - when left unchecked, this
person can clock anyone in/out.
The four combinations of how these boxes are checked and their functions are explained below.

When checked as above, this person is allowed to clock ANY/EVERYONE in/out, and to make adjustments
for ANY/EVERYONE.
This would be the setup for owners, supervisors or office managers.

When checked as above this person is allowed to clock ANY/EVERYONE in/out, but is NOT ALLOWED to
make any adjustments.
This would be the setup for store managers, assistant managers, or key employees.

When checked as above this person is allowed to clock only THEMSELVES in/out, and is NOT ALLOWED to
make any adjustments. This would be the normal setup for most employees.

                                                                                         107
When checked as above this person is allowed to clock only THEMSELVES in/out, and to make adjustments
for only THEM.
This would be a seldom used setup.

Log In ­ to clock in the time clock, simply enter the
Salesperson Login - Enter a Salesperson #.
Password - Enter the password for this Salesperson. You must have a Password setup in Salesperson to
Login.
Salesperson - Enter the Salesperson to login.
Time In - The login time will default to the current time.
Non-Sales Hours - Check on for Non-Sales Hours.
Store - (Multiple Stores Only) - Enter the store #.
[Save] - Save the information.
Log Out in the time clock, simply enter the
Salesperson Login - Enter a Salesperson #
Password - Enter the password for this Salesperson.(You must have a Password setup in Salesperson to
Login)
Salesperson - Enter the Salesperson to logout, it will then show you the clocked in time.
Time Out - The logout time will default to the current time, and show the elapsed time.
Non-Sales Hours - Check on for Non-Sales Hours.
Store - (Multiple Stores Only) - Enter the store #.
[Save] - Save the information.

                                                                                         108
Turn Time Clock On

To turn on the time clock function in RICS you must first change the RICS.CFG by going to Utilities2 and the
Option
Change RICS.CFG at both the Main Computer and at all Point of Sale Computers.

In the Change RICS.CFG screen enter the following information:
Section: TimeClock (No space between Time and Clock)
Item: Enabled
Entry: Y (Change the N to a Y)
Then Save the information.
You can also require a Cashier to be on the Time Clock before entering sales by also entering the following
information.
Section: TimeClock (No space between Time and Clock)
Item: ReqCashier
Entry: Y (Change the N to a Y)
Then Save the information.
Note: After making the changes in RICS.cfg you must first Exit RICS and then re-enter RICS for these
changes to take effect.

Time clock administrator

The time clock administrator is allowed to make adjustments to existing (unposted) time clock records until
the sales records are posted. Once the records are posted you can not change the record, but you can make
adjustments or reverse hours an employee's hours.

                                                                                         109
Print Time Clock Data

When printing this report, select the data you want to review.

Print salesperson detail - unchecked shows totals and totals the hours.

Print salesperson detail - checked shows every clock in/out and totals the hours.

To calculate the percentage of hours into minutes in the Total Hours column on this report take the percent
number X 60. Example: 70% x 60 = 42 minutes

Enter Commission Overrides

          Change a salesperson's commission depending on the department's merchandise sold

This job allows a different commission rate for any combination of salesperson/RICS department. If no
override is specified, the rate from Enter Salespeople screen will be used.
Salesperson # - a valid RICS salesperson ID

Enter Hours/Perks

                                        Enter the hours worked or extra Perks earned
Enter hours worked and perks (PMs, multies, spiffs) which appear on the Employee Analysis Report. The
hours worked are used to calculate sales per hour and profit per hour on the Employee Analysis report. If you
do not need this report, you do not need to enter any hours or perks.
This screen also shows the total Hours and Perks for PTD, MTD, STD, and YTD.

Salesperson Analysis Report

                                              Measure productivity of sales people
Measure the productivity compared to other sales people and to store averages. Whether you pay
commissions or not, these reports generate the information to reward excellent performance or critique poor
performance, and provide guidelines on areas to improve selling behavior.
The report prints employee performance showing sales, profit, commission, perks, hours and sales per hour
for the current pay period, month, season and year. It also prints total number of tickets, number of tickets
with more than one item sold, average sale amount, average number of items per ticket, and percentage of
tickets with more than one item.
The PTD column on this report stands for period-to-date. A period can be whatever you use for a pay period:
weekly, bi-weekly, semi-monthly, etc.

            CCLLOOSSEE//CCLLEEAARR

- Overview

Use these options to clear amounts from your data files for specific time periods,
          (i.e., period, week, month, season and year) or to clear certain files

IMPORTANT: RUN ALL REPORTS BEFORE CLOSING. You must close the selected period AFTER running
all the desired reports for a period and BEFORE entering new data from the next period.

Close Week

                                               Clears out weekly sales information
IMPORTANT: RUN ALL WEEKLY REPORTS BEFORE CLOSING. This option is used to clear weekly sales
information. A week can be any user defined time frame. For example, your week can go from Monday thru
Sunday, Sunday thru Saturday, or you may choose to close your week every other week. In the last scenario,
weekly sales would then become bi-weekly sales. Many users will close the week every Monday, after posting
sales for the week end.

Weekly Reports
There are two reports available to you for viewing weekly sales and performance. Those reports are the Sales
Analysis, and Best Sellers reports. For more information, see Sales Reports.

Eight Week Trending
If you are going to use the eight week trending feature, you will need to close your week out every week. See
Eight Week Trending.

You need to make a backup of your data before running this option.

You may choose to close only selected stores.

If you are not interested in weekly sales figures it is not necessary to clear the sales each week. However,
you should clear them at the end of the month so that quantities do not become too large.

Close Month/Season/Year

                                      Clears month, season, or year sales information

Before using this option:
Make sure all sales are printed and posted for the month you have just finished. Run any necessary month
end reports. Once you have closed out your month you will not be able to re-run monthly reports.

You need to make a backup of your data before running this option.

You may choose to close only selected stores.

If you are not interested in weekly sales figures it is not necessary to clear the sales each week. However,
you should clear them at the end of the month so the quantities do not become too large.

You must use this option at the end of each month to close out the month you have just completed. RICS will
not allow sales for the next month to be posted until you run this option. The screen will indicate which month
you are closing.

IMPORTANT: DO NOT forget to backup. It is recommended to use different diskettes for labeled each
month and save them. This provides additional security, and provides the ability to re-run this month's reports
at a later time if needed.

            113
Report Suggestions
There are no right or wrong reports to run at the end of the month. Whatever information is important to you
will determine the reports you should run. Some suggestions are:

     Sales Analysis - Analysis by category and category summary
     Sales Analysis - Analysis by vendor and vendor summary
     Best Sellers - Top SKUs in each category
     General Ledger Summary
     Purchase Order Reports - Looking at all past due POs
     Salesperson Analysis Report - Review monthly salesperson performance
     Recommended Transfer Report - Balance inventory between stores
     Transfer Summary Report - Totals the amount of transfers between stores
Close Season/Year - This is done automatically when you close the month setup as the End of Year month
in Company Setup.

Clear Saved Sales Transactions

                                      Removes information for Posted/Saved Sales
Each time you post sales the system takes that current batch of sales and adds them to a cumulative saved sales
file. These sales are then used to print selected reports from the Sales menu. When running reports such as Print
Sales by Time, Print Salesperson Summary, and Print Sales by SKU you may choose to print from current sales
(unposted sales) or posted sales. This allows you to run analysis of sales by time, salesperson, or SKU for a
selected date range from those older posted sales.
You will want to clear or delete those saved sales once these reports are no longer needed for that time period. If
you never need to print these reports for sales older than three months ago, each month you should run this
option to clear sales prior to a date of three months ago. Keeping this file smaller will reduce your data backup
time and allow the reports to print quicker.
The option to Save Posted Sales is in Company Setup.

Clear Saved Time Clock Data

Each time you post sales the system takes that current batch of Time Clock information and adds them to a
cumulative Time Clock file. This screen shows how many time clock records are in the file. You will want to clear
or delete those older saved time clock data files once this data is no longer needed for that time period. For
example, if you will never need or review the Time Clock Data older than three months ago, each month you
should run this option to clear all records dated before with a prior date of three months ago.

                                                                                         114
Clear Deleted Record Keys

                                                Clears Deleted records for the POS
This option is only for stores that do communications over the phone.
As records are deleted on the main computer (SKUs, salespeople, customers, etc.) a separate file stores the
deleted records. Those deleted records will be transmitted to the Point-of-Sale during communications and
then the same records are deleted at the Point-of-Sale computer. Because occasionally communications are
not successful, those deleted records are kept in this file so they could be transmitted again. At least once a
month, after communications are successful, this file should be cleared.

Automatically Delete SKUs

                                  Deletes SKUs automatically based on selected criteria.
This option prints and/or automatically deletes all SKUs with NO on hand quantity, NO on order quantity,
are NOT on any purchase order, has NO YTD sales and NO sales for the prior year.
Don't delete any SKU that has been modified on or after _______ (date).
This allows you to keep new SKUs entered on or after a given date, but because they have no on-hand, on-
order, or any sales history, they would have been deleted.
Include only selected - allows you to pick and choose limited auto delete selection of SKUs based on certain
SKUs, Vendors, Categories, Seasons, Size Types, or Groups that you choose.
Selected Stores - Normally leave stores blank to select all stores, and the system will delete all history and
SKU information when there is no remaining information or history for all stores combined. If you enter a
selected store or stores, the system will only delete the history from those selected stores and will not delete
the SKU information.
Note: It's a good idea to run this program after closing out a year.

                                                                                         115
Clear Saved Inventory Changes

                                                  Clear Saved Inventory Changes

Each time you change your inventory quantities by receiving, returning, transferring or updating via physical
inventory, the system saves those changes and adds them to a to a cumulative Inventory Change file for
review in Inventory Inquiry. This screen shows how may inventory change records are on file. You will want to
clear or delete thee saved inventory change records once the data is no longer needed for review by entering
the date of those inventory changes you wish to purge from the system.

Clear Gift Certificate Data

As customers fully redeem the gift certificates you may want to clear or delete these gift certificate records
once the data is no longer needed for review by entering the date you wish to purge the fully redeemed gift
certificates with no activity from the system.

Enter Mailing List

                                                     Enter customer information
Account # - any combination of 15 characters or numbers. The phone number (5152708182), or the
customer's name (JOHNSONMAR), could be used as an account number. Using the Phone number is
strongly recommended. DO NOT use parenthesis or dashes when entering the phone number.

Name - could be entered one of two ways: First name, then last name (i.e. MARY JOHNSON), or last name,
first name (i.e. JOHNSON, MARY). It is recommended that you do last name first. You could then print your
mail list in alphabetical order, and it will make it easier to do a customer lookup. Printing a mail list on labels
flips names separated with a comma (i.e. JOHNSON, MARY prints as MARY JOHNSON). This can be up to
35 characters.

Customer Lookup - the lookup can be done by account #, name, or in the name field type in the last name or
the first few letters of the last name, and press [Enter]. The name with the first occurrence of the letters typed
in will then be displayed. See Look Up for more information.

Optional Fields - These optional Extra Mail List Fields (up to 6) would appear if setup in Mail List Setup.

Credit Limit - assigned to each customer at the main computer only.

Current Balance - maintained whenever a house charge or payment is made when entering sales. This
cannot be changed at the POS.

Store Credit Balance - shows the balance of outstanding Store Credits.

Frequent Buyer Information - displayed if you are using the frequent buyer plan. None of that information
can be changed at the POS. For more information, see Frequent Buyer Plan.

Comments - can be added for each customer.

CUSTOMER ALERT: Users can code a customer with an 'ALERT' flag in their comments so that the entire
comment is displayed on the sales screen before a sale can be entered for that customer. Sales people can
then be automatically alerted to problem customers, such as one who writes bad checks, or one who returns
a lot of merchandise, etc.
To set up an ALERT: At the beginning of the 1st comment line, type [ALERT], all in capital letters, then your
comments.

[Clear] - clears the screen
[Delete] - deletes all information for the displayed customer
[Copy] - copies the screen
[Next] - displays the next name
[Prev] - displays the previous name
[Detail] - displays customer purchases for the displayed name (See Mail Detail)
[Label] - saves the mailing label information for the customer (See Print Stored Address Labels )
[Family] - displays the family member screen, and allows you to enter information, and track sales for all
family members under one account number. You can also view Mail Detail for each member.

For more information on Mail List Ideas see Marketing Tools.

Mail Detail - Look At

     · Wide report (1 line per customer) - prints most customer information on a single line
     · Narrow report (2 columns) - prints names and address on 8˝" X 11" paper in two columns

          Asks Print detail from ___ to ___ for a range of dates.
     · Mail Labels - prints names and addresses on the label printer.
     · Export comma-delimited file - does not print anything. Generates a comma separated data file

Account Criteria -

                                                                                         119
Select specific choices, ranges or combinations for Account, Zip Code, State, Name, and any optional
      fields (Setup #1-6) you have setup.

Sales Criteria -

You have options for Added to computer from __ to __, Date of last purchase from __ to __, Period-to-
      Date Sales, Year-to-Date Sales, and Total-to-Date Sales. They can be specific, ranges or
      combinations. If using the Frequent Buyer Plan you have the option for Frequent Buyer Plan, Frequent
      Buyer Quantity, and Frequent Buyer Dollars. These apply only if you are if you are saving detail
      information.

Detail Criteria -

You have options for Made a purchase from __ to __, Store, Salesperson, SKU, 'Column', 'Row',
      Category, Vendor, Return Code, Selected Detail Sales. They can be specific, ranges or combinations.

File List Criteria -

                                                                                         120
This screen gives you the option to restrict your output to accounts that either are in selected files or are not in
selected files by entering the filename to include/exclude names from. The files must be comma-delimited
with the RICS account number as the first field, like the export comma-delimited file option that this report
makes. You must include the full path in the file name fields. If files are entered in the 'Include' section, only
accounts that are in the specified files are considered for the report (Note: the accounts must still match any
other criteria you specify). If files are entered in the 'Exclude' section, accounts that are in the specified files
will never be considered for the report.

The File List Criteria is a powerful tool when creating comma-delimited export files in the RICS system. For
example, consider a user with 2 stores that need 3 sets of mailings as follows:

       1) A mailing to customers who only have made purchases in store #1
       2) A mailing to customers who only have made purchases in store #2
       3) A mailing to customer who have made purchases in both stores.

To accomplish this task, first create 2 comma-delimited export files:
      File STORE1 - selecting any customer having made a purchase in store #1
      File STORE2 - selecting any customer having made a purchase in store #2

Next, create a comma-delimited file containing all customers in file STORE1 but not in file STORE2.
      File ONLYSTORE1 - including file STORE1, excluding file STORE2 in the file list criteria with no other
      criteria selections. These are the customers who have only made purchases in store 1.

Now, create the labels:
To create the labels for customers who only have made purchases in store #1, simply include file
ONLYSTORE1 with no other file list criteria.
To create the labels for customers who only have made purchases in store #2, include file STORE2 and
exclude file STORE1.
To create the labels for customers who have only made purchases in both stores, include file STORE1 and
exclude file ONLYSTORE1.

Misc. Options -

You have options for All selected accounts (Default Selection), All selected accounts that have an e-mail
      address on file, All selected accounts that do NOT have an e-mail address on file.

Another Miscellaneous Option is to limit the report to customers that have an ALERT in their comment field.

[Clear Selections] key clears all selections on all six-option screens.

Export Options

When Export comma delimited file is selected on the Report Options tab, the Export tab shows export options
when clicked on. Here the user enters the filename of the Mail List and chooses additional options to export
including email addresses, user-defined fields, and customer sales totals.
If the Export Customer Purchase Detail option is checked, a separate Mail Detail export file is created
with the option of exporting only selected detail from the Detail Criteria tab.

There are six screens you use to define the customer analysis.
To analyze all customers, click on the [Clear Selections] button, select the Report Options you wish to

Report Options ­

This screen determines how RICS will analyze the selected customers. You may group your customers in 6
ways. If you are analyzing by Zip Code, you are prompted to tell RICS how many characters of the zip code
must match to be grouped together. You may also restrict the analysis to mail detail (purchases) in a specified
date range. For example, by restricting the detail to the current year, you tell how much of your current
business is due to new customers by analyzing by Year/Added.

                                                                                         128
Import Mail List Names

                                 Import Mail List Name from an outside source into RICS

This job is used to import mail list names from an outside source into your RICS mail list. These names could
come from a purchased mail list, an internet site, or even your own mail list exported and sent to be CASS
certified for bulk mailing. The file must either be in a comma delimited format or a DBase format(DBF file). It is
important that you have a current backup of your data before importing mail list names as all the
changes to the mail list data will be permanent.
The General Tab requires the following information:

     File Name - The file must be in the RICS data directory. Please note that the extension is in a separate
          field.

     Account Number Location - The account number may be a field in the import file, or RCS will create an
          account number form the Phone Number or Name (not recommended)

     Account Name Location - RICS stores the customer names in the format Last,First. In order to keep this
          format, RICS needs to know the format of the name in the import file. If the first and last names are
          separated in the import file, select the indicated option and RICS will format the name automatically. If
          the Name is in 1 field in the file, RICS needs to know whether to leave the name as is 'Use the Name
          directly from the file', or to determine the last name (and suffixes) by its location in the import file
          names.

                                                                                         129
     File Format - If the file is a flat file (not comma delimited, the fields are in fixed locations in each record)
          with a fixed length(each record is not separater by a CR/LF carriage return / line field), RICS will need
          to know how long each record is. A DBF file is considered a fixed length flat file.

     Overwrite existing mail list acounts - When checked , this will allow RICS to overwrite the information
          for mail list accounts already on file. If unchecked, RICS will not overwrite any accounts that are
          already on file.

     Have you made a backup of your data? - Please make sure you have backed up your RICS data
          before running this job.

The Fields Tab is where you will enter the location of each field. If the import file is comma demited, RICS
needs to now which position in each import record to obtain the desired field. If the import file is a flat file,
RICS needs to know the starting position and length of each field. When the job is run, RICS will validate
each record and provide an audit trail of all exceptions.

Print Stored Address Labels

                                                    Prints Saved Address Labels
This prints the stored address labels, which can be for Customers, Stores, or Vendors. This option also tells
you how many labels are stored before printing them. You may print up to 99 copies of each label by entering
Number of labels to print per address. You must have the Mailing Label setup in Printer Setup before
running this option.

Gift Certificate Maintenance

Gift certificates are created in RICS 2 different ways. The first is enter and post a new gift certificate sale. The
second allows you to enter previously sold gift certificates in the maintenance screen.

Gift Certificate ID - identifies the gift certificate. If this is a number, the gift certificates are auto-numbered
when created. If not it has to be assigned at the time of purchase.
Sequence - allows multiple Gift Certificate IDs to be used and still be unique.
Account - the account of the customer that purchased the gift certificate.
Amount - the original amount of the gift certificate

                                                                                         131
Redeemed - the purchased amount the user has applied towards this gift certificate
Balance - the remaining balance of the gift certificate
The Purchase Info tab has the following additional information for the gift certificate:

     For Account - the Account # of the customer that the gift certificate was purchased for
     Store - the store # the gift certificate was purchased at
     Ticket - the ticket # the gift certificate was purchased on
     Date - the date the gift certificate was purchased

The Redeemed Info tab has a grid showing the store, ticket, date, account, and redeemed amount when the
gift certificate was tendered.
Adding Redeemed Info
To add a new redeemed line, click [New] or press [ALT] + [N] button. Enter the tender information when the
gift certificate was used including the store #, Ticket #, Date, Account # using the gift certificate, and the
amount tendered.
Editing Redeemed Info
To edit an existing line, click [Edit] button next to that line. Make the necessary changes and click [Save] or
press [ALT] + [S].
[Clear] - Clears the gift certificate screen
[Save] - Saves the gift certificate and redeemed information
[Save and End] - Saves the gift certificate and redeemed information and clears the screen
[Delete Gift Cert] - Deletes the selected gift certificate and all redeemed information
[Exit] - Closes the Gift Certificate Maintenance screen

the gift certificate file.

Check Print all detail for any gift certificate selected checkbox to print all detail lines for each gift
certificate that meets the criteria of the report.

outstanding balance remaining.

Quote Setup

              Setup your quote header

Enter text that will appear at the top of each Quote and [Save].

Enter Quotes

              Enter the Quote information.

The user can enter quotations for selected customers for special pricing, which includes an effective date and
ending date. The quotes can be printed on 8 1/2" x 11" paper for internal use which includes cost, and profit
margins or they can be printed without costs to give to the customer. Quotes can be changed from an inactive
status to active at any time. Multiple different quotes can be on file, even though only one quote can be active
per customer. Quotes can be merged together into one quote. Once a quote is active, those special prices for
the SKUs on the quote for that Account# will be automatically used on the sales screen when entering sales
on both the main computer and the POS computer for that Account#.

Account # - a quote must have an Account number. When you enter an account number, displayed below
the name and address will be any existing Quotes, and the Active Quote for this account #.
Quote # - Quote # can be from 1 - 99.
Effective Date - Enter the date the Quote prices are to take effect.
Ending Date - Enter the date the Quote prices are no loner to be in effect.
Active - Check on if this will be the Active Quote, only one quote can be active per customer.

Comments to print at bottom of the quote simply type in text you want to print.

SKU - A quote can have as many SKUs as necessary. An SKU must be set up before you can enter it in a
quote, if an SKU is not yet set up simply click [Add] in the SKU Lookup. After an SKU number is entered, the
description and style/color are displayed from the inventory screen. The Retail Price, Markdown Price and
Current Cost and G.P. %'s are also displayed.

When looking at an existing Quote, click or press [Ctrl] + [Q] to view all the SKUs on this Quote.

Quote at - this is the Quoted price. Gross profit percents (G.P. %) are also displayed.

To save a quote, after the SKU and Quote are entered, click [Save] or press [Alt] + [S] to save this
information. The SKU clears and the cursor will go back to SKU. You can then enter another SKU and its
quantities. You would click [Save] after each SKU and its quantities are entered.

Click [Save & Print] or press [Alt] + [A] after the last SKU is entered for that Quote. The Quote prints and
clears the screen allowing you to enter another Quote.

Click [Merge] or press [Alt] + [M] to merge this quote with an existing quote.

To print quotes in the system, your options would be:
Accounts - Selected, range or all account #'s.
Effective from __ to __ - Enter the date range the Quote prices are to take effect.
Ending from __ to __ - Enter the date range the Quote prices are no loner to be in effect.
