            PPHHYYSSIICCAALL IINNVVEENNTTOORRYY

- Overview

There are two ways to do an inventory: 1) physically enter your counts, 2) scanning the inventory with a
Portable Reader. Use these options to assist you in taking an inventory, entering the counts, reconciling
counts, running reports and updating the inventory.

IMPORTANT: The inventory quantity on hand is only changed or updated when you select Update
Inventory and then run it, it does not change when entering the counts. Therefore, do not enter other
information, such as sales, receipts, or transfers that occur after the physical inventory, until you
complete Update Inventory.

Before doing an inventory: Check to make sure you have done the following items before doing your
inventory:

     · Enter all receipts, vendor returns and transfers in RICS.
     · Printed and posted all sales.
     · Know where your entire inventory is, clean up stock rooms, hold shelves.
     · Have a plan on how you'll count/scan your inventory.

          Example: Count all shelves starting from bottom to top and from left to right, or by vendor.

To do a physical Inventory: Make sure you have completed the above items and then do a physical
inventory the normal routine would be as follows in order.

     1. Print Worksheets to record your counts on
     2. Count your inventory.
     3. Enter Physical Counts will enter counts to inventory count file.
     4. Print Items Not Counted Report, review report and make corrections.
     5. Print Variance Report, review report and make corrections.
     6. Backup Data
     7. Update Inventory replaces old on hand counts with new inventory counts.

To do an Inventory using a Portable Reader:

     1. Scan the inventory into your Portable Reader.
     2. Get Data from Portable Reader gets counts into the computer.
     3. Post Data from Portable Reader posts counts to inventory count file.
     4. Print Items Not Counted Report, review report and make corrections.
     5. Print Variance Report, review report and make corrections.
     6. Backup Data
     7. Update Inventory replaces old on hand counts with new inventory counts.

            136
Print Worksheets

                                 Prints an Inventory Worksheet to record your counts on
This report is optional. It prints out a form to record your counts when manually taking a physical inventory.

You can print all SKUs or only SKUs used in a particular store (SKUs that have activity, such as sales history
or on-order for that store). This report is printed in order by vendor or by category, to make it easier to locate
your inventory. This report may also be printed for specific vendors, categories, or SKUs, seasons or groups.

NEW STORES: To print a worksheet to assist you in entering your beginning inventory, you must print all
SKUs because no activity has occurred for any SKU (Enter your beginning counts using Enter Manual
Receipts). The next time you do a physical inventory, you would probably want to print only the SKUs for a
store.

Enter Physical Counts

                     To enter either physical counts or make adjustments to an original count

New Users: DO NOT USE THIS OPTION to enter inventory counts for the first time. Instead, use the option
Enter Manual Receipts.

Entering Physical Counts - Enter in the exact on-hand quantity for the counted SKU, then
save them. Only SKUs that have quantities entered will be updated. When you save a count it is ADDED to
the existing count for that SKU (if there is one), it DOES NOT overwrite the existing count, so if you have the
SKU in three different locations in your store, you could enter your 1st location count (5), save it, enter your
2nd location count (7), save it, and enter your 3rd location count (3) and save it, your count for this SKU would
then be the total of the 3 counts added together (5+7+3=15).

The  button automatically places your on hand quantities in the count grid for the selected SKU

and store that is entered. If you already have counts entered for an SKU for the store you are entering you will

not be able to use this.

The  button places the quantities you have already entered in the count grid for the selected

SKU and store that is entered. This is a simple way to check any item when you have a question about what

was already entered, or want to review your counts for an SKU.

Revising Counts: For counts previously entered (Using either this option or using a portable reader), but not
yet updated, you should enter a positive or a negative adjustment. For example, you entered a count of 5 for
an SKU/Size. You realize later it should be 4. You should enter a -1 to reduce the count by one. DO NOT
enter adjustments for SKUs that do not have any physical counts entered.

Zeroing Counts: AN SKU should be zeroed out if there is "0" on-hand quantities (i.e. any size of any width).
Print Items Not Counted Report lists SKUs that possibly need a zero quantity entered. Enter a zero count in
any column of any row to zero out the SKU.

Physical Inventory with a PC: RICS has the ability to have physical inventory counts scanned directly into a
computer. A decoder and scanning device would need to be connected to the computer. To start scanning,

enter the store number and press  a line will then appear that says Bar codes you can then start
scanning the bar codes.

Remember, entering physical counts does not update your inventory. To update your inventory, you must run
Update Inventory.

                                  137
Get Data from Portable Reader

                           Transfers the data from your portable reader into your computer
For more information see Portable Bar Code Reader. (on page 18)
Connect the cable from your portable reader to the selected com port on the back of your computer, press the

                button. After getting data from the portable reader, RICS will then display the Post Data from
Portable Reader screen.
You must first post data from portable reader before running this option again.

Post Data from Portable Reader

                Use this option to post inventory from the PT2000 as physical inventory counts,
                                           transfers, manual receipts, or PO receipts

 Please make sure you have a current backup of your data before proceeding with any posting option

Posting physical inventory counts:
Click on Post which: Physical Inventory Counts and then run. Physical Counts are then be posted for the
store# that was entered in the portable reader.
NOTE: Your counts are not posted directly to the inventory files; those files will be updated when you select
Update Inventory
Any "exceptions" report from your scanned inventory print out when you run this option (i.e. invalid SKU,
ROW/COL, or UPC). This report lists the previous valid SKU and the next valid SKU. This information is
useful to locate where on the floor or stock room that item is located. Once you locate the item, you need to
enter it into inventory using Enter Physical Counts.

                                                                                         138
Posting transfers:
Before scanning the inventory to transfer, it is necessary to enter the store number on the PT2000 as "00",
otherwise the inventory will not be transferred.

Click on Post which: Transfers and new lines appear for the From store and To store. Enter the From store
#, which is the store the inventory is being transferred from, and the To store#, which is the store the
inventory is being transferred to. A report is created listing which items and sizes were transferred, with totals,
when this option is run.

Posting manual receipts:
Before scanning manual receipts, it is necessary to enter the store number on the PT2000 as "00" otherwise
the counts will be "rejected" as receipts.

Click on Post which: Manual receipts, a new line appears for the Store #. A report prints listing which items
were received, with totals, when this option is run.

Posting PO receipts:
Before scanning PO receipts, it is necessary to enter the store number on the PT2000 as "00" otherwise the
counts will be "rejected" as receipts.

Click on Post which: PO receipts. Using this option lowers your on-order quantities. The inventory is
received at the "current" cost that is on your inventory screen.

When entering or scanning PO receipts into the portable reader, enter the PO number being received in the
SKU field. Then enter REC for column and PO for the row. The following entries will be posted as received for
that PO number. If you wish to enter receipts for another PO, again enter the new PO number as SKU, and
REC and PO for column and row.

A report is printed listing which items were received, with totals, when this option is run.

Posting manual returns:
Before scanning manual returns, it is necessary to enter the store number on the PT2000 as "00" otherwise
the counts will be "rejected" as returns.

Click on Post which: Manual returns, a new line appears for the Store #. A report prints listing which items
were returned, with totals, when this option is run.

Print Items Not Counted Report

                         Lists all SKUs that do not have a physical inventory count entered

Why is this Report Important?
This is important because if a SKU does not have any counts entered, its inventory will be unaffected when
you Update Inventory. That means your inventory could be over or under-stated, unless you "zero out" those
SKUs.

You may select ranges of items in which the report should print. If you are doing an entire inventory, leave
these fields blank. You may also select whether or not you want SKUs that have zero on-hand to print on the
report. Items on this report that have a non-zero quantity need to have a zero physical count entered.

To zero out a SKU: use the option Enter Physical Counts. Type in the appropriate store number and SKU,
enter a zero count in any Column (size) of any Row (width) and save.

                                                                                         139
Print Variance Report

                                     Compares inventory counts to on-hand quantities
This report prints the counts that have been entered and compares them to what the computer has for the
actual inventory on-hand by units and cost. It is used to determine if any errors have been made when
entering the counts and also what your inventory variance is in total units and total dollars.
Click on Print only varying items to only print the SKUs where there is a discrepancy between the count and
the actual on hand quantity, otherwise all SKUs will print and this maybe a lengthy report.
Review this report, if corrections are needed, use Enter Physical Counts enter the appropriate quantities, and
rerun this report. If you do not enter counts at all for any SKU it will NOT print on this report, instead it would
print on the Items Not Counted report.
Important: If you take an inventory for one vendor, or one category, do not enter that vendor or category on
the Variance Report selection screen. The system prints those SKUs that you entered a count for. Otherwise,
if you accidentally entered or scanned a count for an SKU outside that vendor or category, the system would
update that SKU with a quantity of one and you would never know it.

Update Inventory

                                    Replaces on hand quantities with inventory counts
This option is used after you have entered the physical counts and determined from the various reports that
the counts are correct. After updating the items counted, it changes what was previously on hand and replace
it with the new quantity counted, and items that were zeroed out then have an on hand quantity of "0".
Important: Be sure you have done the following items:

     · Print Items Not Counted Report.
     · Entered a zero count for any items on that report.
     · Print Variance Report, and review it.
     · Back up your data.
Before updating your inventory, you are required to click on each item in Have You? to make sure this has
been done before you be allowed to update your inventory.

                                                                                         140
            FFIILLEE SSEETTUUPP

Stores - File Setup, Taxes

    Setup or change basic information about the Stores, Taxes and Tender Types in your company.
Store Number: The store number can be any number from 1 to 999. You are limited to the number of POS
locations you have purchased for your system. See Technical Support for more information.

Store Name: This internal name is displayed on various screens and printed on reports.

Mail Name: This name is printed on POs. It is usually a corporate name.

The next four folders need be clicked on to fill in the entries.

Taxes

Taxes must be setup for each store. Up to 3 taxes can be entered per store.
Sales Tax: Enter the Description of the tax and the Tax Rate. The description can be up to 10 characters in
length of numbers, letters, or combination of the two (Example: State 5.00).

Select how your sales tax is computed: The three choices are:
     Round to the nearest cent (#1 is normally used)
     Always round up
     Always round down

                                                                                         141
The general tax rate of most items should be entered on the store screen.
If some items have a different tax rate, see Sales Tax Override.
NOTE: A DESCRIPTION MUST BE ENTERED. You cannot enter a tax rate without a description first.

Tender Types, General, Bill-To Address

                                 Tender types are used to identify how a sale is paid for.

Description: Enter the description of the tender type. The description can be up to 10 characters in length of
numbers, letters, or combination of the two.

Cash: Tender types that are checked are "considered cash" and determine the cash balance of the cash
drawer. Typically these tender types should be Cash, Check, or any credit cards that are accepted and
deposited directly into your bank account. Uncheck the tender types are NOT used to compute the cash
balance of the cash drawer. Tender types Not Used are not displayed on the sales screen
Open Drawer: When checked opens the cash drawer when this tender type is entered.

NOTE: After changing tender types, the store file must be transferred to the POS, and the current batch of
sales must be closed before the changes will take effect.

General

         Is for basic information

Last Ticket Used is the default last ticket used to start a sales batch. This is used when RICS cannot
determine the last ticket number for a user entering sales for a store.

Phone Number and Fax Number are used to print on RICS Purchase Orders.

'Other Charge Description' supplies a different description on sales receipts for the 'Other Charges' field.
For example, a store dedicated to mail order or catalog sales may want to change the 'Other Charge'
description to 'Shipping'. Each register may also have its own unique 'Other Charge' description by entering it
in the local machines private RICS.CFG file in Section Sales Screen, Item OthChgDesc.

Email Address is used to print on various reports.

Bill-To Address

The following fields are basic Bill -To Information: Name, Address, City, State, and Zip Code for each store.

[Bill-To Label] - Saves the label information, to print the label run Mail List/ Print Stored Address Labels.

[Label] - Will save the label information, to print the label run Mail List/ Print Stored Address Labels.

                                                    142
143
Sectors

         A sector is a group of departments

A lot of thought should go into deciding which departments should be grouped with each sector. Since no one
knows your store better than you do, or how simple or detailed you want your information, you are the best
judge of what your Sectors should be, since there are no set sectors. It would be a good idea to number
sectors by using the first department. For example, sector 10 begins with department 10 and ends with
department 20, and sector 30 begins with department 30, and ends with 40, and so on.

Sector 10 Men's Items includes

    Department 10 Men's Shoes includes:
                         Category 110 Men's Dress
                         Category 120 Men's Casual
                         Category 130 Men's Walking
                         Category 140 Men's Dress Boots

    Department 20 Men's Clothes includes:
                         Category 210 Men's Dress
                         Category 220 Men's Casual
                         Category 230 Men's Walking
                         Category 240 Men's Dress Boots

By leaving gaps, it is easier to add new sectors later. Several reports will group information by sector, with
sector sub-totals.

Sector: can be any number 1 through 99. [Ctrl] + [P] displays a list of sectors you have already entered.

Description: can be up to 20 characters in length.

Begin department: is the first department number in the sector.
In the example above, Sector 10, Men's Items, the Starting department is 10.

End category: is the last department in the sector.
In the example above, Sector 10, Men's Items, the ending department is 20.

Departments - File Setup

                                              A department is a group of categories
A lot of thought should go into deciding which categories should be grouped with each department. Since no
one knows your store better than you do, or how simple or detailed you want your information you are the
best judge of what your Departments should be, since there are no set departments. It would be a good idea
to number departments by using the first two digits of the first category in that department. For example,
department 10 begins with category 100 and ends with category 199, and department 20 begins with
category 200, and ends with 299, and so on.

    Department 10 Men's Shoes includes:
                         Category 110 Men's Dress
                         Category 120 Men's Casual
                         Category 130 Men's Walking
                         Category 140 Men's Dress Boots

By leaving gaps, it is easier to add new departments later. Several reports will group information by

                                                                                         144
department, with department sub-totals.

Department: can be any number 1 through 99. [Ctrl] + [P] displays a list of departments you have already
entered.

Description: can be up to 20 characters in length.

Begin category: is the first category number in the department.
In the example above, Department 10, Men's Shoes, the Starting category is 110.

End category: is the last category in the department.
In the example above, Department 10, Men's Shoes, the ending category is 140.

Printing a Department List: To print a list of all or selected departments, see
Print Department File.

Categories - File Setup

                                    Categories are used to group similar SKUs together
It is not difficult to enter your categories, but a lot of thought should go into deciding what categories to use,
since they determine how the reports are printed. No one knows your store better than you do, or how simple
or detailed you want your information, so you are the best judge of what your categories should be, since
there are no set categories.
It is important to group similar categories together and not number them consecutively. By leaving gaps, it is
easier to add new categories later if the need arises. Consecutive categories make up departments. Each
SKU must be assigned to one of these categories. Many reports group information by category with category
sub-totals, and/or allow selection of categories.

Category: can be any number 1 through 999.

Description: can be up to 20 characters in length.

Printing a Category List: To print a list of all or selected categories, see Print Category File.

Changing Categories: If necessary, there is a utility available to renumber categories. For more information,
see Change Categories.

                 Categories might be setup something like this

Dept 10  Simple  Description                Dept 10      Detailed  Description
Men's    Cat #                              Men's Shoes  Cat#
Shoes    110     Men's Dress                             110       Men's Dress Tie
         120     Men's Casual                            115       Men's Dress Wingtips

         130     Men's Boots                             120       Men's Dress Slip On
                                                         125       Men's Dress Boots
                                                         150       Men's Casual Tie
                                                         155       Men's Casual Slip On
                                                         160       Men's Walking
                                                         170       Men's Work Boots
                                                         175       Men's Hiking Boots
                                                         177       Men's Rubber Boots
                                                         180       Men's Slippers

Groups - File Setup

                                                    145
 Groups are used to link SKUs together from different Categories, Vendors, or both for report options
                                                     or entering price discounts

A Group is an option to link SKUs together for reports that may be in different categories or have different
vendors (Some Examples of using groups might be all SKUs on a sale rack, all items that were bought for
promotional pricing, or SKUs with high performance that needs to be reviewed more often for possible fill-ins).
You may also use groups to take price discounts (mark down the current selling price for all SKUs within a
group).
Group Code: Can be up to 3 characters in length of numbers, letters, or combination of the two.
Description: Can be up to 20 characters in length describing the group.
Add, change, or delete an SKU in a group: Enter, change or delete the group code for the SKU on the
group line in SKU maintenance. See SKU Maintenance
Reports by Group: In all sales reports in which criteria is an option, groups will be listed as one of the
options. See Sales Reports
Price Discount by Group: An option to mark down an entire group of SKUs instead of marking down each
SKU individually (Mark down 200 SKUs in group W-White Shoes at the end of the season). See Price
Discounts
Printing a Group List: To print a list of all or selected groups.
For more information, see Print Group File.
Changing Groups: If necessary, there is a utility available to renumber groups and the SKUs in those
groups. For more information, see Change Group Codes.

                                                                                         146
Size Types

            Size types are created for different types of merchandise

A size type can be a maximum of 54 columns by 27 rows. (i.e. 54 sizes by 27 widths)
Note: DO NOT create a size type for those items that do not come in sizes.

You do need not to create a lot of different size types if you create a size type that fits all your sizes. For
example: You carry men's shoes in sizes 6 1/2 to a 15 and from a N to WW this one size type would be for all
styles that come in those sizes, even if you only carry a style from a size 9 to 11 in M widths only.

Size Type can be any number up to 3 digits. This number is then assigned to a SKU to create the sizes
associated with the SKU. [CTRL] + [P] displays a list of available size types already entered.

Description can be up to 20 characters. This description is only used to identify the size grid. Some
examples of size type numbers and descriptions are:

      100 Men's Shoes N-WW
      101 Men's Shoes A-3E
      102 Men's Athletics
      200 Women's Shoes S-WW
      201 Women's Shoes AA-EE
      800 Clothing S, M, L
      805 Clothing 3,5,7,9

Column Description can be up to 5 characters. Some examples might be: SIZE, WAIST, NECK, or
COLOR. Remember, a size type is NOT created for items without sizes.

Row Description can be up to 5 characters. Some examples might be: WIDTH, LNGTH, and COLOR. Do
not have a row description unless it is necessary. For example: Athletic shoes may only come in sizes, but
with in no widths.
Column on the size grid needs an identifying "label", up to 3 characters. For example: a size 6 would be
060, a size 6˝ would be 065, and a size 10 would be 100.

Row, when used, need an identifying "label", up to 2 characters. For example: widths of N, M, W, and WW.

                                                                                         147
NOTE: All COLumns and/or ROWs do not have to be used. DO NOT have identical COLumn and/or ROW
"labels" on the same size grid.
Changing a size grid: BE CAREFUL changing a size grid. You can add sizes (COL) at the end of a size grid,
move or add widths (ROWs) without difficulty. DO NOT add sizes (COL) to the beginning, or insert in the
middle of the grid by "moving" sizes over. If it is necessary to add sizes to the beginning, or in the middle of
the grid, see Change Size Types.
NRF Codes: NRF codes are not needed unless receiving UPC cross-reference diskettes, using EDI, or
doing Direct Sale. See NRF Codes.

NRF Codes - File Setup

                                             A 5 digit code to cross-reference sizes

The National Retail Federation has established a unique five-digit number for most every size and width. This
five-digit NRF code eliminates confusion between you and the vendor. For example: a size 7 could be 070, or
7.0, or just 7. Widths could be XW and WW. For example, a 7˝ Narrow would be NRF code 50414.
Entering NRF Codes: Enter a size type number. Click on NRF Table to display the NRF code grid. For shoe
size types, the Table Number is 5 (NOTE: The table number is the first digit of the NRF codes). Enter the
last three digits of the NRF codes in the appropriate column, if the code # begins with 50, or the last four digits
if it does not begin with 50.

Anything Else

                                152
GMAIC Format

GMAIC format is a 160-byte record followed by a carriage return/line feed. The file must contain the NRF size
code for items that have sizes. Actual file layout is listed below.
Fields required:

Position #               Description  Length

1             Qualifier               2

3             Vendor ID               10

21            UPC Number              12

33            Product ID (SKU#)       20

85            NRF Size Code           5

Vendors - File Setup

                     The Vendor you bought the SKU from. Vendor # is required for all SKUs

Vendor #: A vendor number must be assigned for each SKU. It is recommended that the vendor # be the first
4 letters of the vendor name. For example: Nike is NIKE, Rockport is ROCK.

Name: This internal name is displayed on screens and reports.

Mail Name: This name is displayed on Purchase Orders. For example: Vendor name may be Naturalizer, but
the Mail name may be Brown Shoe Company.

Fax: The fax number will print on purchase orders.

Email: The email address for the vendor.

Contact: Sales men or service rep (Not required).

Comment: Any information you want (Not required).

Terms, Ship Via: These are the default settings for the Vendor and displayed on Purchase Orders. These
can be changed on any Purchase Order.

EDI Qualifier, ID: is used to identify vendors. This field does not appear unless you use EDI, see Technical
Support.

Account #: Each store can be assigned a separate account number. For multiple stores enter the account #
for the stores listed.

[Label] - Save the label information, to print the label run Mail List/ Print Stored Address Labels.

Printing a Vendor List: To print a list of vendors, see Print Vendor Files.

Changing Vendors: If necessary, there is a utility available to rename the vendor numbers. For more
information, see Change Vendors.

                                 153
SKUs - File Setup

                                     SKUs are used to identify all merchandise in RICS

SKU#: You can use any combination of letters and/or numbers up to fifteen characters for the SKU number.
This is the number used to identify all merchandise in reports, sold, ordered, transferred, returned, and
received in RICS. You should try to use the vendor's SKU as the SKU in RICS when ever possible.

Changing a SKU Number: SKU numbers cannot be changed on this screen if it has been sold, ordered, or
received. See Discontinue SKUs.

Vendor: A vendor number must be assigned for each SKU. This is a required field.
See Vendors.

Vendor SKU: Entered if you are planning to use the vendors UPC bar codes in EDI, Vendors cross reference
diskettes, Shoe & Sport Talk, or Direct Sale, otherwise it is not a required field. If the Vendor's SKU was used

as the SKU above, press the  button, or [Alt] + [V] to duplicate the SKU# in this field. This is
not a required field.

Color Code: This field only appears when a vendor is chosen with a Qualifier ID that requires color codes.
This field is used only with EDI, S&ST, or when using vendor UPC cross-reference diskettes.

Category: A category number must be assigned for each SKU, this is a required field.
See Category.

Size Type: must be entered for SKUs that are broken down by size, color, etc. Leave blank or enter a zero for
SKUs that are not to be tracked by any sizes (quantity only).
See Size Type.

Group: (Optional) is entered if you are planning to use Group Codes. See Group.

                             154
Description: This is the name you call an item. This prints on the customers receipt, stock labels, and on
all reports that use SKU detail. The description is also one of the options to index the SKU lookup.

Style/Color: is used to identify a style or color, but not both. You should be consistent when entering this
information. Many reports options use Style/Color, along with price discounts, plus it is also one of the options
to index how the SKU is looked up. If the same style or color is entered two different ways, the summaries or
index will be different. For example: Black shoes are entered as either BLK, or BLACK, in this case all BLACK
would be listed or totaled before the BLK.

Location: is used ONLY by companies that have a central warehouse location where merchandise is
received. This location is a sort option on the Automatic Transfers report.

Comment: is used to put in any internal information about the SKU. This does not print on receipts or reports.

Current cost: is the amount you are now paying for this SKU. It is also one way to determine the current
value of your inventory, and determines your G.P. % (Gross Profit %) in the Pricing portion of SKU setup. All
SKUs should probably have a current cost of greater than 0.00. Gross Profit on reports is calculated from the
average cost, not current cost. RICS automatically calculates average cost when merchandise is received
and/or transferred. Changing the current cost does not change the Average Cost.

Season: is another way to group like SKUs together. Many reports options use Season, along with price
discounts. See Season Setup.

Keywords: another way to categorize SKUs. The difference between a keyword and group codes, seasons,
or style/colors is that one SKU can have multiple keywords. In the example above, this SKU can be included
in a report of all 'SALE0800' items, which were items put on sale in August 2000. But Cindy, the merchandiser
can also run a report showing only items she wants to keep a close eye on for reorders. She has given these
SKUs the keyword 'CINDY'. You may assign up to 60 characters of keywords for each SKU. Each keyword
must be separated by a space. If you want to add a keyword to a SKU, you may click on the lookup eyeball to
the left of the keyword, select the desired keyword, and RICS will automatically assign the keyword to the
SKU.

Coupon SKU: Checking the Coupon SKU box will cause the SKU to be defaulted to a -1 at the Enter Sales
screen when scanned or otherwise entered. It is called a coupon SKU because this option works ideally with
coupons. Checking this box allows the quick scanning of Coupons or other SKUs at a sales register.

Picture File Name: You may enter a valid file name of a picture to be associated with the SKU. The accepted
file formats are JPG, BMP, or GIF. The file must reside in the RICSPICS subdirectory under your RICS Data
Directory. If you have a file in the RICSPICS directory with same name as the SKU being added, the picture
filename is added by default. When a SKU name is entered on various RICS screens, its picture is displayed
in the corner of the monitor. To find out more about the SKU picture form, see SKU Pictures.

Pricing:

List Price (Optional) is used by discount stores. The stock labels that are printed could display "List" price,
"Our" price, or anything up to 4 characters.
Retail Price is the "regular" (normal) selling price of the item.
Markdown 1 could be a "sale" price of the item.
Markdown 2 could be an additional "sale" price of the item.

                                                                                         155
Normally RICS will calculate the G.P. % based on the current cost and prices you enter. Alternatively, you
may enter the cost and then your desired Gross Profit in the G.P. Field, press the [Calc] field and RICS will
insert the retail price that will give you the desired profit margin. You can still change the price manually to
conform with your store's pricing conventions.
What is the current selling price? The current selling price of the item is reflected in the Pricing section of

          the screen. The three options: Retail, Markdown 1, and Markdown 2 each have a selected option next
          to them under the Curr label. The option with the black circle in it is the selected current pricing
          option. In the example above, the Retail Price is the current price. To change the current price, click a
          different option.
Perks: (PMs or spiffs) entered here automatically post to the appropriate salesperson when a sale is made.
Perks may also be manually entered when sales are done or in Enter Hours/Perks. The Employee Analysis
report prints the amount of perks for each salesperson.
Label Type:

Click on the box for the type of label you want for this SKU, or select No Labels for those items that should
never have a label printed. A selection on label code is available when printing labels. See Print Stock Labels.
Oversize Pricing:

(Optional) Oversize pricing can be entered for large size of a SKU. Column (from the size type file given for
the SKU) is the size that begins the extra amount charge. The amount is added to the selling price.
(Example: $2.00 is added to the price on any sizes 10 1/2 or larger.)

When you save a SKU number, all of the information is displayed on the screen, except the SKU number,
until you override it. This is useful when you setup SKU items that are similar (i.e. 855N30 - Royal Black and
655N30 -Royal Navy), in which case you need only enter the new SKU# and the new color.

Delete all UPC codes for the selected SKU.

A SKU normally should not be deleted. The item should usually be discontinued. A SKU should only be
deleted if there is no sales history or orders for it.

SKUs ­ Picture Configuration

                             Pictures of SKUs can be configured to display on your screen

When you have assigned a picture to a SKU and bring the SKU up in many of the RICS screens, the form
above will be displayed. By selecting Options, you are able to change the way the SKU picture is displayed.

The Stretch option allows you to resize the form the picture resides on. This also stretches or shrinks the
picture to fit the new form co-ordinates. This may cause the picture to appear abnormally elongated. To avoid
this side effect, select the Retain Size Ratio. Retaining the size ration allows the picture to expand or contract
with the form without distorting the picture.

The Bottom Right, Bottom Left, Top Right, and Top Left options position the SKU picture in the selected
corner of the screen.

The Close option closes the SKU picture form and no more pictures are displayed until the option is re-
enabled in the RICS Main Menu menu bar under Miscellaneous Options, Allow SKU Pictures.

Open To Buy Plan - File Setup

                                                  Creating an Open -To - Buy Plan
This file is optional. It is used when printing the Open-To-Buy vs. Sales Report and the Open-To-Buy Report.
The option for which method you select is entered in Company Setup. There are two methods for calculating
planned sales for each store/category/month:

      Use % of total store sales and fixed monthly percentages.
      Use % change over last years sales for each category.
Use % change over last years sales for each category is the most commonly used. It is for having the
system compute planned sales using a percentage of increase or decrease from Current Year/Last Year
actual sales. The Current Year Sales are automatically entered at the Close of the Month. The following
screen would be used:

Enter the Store # and Category #.
Enter the % change from last year to this year and/or % change from this year to next year.
Enter the Planned turnover: 1st 6 months & 2nd 6 months, and Planned Gross Profit %.
[Copy] copies the current category information to the next category entered if that category has no saved
information for it.
[Copy Sales] displays a choice on screen:

This option is used if you want to duplicate this years planned sales to be exactly as the previous year actual
sales, or to duplicate this years sales to be next years sales.

                                                                                         158
[ReCalculate] automatically fills in the monthly amounts based upon the current year and next year
projections and recalculates the planned sales or recalculates the totals if you change the percent. Enter a
decrease in planned sales as a negative percent.
The "Last year sales" column does not show figures until you close your month at year-end.
Use % of total store sales and fixed monthly percentages. This option would be used for new stores that
have no history records, it allows category percents, monthly sales percentages and monthly markdown
percents to be entered, and automatically applies them to the annual total entered for each stores projected
sales. The system then calculates each months planned sales for the categories.

Enter the Store # and Category #.
Enter the % change from last year to this year and/or % change from this year to next year.
Enter the Planned turnover: 1st 6 months & 2nd 6 months, and Planned Gross Profit %.
Then enter sales % that that category will contribute to each month's sales. Perform this step for all
categories in the store.
[Copy] copies the current category information to the next category entered if that category has no saved
information for it.
[ReCalculate] automatically fills in the monthly amounts based upon the current year and next year
projections and recalculates the planned sales or recalculates the totals if you change the percent. Enter a
decrease in planned sales as a negative percent.
[Store Totals] The following screen will be displayed to enter the total store planned sales:

                                                                                         159
Enter Store # and This year's projected sales and Next year's projected sales. This should be retail
dollars, less expected markdowns.
Enter the % of Sales for each month and the Sales are automatically calculated (total must equal 100%).
Enter the % of Markdowns for each month.
[Category Totals] takes you back to the Open-To-Buy-Categories Screen.
[Apply] calculates each month's planned sales based upon the %s set up for each category. The following
message will appear:

Choose your selection by pressing the appropriate number. If the category percentages do not add up to
100%, the following message appears:

If your total does not add up to 100% you should Print Open-To-Buy File to check the totals and correct the
percentages to equal 100%. If the percentages all equal 100%, then each categories planned sales are
calculated. Now, if you return to the [Category Totals] screen, each category has planned sales for each

                                                                                         160
month.

Sales Tax Override - File Setup

                            Used for different tax rates for different types of merchandise.

This file is optional. It is used in states that have different tax rates for different types of merchandise. In the
store file enter the sales tax rate that is the most common for that store. Then, in this sales tax file, enter
each category that is taxed at a rate different from that in the store file.
Example: In some states only handbags and some accessories are taxable. Setup a -0- sales tax rate in the
store file. Then, in this tax file, enter the sales tax rate for each taxable category.
A price threshold can be set to apply the tax over or under the price threshold.
Example: If the rate is 5%, the threshold is set at $50.00, and the Only tax amount over threshold is
checked, the item is taxed at the specified rate. An item in this category that is $75.00 would be taxed $1.25
($25.00 over the $50.00 price threshold). If the Only tax amount over threshold is unchecked, then the tax
would be $2.50 (tax the first $50.00).

Case Packs - File Setup

                               Create a pre-set group of quantities for selected size types.
Case packs are a pre-set group of quantities you create for selected columns and rows. They are used in any
option that allows size entry, to speed up the entering of data. To use case packs, you would enter the case
pack number and the standard case pack quantities (entered on this screen after size type is entered) would
be automatically displayed. Make your own case packs for sizes you normally carry in your store (such as a
standard 24 pair size run). When entering information for a SKU, only case packs set with the same size type
are displayed.
Case Pack: Can be up to 6 characters in length of numbers, letters, or combination of the two.
Description: Can be up to 20 characters in length describing the case pack (i.e. 24 pair women's N-W).
Size Type: Is a required field. See Size Types.

Communications - File Setup

                                              File Setup for Store Communications

                                                                                         161
A communications file must be set up for each store and each POS/register at the location you want to
communicate with. You also have the option to set up which files you want to transfer to each location.

Store # is the store number that the modem will be calling.

Register is any letter A through Z. If you are only communicating with one POS/register at a store, set that
register to A. Each subsequent register at a store will be: B, C, etc.

Phone # is the phone number that the main computer calls to connect with the POS/register. For touch-tone
service, preface your phone number with a 'T' (e.g. T15152708182). If you have "call waiting", you can
disable call waiting by prefacing the phone number with `T*70,' (Note: make sure you include the comma
after the zero and before your phone number) (e.g. T*70,15152708182). You can call more than one
POS/register on the same phone # by setting the POS/register to answer on a different number of rings.

Note: If you are communicating with a register via the internet or a LAN connection, place the word
'INTERNET' in the phone number. If you are communicating via a direct connect cable, place the word
'DIRECT' in the phone number.

Baud is the speed of your modem. Valid choices are 1200, 2400, 9600, 14.4, 19.2, 38.4, or 57.6. DO NOT
enter a speed faster than your modem will communicate. Make sure your main and your POS computers are
set at the same baud rate to communicate.

Use CTS Flow Control for file transfers should be checked on.

RICS Version is the current RICS version on this POS register. If the POS register is not on the current RICS
version, you will not be able to send any data files to it.

Note: The entire file is not downloaded; only the changes in the file since the last communication was
done will be sent.

To Send Files:
Check the files you want to transfer to each location. All files do not need to be downloaded all the time. The
files to download each time may include:
Send SKU & Store changes sends changes to SKU #'s, store information.
Send Inventory changes sends changes to SKU's for Inventory Inquiry information.
Send Purchase Order changes sends changes to Purchase Order information.
Send Mail list changes sends changes to Mail List information.
Send Unprinted Stock Labels sends changes to print Stock Labels (Use only if the location is going to print
stock labels at that location).

Since: This will usually be the date and time of the last successful communications. Only new information
would be sent to the POS register(s). This would need to be changed if a register(s) were updated with a
diskette. The date and time would then need to be changed to when the backup was done, not the restore.

Send Pictures: When selected will send all pictures with a modification date later than the 'Changes Since'
date. When unselected, no picture file will be sent.

Send for all stores: (Send Inventory changes) When checked would download the information for all stores
to the selected store, which would give that store the ability to inquire on all other store's inventory.
Unchecked would download only the information for that store's changes.

Send inventory detail: (Send Inventory changes) When checked will send all the inventory change records
for each Store/SKU's inventory record that is sent. This will allow the store to see up-to-date inventory change
detail in the Inquiry screen.

                                                                                         162
Send for all stores: (Send Purchase Order changes) When selected would download the information for all
stores to the selected store, which would give that store the ability to inquire on all other store's purchase
orders. When unselected would download only the purchase orders that the selected store is a party to by
being the bill-to or ship-to store.

Send mail detail: (Send Mail List changes) When checked would download the mail list detail information
for all stores to the selected store, which would give that store the ability to see the mail list detail for all other
stores.

to move them over to the Functions not allowed column. To allow functions that were not allowed

select (highlight) the options in the not allowed column as above but click the  to move them back to

                                                                                         164
Keywords - File Setup

              Keywords are a flexible way to group SKUs with common characteristics together

A Keyword is used to assign characteristics to SKUs in order to run reports on SKUs with the same
characteristics (same keyword(s)). Unlike a group code, a single SKU can have many different keywords.
This will allow 1 SKU to fall into multiple keyword groups. If you were having a sale on some SKUs and
wanted to see how the sale did by running a Sale Analysis Report, and also wanted to identify some of those
same SKUs (along with other non-sale SKUs) in order to run a Stock Status Report for re-ordering purposes,
you could assign the Sale SKUs a keyword 'SALE' and the reorder items a keyword 'REORDER'. Then you
could run both the Sales Analysis and Stock Status reports to pinpoint the exact SKU's you need to track.
Keyword: 1 to 10 characters (no spaces). The shorter your keywords are, the more keywords a SKU may
have.
Description: Can be up to 20 characters in length describing the keyword.
Assign keywords to SKUs: Add, change or delete the keywords for an SKU in SKU Maintenance.
Reports by Keywords: In many reports where setting criteria is an option, you may limit the report to only
SKUs that meet assigned keyword criteria. See Sales Reports.
Printing a Keyword List: To print a list of all or selected groups.
See Print Keywords.

                                                                                         165
Return Codes - File Setup

                            Return Codes help to track why merchandise is being returned

A Return Code is used in the Sales Screen to identify the reason a customer is returning an item. You may
have up to 99 return codes. A report is generated for all returns that are checked as trackable while Posting
Sales to Inventory. This will help you to correct the inventory for damaged returns or identify other recurring
problems with your merchandise.
Return Code: A number from 1 to 99
Description: Can be up to 20 characters in length describing the return code.
Trackable: When checked, trackable returns are printed out when posting sales to Inventory.
Printing a Return Code List: To print a list of all or selected return codes, see Print Return Code File.
Returns may be summarized by code in the Sales Journal. Return Codes can be forced to be entered with
any returned merchandise on the Sales Screen. Please call CSI Support to explore these options.

                                                                                         166
Promotion Codes - File Setup

                              Promotion Codes help to track and analyze your promotions

A Promotion Code is used in the Sales Screen to identify why a customer was brought into the store. It may
be a mailer, newspaper ad, coupon, or e-mail campaign. You may have up to 99 return codes. report is
generated for all returns that are checked as trackable while Posting Sales to Inventory. This will help you to
correct the inventory for damaged returns or identify other recurring problems with your merchandise.
Code: Any 6 character code to identify the promotion. It must be something the customer will be able to
communicate to the cashier.
Description: Can be up to 20 characters in length describing the promotion
Pieces: Knowing how many mailers or e-mails were distributed will allow RICS to track a response rate.
Cost: Knowing how much the promotion cost will allow RICS to report on your profit or loss on the promotion.
Printing a Promotion Code List: To print a list of all or selected promotion codes, see Print Promotion Code
File.
The Promotion Analysis Report will print summarize the sales attributed to a promotion and compare them to
the pieces and cost of the promotion.

Copy From POS Diskette

                                            To copy information from a POS diskette

Use this option to read POS transactions, and mail list changes, also inventory changes (if doing a Main setup
at POS) from a diskette. When the copy has successfully completed, the files are erased from the
diskette.

Path: This is the path to the location where the files from the POS are located. You can enter a diskette path
(usually 'A'), a local data path, networked data path, or a CD-ROM.

[Process] or [Alt] + [P] will begin to copy the POS files from the diskette. You can repeat for more than one
sales diskette and/or stores.

After copying the sales diskettes you must Print Sales Journal and Post Sales to Inventory before the
items sold are deducted from inventory and the sales dollars and quantities will increase.

Sales Diskettes: It is recommended having a diskette for each day of the week. Label the diskettes: Sales
Disk- Monday, Sales Disk- Tuesday, Etc. Don't use these diskettes for anything but transferring sales.

Send Messages to Stores

                                 To send a message to POS Stores when communicating
This option is available on both the main computer and the POS computer. However, on a POS computer,
there is no need to specify which stores to send to, because all messages will go to the main computer.

Whenever the main computer calls the POS computers, messages are transferred from the main computer to
the POS computer and from the POS computer to the main computer. Because messages print automatically,
the store should leave their POS printer on when doing communications.

Send to Stores: enter the store #'s you want to send messages to.

Message: Write your message.

[Save] the message to send when you Call POS Registers.

Call POS Registers

                                            To Schedule a call to your POS/registers

Use this option on your main computer to receive POS transactions, mail list changes, and any messages
from the POS computer(s). Optionally, updated information can be transferred to the POS computer(s).
Note: The entire file is not downloaded; only the changes in the file since the last communications are
sent.

Before using this option you need to setup Communications for the store(s) you want called, and indicate the
COM port the modem and/or direct connect cable is connected to in Communications Setup.

Report Comment: Can be made and the setup Options saved to be retrieved later.

Stores: Indicate the store(s) to be called. The default for this field is the stores setup in Communications.

Registers: Indicate the register(s) to be called. Leave Blank to Call ALL Registers.

                                                                                         173
Select from the following options when you want the communications to occur:
Call Immediately
Call at the default time of (The default is 4:00 AM the next morning.)
Schedule call a box will appear where you can enter the date and time to call. The date is entered in a
MM/DD/YY format. The time is entered in the 24 hour format. (For example: to call October 29,1998 at 10:00
PM you would enter 10/29/98 22:00.)
Do you want to send data to these Stores/Registers check/uncheck the box.
If you will be calling these stores again after you post your sales, you can create a Super Job to
automatically Call Stores to receive their sales (Do not send Data to Stores), Print Sales Journal, and Post
Sales to Inventory then Call Stores again and (Send Data to Stores). By doing your calls this way your POS
will be up to date at the start of every day.

Poll POS Registers via Internet

                         To communicate with your POS registers by an Internet connection

Use this option on your main computer to receive POS sales, mail list changes, inventory change, and
messages that your registers have previously stored on the internet. You may also create files of data you
have changed since your last communication on the Internet for your POS registers to download later.
Before using this option you need to setup a Communications record for any registers you want to send data
to and indicate your Internet data transfer method in Communication Setup.
Report Comment: Can be made and the setup Options saved to be retrieved later.

                                                                                         174
Collect Data: Selecting this option will cause the job to retrieve any files your POS registers have previously
          sent. The data is unzipped and merged with the main office data.
               You may schedule the data collection in one of the following 3 ways:
                     Collect Immediately
                     Collect at a default time: (The default is 1:00 AM the next morning, but can be changed.
                                Contact CSI to find out how.)
                     Schedule at a specific date/time: A box will appear where you can enter the date and time
                                to collect your data. The date is entered in a MM/DD/YY format. The time is entered
                                in the 24-hour format. (For example: to call October 29,2000 at 10:00 PM, you could
                                enter 10/29/00 22:00.)

Send Data: Selecting this option will cause the job to create a file for each selected POS register. This file will
contain any changes since the last time a file was created for the POS register and will be sent to the internet
for the POS register to download and merge. If you have opted to both collect and send data in the same
job, the data will be collected and merged first.

               You may schedule the sending of data in one of the following 3 ways:
                     Send Immediately
                     Send at a default time: (The default is 3:00 AM the next morning, but can be changed.
                                Contact CSI to find out how.)
                     Schedule at a specific date/time: A box will appear where you can enter the date and time
                                to collect your data. The date is entered in a MM/DD/YY format. The time is entered
                                in the 24-hour format. (For example: to call October 29,2000 at 10:00 PM, you could
                                enter 10/29/00 22:00.)
                     Stores: Indicate the store(s) you will be creating files for. The default is the stores setup in
                                Communications to communicate by Internet.
                     Registers: Indicate the register(s) to be included. Leave Blank to Call ALL Registers.

If you want to post your sales after you have received data but before you send data to the registers,
You can create a Super Job to automatically Poll the registers (without sending data), Print Sales Journal,
Post Sales to Inventory, then Poll the registers again (sending data this time). By communicating this way
your POS will be up to date at the start of every day.

now archived as an old file 1 time ago, should you need to copy it again.

Logout From System

                       To close the RICS job list and run programs after shutting down RICS

This option is used to exit the RICS job list without starting the RICS screen spool file view. This option can be
run at the end of any super job to ensure that unwanted screen spool files are not available for viewing in
case the computer's primary user is away from their desk when the job list finishes. It can also prevent
unauthorized access to screen spool files after overnight polling has completed. You may also add a program
to run after the job list is exited. In the example above, when the job list finishes, RICS will launch a tape
backup program. To ensure that these operations run properly, please remember to exit the RICS Main Menu
after running Logout from RICS job either stand-alone or as part of a Super Job.

Import Internet Sales

                                       To import Sales exported from an Internet store

This option may be used to import sales from an internet store or any other source that can create a comma
delimited file adhering to the RICS import specifications. The file will be vigorously validated. If any data is
incorrect, the entire file will be rejected and the sales will not be placed into the RICS system. The RICS sales
import specification is listed below. It will be up to you or your web store provider to export the file according
to the RICS sales import specifications. If you or your provider has any questions about the RICS sales import
specifications, please contact RICS Technical Support.

                                                                                         180
File Name - the name of the file that will be imported. Include the full path name and drive letter.
If there are any exceptions, a journal will be generated and No sales will be imported. If there are no
exceptions, the sales will be merged into the existing sales file and the job will end. Under no circumstances
will RICS delete the import file.
After importing the sales file you will have to print the Sales Journal and Post your Sales to Inventory
before the items sold are deducted from inventory and the sales dollars and quantities will increase.

Backup Data

             Backups your data to diskettes, CD or Zip disk

Backup your data daily!!! CSI recommends that you backup your data at least once a day, if not more often.
When you enter data on your computer it is being stored on your hard disk. Backups are done as an
"insurance policy" to prevent data loss. It is not common, but situations can occur that can cause your data to
become damaged or lost. Your data is valuable, so protect it. Backing up copies your data information from
the hard disk to diskettes, over-writing what was previously on those diskettes. If you have a problem with
your computer you can then restore the data from the diskettes on to a different computer, you would then
only lose data entered since the last time you backed up your data.

Do not use this option to backup data to update your POS computers,
use Backup Files for POS instead.

Daily Backups - We strongly recommend that at least seven sets of backup diskettes (One labeled for
each day of the week) be kept in the office.

Monthly Backups - It is wise to use different diskettes labeled for each month (12 sets of backup diskettes).
This provides additional security, and provides the ability to re-run that month's reports at a later time if
needed. Also, we recommend having one set of backup diskettes stored off the premises and updated
periodically, such as weekly, bi-weekly, or monthly.

If you check the End of Month Backup check box, the Backup Path will change to the PKZIP
DRIVE\YYYYMMM\. An example would be if PKZIP DRIVE was C:\RICSWIN\, and you are backing up in
2003 with the Current Month set to 2 the new Backup Path would C:\RICSWIN\2003FEB\. If the directory
does not exist, you are prompted to create the new directory. If you chose yes, the backup creates the
directory and continues normally. If you chose no, the backup stops without completing.

To change your diskette drive location in Change RICS.CFG in the line for Section type in General on the
line for Item type in PKZIP DRIVE and in the line for Entry type in the location of the drive.

You can now backup to CD if you have a Read/Write CD-Rom, saving you time and requiring only 1 CD,
compared to multiple diskettes. You should still use a different CD for each day!!

An enhancement called RICS common files was made to increase speed between the POS computers and
the data server. If you attempt to backup and other computers are in RICS, you may receive the following
message:

The RICS common files must be closed to guarantee an accurate backup. RICS will automatically close those
files when there is no activity for 5 minutes. The user attempting to backup can have the other users close
their RICS common files by using the menu option Options -> Miscellaneous -> Close RICS Common Files.
Once the common files are closed the backup will proceed automatically. To retry before the 30 second
automatic retry, press the [R] key. Pressing any other key, or clicking on the form will cancel the backup
process.

                                                                                         184
Restore Data

                                         Restores Data from diskettes, CD or Zip Disk
IMPORTANT: Make sure you know what you're doing before restoring information
All YOUR CURRENT DATA ON THE COMPUTER WILL BE OVER WRITTEN.
Restoring is the opposite of backing up. Restoring copies information from diskettes to the hard disk, over-
writing what was previously on the hard disk.

Look at Job List

                                           Look at or change Jobs scheduled to Run

Many RICS menu options (i.e. reports) can be put with other options into a Job List which can then be run at
one time. You can use this multi-task option by clicking [Add Job and Continue] or [Alt] & [C] instead of
[Add Job and Run] on the report selection screens. It will display the status of all jobs submitted and let you
cancel, or change the priority of the jobs submitted. To run the same set of Jobs over you can create Super
Jobs.

Click on the Job you want to change. The following keys will make these changes to the Job List:

Priority        Click the arrows to move the selected Job up or down in the Pri (Priority) list.
[Hold Job]      Puts the task on hold (it will not run until it is released).
[Release Job]   Releases job previously put on hold.
[Delete Job]    Deletes or cancels the job from running.
[Reset Output]  Changes the output of the selected job to the output of the current Printer Setup
[Refresh]       Redisplays the Job List to display any new changes
[Start Jobs]    Starts (or Runs) the jobs

Look at Screen Spool File

                                   Look at Screen Spool file (Output/Reports) on Screen
This option is used to view reports, journals, logs, etc. that are printed to a screen spool file (Instead of
directly to a printer). This option will let you look at and manipulate the screen spool file. See Printer Setup, for
more information on how to print to a screen spool file.

Selecting a Report - highlight the report. Once the appropriate report is selected, click [OK].
Note: The Screen Spool Files are listed in the format: User, Date (YYear, MMonth, DDate), Time
(HHours,MMinutes,SSeconds), Report Name. Example: JOHN 1998-11-16 123141 Salesperson List.scn
would mean the Salesperson List was run by JOHN on 11/16/1998 at 12:31:41 the .scn at the end of the
report name refers that it is a screen spool file. All reports will always be listed in the order they were ran,
with the most recent reports listed first.

Deleting a Screen Spool File - Deleting a screen spool file will NOT delete any data. It is the equivalent of
"throwing away" a printed report. It is a good idea not to have too many screen spool files. If you need to keep
a report, print it out and then delete it. If you do not need to keep a report, click [Delete] or [Alt] + [D]. This
will delete the highlighted or the displayed screen spool file.

Deleting more than one Screen Spool File - To delete more than one screen spool file at a time, highlight
the first screen spool file you want deleted, hold down the [Ctrl] key then click the mouse on the next file you
want deleted and continue till you are finished selecting, click [Delete] or [Alt] + [D]. This will delete the
highlighted screen spool files.

Deleting ALL Screen Spool Files - To delete ALL screen spool files click [Delete All].

Printing a Screen Spool File - To print a report from the selection screen without viewing it, select the report
in the list you want to print. Click the [Print] button or [Alt] + [P]. To print multiple screen spool files, select
the files you want to print by holding down the [Ctrl] key and then clicking each file you want to print. To print
a range of pages, you must print after displaying the report on the screen.

Export a Screen Spool File to PDF - To export a report to PDF (Portable Document Format) from the
selection screen without viewing it, select the report in the list you want to print. Click the [PDF] button or [Alt]
+ [F]. To export multiple screen spool files, select the files you want to export by holding down the [Ctrl] key

                  186
and then clicking each file you want to export. To export a range of pages, you must export after displaying
the report on the screen.

Viewing a Report on the Screen - Because a printed report can be up to 230 columns wide and most
screens are only 80 columns wide not all of a report will fit on the screen at once. Use the arrow keys to
navigate the screen.

To move Up or Down:
Click the Line box arrows in either direction to move one line at a time, or click and hold the mouse, after a
brief pause you then scroll in the direction you choose. The up/down arrows on the keyboard will also move
1 line in that direction, or hold down to scroll.

Click the Page box arrows in either direction to move one screen at a time, or click and hold the mouse, after
a brief pause you then scroll by page in the direction you choose. The [Page Up] and [Page Down] keys will
shift an entire screen at a time, or hold down to scroll.

The vertical scroll bar may be used to move to an approximate section of the report.

The [Home] key will jump to the beginning of the report; the [End] key will jump to the last page of the report.

To Left or Right:
Left Click and hold you mouse on the scroll bar and move your mouse in the direction you want to move, or
click the box arrows in either direction to move one line at a time, or click and hold the mouse, you then scroll
in the direction you choose. The left/right arrows will move 10 columns in the direction of the arrow. [Shift] +
left/right arrows will move 1 column in the direction of the arrow. [Ctrl] + left/right arrows will move to the
beginning/end of the row.

Selecting a Different Report - When you are looking at an existing screen spool file, click [New File] this will
display a list of your available screen spool files. Select the other report you want to look at, and click [OK].

Split Screen ­ Click the [Split] button to divide the screen in half with the same report. You can then position
both halves to view two different areas of the report at the same time. To turn split screen off, click the [Un-
Split] button.

Switch between the Split Screens ­ If the screen isn't split, see the Split Screen section above. You can
then scroll only the active screen report. To get the other half of the screen active, click the [Switch] button.

Locking part of the report ­ Click the [Lock] button to lock a portion of the screen horizontally. Locking the
screen horizontally allows you to keep certain columns of information on the left side of the screen "frozen".
Example: You printed a sales analysis report with SKU detail and YTD sales. [Lock] would "freeze" the
number of columns necessary to keep the SKUs on the screen.

Searching for a number, character or text string ­ Click the [Find] button to bring up the Find window. A
new box will appear and say Find What. Type in the number (which may be an SKU number), character, or
string of text you want to find and click [OK]. It will stop and highlight where it finds your request. To start
scanning from the beginning of the report, press the [Home] key before clicking [Find]. Click [Repeat Last
Find] and it will then find the next occurrence of that text string in the report.

Printing a Report from the Screen ­ Click the [Print] button to display the Print window. A new box will
appear and say Print from page and to page. Enter the number of the pages you want to print (Print from

                                                                                         187
page 1 to page 999999 is the default, and will print the entire report).
Exporting a Report from the Screen to PDF ­ Click the [PDF] button to display the Export to PDF window.
A new box appears and lists a PDF Filename. By default, the filename is the same name as the report and
the directory the PDF file is saved is the same directory as the RICS data path. To default to a different
directory, add the following entry to the RICS.CFG:
Section: ScreenSpool
Item: PDFDir
Value: Enter the directory you want the PDF documents saved to in the format "C:\RICSWIN\PDF"
Click [Export] or press the [ALT] + [E] keys to export the file to PDF.

Reminders

                                                Set up Reminders or Appointments
Reminders are an optional feature of RICS. Whenever you log into RICS, all the current day's Reminders are
displayed. Also, if you are logged into RICS when an appointment is due, an alarm will ring, and the message
for that Reminder will be displayed on the screen.
Entering an Reminder -
Enter your User ID, if you do not have User IDs enter in SUPERVISOR. If you use passwords, you may enter
another user's appointments by entering a different ID number. Appointments entered for different users will
be displayed as, "in use by someone else". Only your appointments will be displayed.
Enter in the Date/Time you want to be informed of the reminder in the following format
MMonth/DDay/YYear HHour:MMinutes. Make sure you enter a space after the Year and before the Hour.
Example Dates:
01/01/05 10:00 ­ Close year
01/31/04 22:00 ­ Close month (notice military time for 10:00 PM)
Enter a brief description of the reminder in Subject, and the Message.
You may automatically Reschedule the reminder for a later date. Your options are Don't Reschedule,
Reschedule in ___ days, Reschedule next month, Reschedule next year.

Super Jobs

                                      Super Jobs are many Jobs saved to run together
For a group of Jobs you want to run together, again and again you can save them to create Super Jobs (i.e.
Call Stores, Weekly Reports, Close Month).

                                                                                         189
To create a Super Job, enter in a new Super Job Name and press enter. A list of Available Job Names will
appear on the left and a list of Saved Selections for that option will appear on the right. You can scroll the list
using the scroll bar, up/down arrow keys, Page Up/Down keys, or Home/End keys. Use the mouse or
press the [Tab] to activate the options on the right.

Highlight the option on the right and select [Add New Job] or [Alt] + [N] to add to the current Super Job list.

The items in the list will run in their order in the list. You can choose items in the Super Job list to either
[Move Up], [Move Down], or [Remove] them from the list.
