so the daily Unattended Backup can be added to a Super Job.

Backup to CD

To backup to CD you must have a Read/Writeable CD-Rom drive.

Media Choices
CD-R

     Advantage:
          · Many newer CD burners can write 12 times faster to a CD-R than a CD-RW.
          · Can reuse the CD.
          · Inexpensive

     Disadvantage:
          · CD-Recordable discs have a limited life. Once an area on the disc is used, it is cannot be
                re-written meaning that the number of times a CD-R can be used is limited to how large
                the backup file is.

CD-RW
     Advantage:
          · CD Re-Writeable discs can write over an area previously written multiple times. It can
                also be formatted or erased to clear the CD completely.
     Disadvantage:
          · More expensive than CD-R discs
          · Slow burn speed (typically 4x) resulting in longer burn time

Getting Started
     1. From the Utilities 1 screen, click the Backup Data button
     2. Place the media (CD-R or CD-RW) in the Writeable CD-drive.
     3. Set the Backup Path to the drive letter of the CD burner
     4. Click the [Backup] button
     5. When you are backing up to a CD, RICS creates a temporary folder /TEMPBACK under the
          RICSWIN directory to hold the backup file before writing to CD.
     6. Once the backup file is created, it is then written to the CD.
     7. Once the backup file is written to the CD, the CD tray will eject (if your CD-Drive supports this).

NOTES:
     · Use seven (7) CD's for daily backups, one for each day of the week. DO NOT REUSE THE SAME
          DISC FOR DAILY BACKUPS EACH DAY.
     · You can use the same CD for end of month backups if you check the End of Month Backup check
          box. This places the backup in a directory on the CD with the directory name containing the year and
          month of the backup. An example would be /2003JAN.
     · CD-R's can hold 650MB-700MB. If your backup file is larger than half the disc size, you will only get
          one use of the disc because a second backup will not fit.
     · Do not put anything else on your backup discs. They should strictly be for your backups.

                                                                                         191
ERRORS:
     Some errors you might receive before attempting to write a backup
     · IsMediaLoaded() failed. Make sure a disc is in the specified drive. - There is no disc in the drive, you
          may have put the disc in the wrong CD-drive, or you put a disc in that is closed. Make sure you have
          a disc in the drive listed in the error. If you do have a disc in the drive, make sure it is a CD-R or CD-
          RW. If there is, replace the disc with a new one because that one is closed.
     · Please Insert Disk #2 - The drive you specified is not a valid Read/Writeable CD-Rom. Check the
          drive letters of your CD-Drives and backup to the Read/Writeable one.

If you have any questions, please contact Technical Support.

                                                                                         192
                                 UUTTIILLIITTIIEESS 22

Compact/Repair a Database

                                                   Compacts and/or Repairs files

Backup all RICS data before using this utility! Listed above are all the data files in RICS and (their
meanings). It is possible for data files to become damaged. This program will compact the files and should
correct any damaged RICS data files, but it cannot always do so depending on the damage to the file. Click
on the file(s) to compact, (to select all files click [Select all databases]) then click [Continue], when
completed you will then be returned to the Main Menu.
The most common reason to run the Compact/Repair a Database is error 3343. Make sure you have a
backup before running this utility! After running Compact/Repair a Database for the affected database,
attempt to re-open the screen that reported the error.

Create/Delete a Database

                                    Deletes the current file and creates a new empty file
Backup all RICS data before using this utility! The screen will list all the data files in RICS and (their
meanings). When you create a file, you lose all existing information currently in the file. If a file is created
that contains a supplemental index, all supplemental indexes in all files will be dropped. Click on the file(s) to
delete then click [Continue]. When completed, you are returned to the Main Menu.

Check Data Integrity

                                                  Checks files for possible errors
Backup all RICS data before using this utility! The screen will list all the data files in RICS and (their

                                                                                         193
meanings). This utility will read a file(s) for any possible errors. Click on the file(s) to check then click
[Continue]. When completed, you are returned to this same menu, only no files will be checked. Two
common errors will be displayed as:

          Record 12345678 (store 1) in file RIINVQUA
          has an invalid row [XXX]
In this example, SKU 12345678 for store 1 has history that is inconsistent with the SKU's current size type. A
size type has been changed. You should usually delete invalid rows.
          Record 12345678 in file RIINVMAS points to file RICATEG
          using key 555 but record doesn't exist
In this example, category 555 has been deleted, but SKU 12345678 still 'belongs' to that category. In this
example, DO NOT delete the SKU. Write down the problem and correct it after the checkout is complete.
Four options are available when an error occurs: press [Esc] to immediately cancel this utility, press [Y] to
delete the record, press [N] to retain, not delete, the record; or press [A] to delete this record and any future
records that might be an error for the file.

Reset Pictures

                                  Assigns pictures to SKUs and deletes unused pictures

 This job affords the RICS user the ability to automatically assign picture file names to SKUs. In order for a
picture file to be assigned the SKU, the picture file exactly must match the SKU and have an extension of
'.jpg'.

 As RICS users delete old SKUs, the picture files still remain on their computer. This job can also optionally
delete all picture files in the RICSPICS folder that are not assigned to any SKU.

criteria and have a future price change.
Another option is to Only change SKUs with Week-to-Date sales. When this option is checked, SKUs that
match the criteria and have Week-to-Date sales are affected.

                                                                                         200
Frequent Buyer Plan

What is the Frequent Buyer Plan?

RICS can optionally track customer purchases and automatically award product discounts after a minimum
purchase requirement has been met. The frequent buyer plan can be configured to award discounts based on
total number of items purchased, total dollar amount purchased, or a fixed discount on every eligible
purchase. Below is a description of each method.

Method 1: A customer would buy X quantity and receive N percent of the average value of those X items on
their next purchase. That means, you tell RICS what quantity the customer needs to purchase to receive a
discount, and what percentage of the average that discount should be.

For example, your plan is for the customer to buy 6 and get 50% of the average value of those 6 items as a
credit on the 7th item. If the customer had six purchases of the following amounts: $50.00, $65.00, $60.00,
$70.00, $62.00, $67.00, they would receive a discount of $31.17 discount on their seventh purchase. That
discount represents 50% of the average value of the previous six purchases.

Method 2: A customer would purchase X total dollars and receive N dollars off on their next purchase. That
means, you tell RICS what dollar amount the customer needs to purchase to receive a discount, and what
dollar amount that discount should be.

For example, your plan is for the customer to buy $500.00 and receive a $50.00 discount on their next
purchase. If the customer had purchases of the following amounts: $85.00, $93.50, $45.00, $104.50, $92.75,
$85.00 for a total of $505.75, they would receive a $50.00 discount on their next purchase.

Method 3: A customer earns a fixed discount percentage on every purchase. For example, the customer
receives a 3% discount on every purchase. For Example, if the customer has a purchase of $50.00, they
would receive a $1.50.

Method 4: A customer would buy X quantity and receive N percent on their next purchase. That means, you
tell RICS what quantity the customer needs to purchase to receive a discount, and what percentage the
discount should be.

Method 5: A customer would purchase X total dallars and receive N percent on their next purchase. That
means, you tell RICS what dollar amount the customer needs to purchase to receive a discount, and what
percentage the discount should be.

For example, your plan is for the customer to buy 6 and get 50% off the 7th item. If the 7th item is $50.00 they
would receive $25.00 discount.

Other Frequent Buyer information
     Phase from one plan to another

You can transition a customer from one Frequent Buyer Plan to another. For example, you are discontinuing
a plan where the customer buys 12, and gets 100% of the average value of those 12 items as a discount on
their 13th purchase. You decide the new plan is buy 5 and get 50% of the average value of those 5 as a
discount on their 6th purchase. If chosen, after the customer has been awarded a discount on the old plan,
RICS will automatically put them on the new plan.

Change Frequent Buyer Plan

                                          Setup or change your Frequent Buyer Plan
In RICS you must create your Frequent Buyer credit and discount SKUs. You may also want to create a
separate category and vendor for those SKUs. For example, you could create a vendor called Frequent
Buyer, with a vendor number of FREQ and category 990, Frequent Buyer. You DO NOT want to assign
those SKUs a size type number. Recommended SKU numbers are FB/DISC and FB/CREDIT.

                                                                                         201
Frequent Buyer Plan Enabled - When checked, the Plan is turned on.

Number of Plans - You may choose up to 5 different plans.

Default Plan ­ select the Plan Number that is the default. This plan number would then be automatically
entered when you add a new customer. If you only have 1 plan enter a 1. If you do not want a default plan,
then leave this field blank.

Modify Plan # - the Plan Number you are working on.

Calculation Method - choose 1 through 5. The methods are defined in What is Frequent Buyer Plan.

Break Point -If using Calculation Method #1 or 4, then this would be the number of pairs (or items) needed to
be purchased to receive the discount. If using Calculation Method #2, #3 or #5, then this would be the $
amount needed to be purchased to receive the discount.

Discount -If using Calculation Method #1, #3, #4, or #5 then this is a %. If using Calculation Method #2 this is
a $ amount.

New Plan - After the break point has been satisfied, you may have the customer changed to a new plan. If
you have another plan that should take effect at that point, enter the appropriate plan #. If you only have one
plan, this would be 1.

Credit SKU - Enter the SKU # that you set up in RICS for frequent buyer credits. CSI recommends
FB/CREDIT

Discount SKU - Enter the SKU # that you set up in RICS for frequent buyer discounts. CSI recommends
FB/DISC

Accum Categories - You can select only those SKUs from certain categories to be eligible towards frequent
buyer purchases and discounts. For example, you may not want polishes, creams, laces, or other accessories
to count as eligible frequent buyer purchases. Categories can be entered as a range using a dash, or
individually using commas. If everything is eligible then leave this blank.

No Qty. Categories - This would be used if you are using SKU #'s for discounts or coupons, and you don't
want the discount/coupon quantity added to their purchase quantity, but you still want the discount/coupon
amount subtracted from the purchase amount in their plan.

Allow Negative Counts - Leave this Checked On, unless instructed by CSI to do something differently

Discount Full Price Only ­ when checked, select only those SKUs that are sold at full price (or above) to be
eligible towards frequent buyer purchases and discounts. For example, you may not want discount or
clearance merchandise to count as eligible frequent buyer purchases.

Retain Partial Credit - RICS can keep track of unused credit after a discount. You would have unused credit
if the discount were greater than the current purchase.

Credit Categories Only - when checked, if the customer is to receive a credit/discount, only SKUs in the
Accum Categories are eligible for the credit/discount. If unchecked, the SKU could be from any category.

Points Factor - For Calculation Methods #2 and #5, the customer can optionally see their dollars purchased
as 'points'. The Points Factor will be divided by the Dollars Purchased to arrive at the customers 'Points'. For
example a customer with $459.78 in Frequent Buyer Dollars purchased would have 9 points if the Points
Factor is 50, but 45,978 points if the Points Factor is set to .01.

                                                                                         202
After the Plan is Setup: All of these changes also need to be done at each POS computer. We recommend
that you copy this file to the POS computer(s). The Frequent Buyer Plan information will be copied when you
include the Inventory master file in Backup File for POS or send SKU and Store Changes to the POS via
Calling the POS Registers or Polling the Registers via the Internet.

Using the Frequent Buyer Plan

                                                   Using the Frequent Buyer Plan
You will add new account numbers in RICS as you normally would. The Plan Number will be filled in for you
automatically if you specified a "default plan number" when you set up the frequent buyer plan. Otherwise,
your salespeople will have to type in the plan number. Qty Purchased and $$$ Purchased will increment
with each purchase. They CANNOT be manually changed at the POS computer. RICS will display the Qty
Purchased and Dollars Purchased (depending on plan #) and the Estimated Discount. The Quantity and
Est Disc is highlighted (and possibly blink) to alert the salesperson that the customer has reached their
purchase limit.
After the customer has reached his/her purchase limit and makes their next purchase, a message similar to
the following will be displayed:

                                          Note: (37)
                       JOHNSON, MARY is now eligible for a

                                Frequent Buyer Discount of
                               $29.99. Apply discount now?

                                        Press Y or N
Press [Y]. RICS will apply the frequent buyer discount on that purchase.
The frequent buyer SKU will print as a negative one quantity with the price being the amount of the discount.
The customer's quantity purchased is then decreased by the amount of the break point. This usually means
the quantity purchased is reset to zero.
The balance of their frequent buyer will also print at the bottom of each ticket. If you prefer this balance to not
print, contact Customer Support.

Existing Customers FBP

                                               Frequent Buyer- Existing Customers
If you currently track a similar frequent buyer plan manually, it may be necessary to transfer those balances
(purchases) into RICS. Staff at the Main or POS computers can put existing customer balances on the
computer. To enter Frequent Buyer information click on Freq Buyer Input from the Run Other Utilities
program.

                                                                                         203
Entering existing customer purchases:
1. Type in the customer's account number and press [Enter]. The default plan number will fill in

     automatically. The cursor will be at the first quantity field. Type in the quantity and price of those items the
     customer has purchased that apply towards their current frequent buyer plan. (NOTE: DO NOT type in
     any item that does NOT count towards their current frequent buyer plan.)

2. After the current purchases are entered, click [Save] to save the information. A total quantity and dollar
     amount will be displayed at the bottom of the screen. You will be prompted to press [Enter]. You will then
     be able to enter a different account and their purchases.

At the POS if you need to enter sales while in the middle of entering existing customers in to the frequent
buyer plan you can. After you are done entering sales, you can then resume where you left off. All previously
entered information will not be lost.

Print - This will print out those customers and purchases that have been entered and not yet copied to a disk.
It will print on a 40 Column receipt printer.

When you are finished entering all existing frequent buyer plan entries, that information is then copied to a
diskette and sent to the main computer. Use a blank disk to copy this information. DO NOT use the same
diskette that is used to transfer sales. To copy the information press:

Copy to Disk - Enter the drive containing the disk and press [Enter].

The diskette can then be taken to the main computer. On the main computer do a backup of your data.
Backup Data then run the Freq Buy Update program.

Frequent Buyer Update

                                                Updates your Frequent Buyer Input

IMPORTANT: After you finish processing the frequent buyer diskette at the main computer, set the diskette
aside. It is very important that you do not process that diskette again. The information on the diskette is not
erased after it is processed. If you process the diskette again, you will double the purchases of each
customer.

Refunds with F B P

                                    Doing Returns when using the Frequent Buyer Plan
When a customer returns an item that counts towards a frequent buyer discount, their quantity purchased is
decreased and the estimated discount is recalculated.
If the customer were to return an item after they have received a discount, you have two choices:

     1) Return the item at regular price, but disregard the discount they received. The quantity purchased
          would then be a negative one. The customer would have to purchase an additional item to offset the
          return to reach their next discount level.

     2) Return the item, taking into account the discount they received. To do this, return the item they
          purchased at full price. Next, sell the SKU used for the frequent buyer discounts for the amount of the
          discount. Below is an example of how this would print on the customer's receipt.

-1 2632 105 M ROCKSPORT TI 84.97-
 1 FB/DISC FREQ. BUYER 49.97
RICS will adjust the quantity purchased and the estimated discount as it was before the customer received a
discount. The customer would then be eligible to receive the discount again on their next purchase.

Macro Management

                                               Macros are used to automate typing
A macro is a single keystroke that represents a series of keystrokes. The best time to use a macro is when

                                                                                         205
the same information is typed continually. Whenever a macro is run--by pressing a special key combination--
the series of keystrokes is automatically "played back". A single keystroke, or macro, could then be used fill in
that information automatically.

Up to nine macros can be defined, with a descriptive name for each. When a macro is "played back", each
keystroke in the macro is executed in turn, starting at the cursor's location. Make sure you start the macro at
the same location every time.

To create a Macro: enter a Macro Name and an Activation Menu Key (must be a number between 1 and 9)
then enter Keys to send when activated and [Save].

To enter to the next field on screen in a macro you must put [{Enter}] (the word Enter within { } braces) or [~]
([Shift] + [`] - the key above the [Tab] key) to represent the enter keystroke.

In the above example this Macro was setup for a City, State, and Zip Code in the mail list.

Other Keys:  {Down}
Down Arrow   {Left}
Left Arrow   {Right}
Right Arrow  {Up}
Up Arrow     {Tab}
Tab          %
ALT          +
SHIFT        ^
CTRL

{bmc keystrokes.bmp}

When a macro has been created an option called Keystrokes will appear on the top line.

To Display a List or Run a Macro: Click on Keystrokes and select from the list of Macros or press [Alt] +
[K] to display the list of Macros and then the [#] number of the Macro.

           AACCCCOOUUNNTTSS RREECCEEIIVVAABBLLEE

Overview

The RICS Accounts Receivable software (if purchased) is a totally integrated module with the RICS Point-of-
Sale. New customers, house charges, and charge payments can be entered and automatically posted to A/R.
The A/R system contains all the necessary reports and display screens to completely track your A/R balances
for both Balance Forward accounts for individuals and Open Item accounts for commercial customers. Send
customer statements, add finance charges, or setup minimum payments are some of the many features in
this software.

A/R Setup

           To setup basic information about your A/R

There are three folders in the A/R Setup. Information must be completed on all three folders for the
statements to print correctly.

General:
Enter the Current Year that you began using the Accounts Receivable Module. This year should not be
changed manually at the end of the calendar year. Instead, you must run menu option Roll Over A/R Current
Year and the current year shown on this screen will update to the new year.

Open Item Account Options - Enter your Terms. The statements for this type of account will always list
each open invoice regardless of its age. This statement is usually used for commercial or business accounts
that pay by invoice. In other words, each payment received on this statement type must be entered on the
main computer and payments are applied to individual invoices.

Balance Forward Account Options - The statements for this type of account will print the Balance Forward
amount from the last statement and then list all new charges, adjustments, and payments from that time with
the total due. This is similar to most regular credit card statements you receive and most individual (non-

                                                                                         208
commercial) accounts will use this method. Payments can be entered on the main computer or the POS
computer and will always automatically apply to the oldest balance due.

Grace period for __ days - used to establish the due date for Balance Forward accounts. For example, if
statements are printed on the last day of the month and payment is due by the 20th of the next month, enter
20 for the grace period.

Minimum Payment - If there is an amount due to print on the statement, enter the fraction of the total
balance due that you want for the minimum calculation. If you do not want a minimum payment to print on the
statement, then enter 1/1 for the minimum.

Accumulate minimum payment - If the minimum payment was not made for the prior month that months
minimum payment balance will be add to this month's minimum payment.

Late Charge - If payment is made after grace period this amount is added to the balance due.

All Account Options -Finance Charges are calculated using the average daily balance method.

Open Item Accounts - the finance charge is calculated if full payment is not received on individual invoices
within the terms described above.

Balance Forward Accounts ­ the finance charge is computed on the average daily balance since the last
statement date if payment in full for the statement balance is not received (less any credit adjustments) by the
number of grace period days described above.

Apply Finance Charges - Check on to apply, and enter the Annual Rate __ % and the Minimum Finance
Charge__.

Allow an additional __ days for the payment to be overdue allows each account (both Open Item and
Balance Forward) to have an additional number of days to receive payment before a finance charge is
calculated. Some users allow an additional 4 or 5 days for a payment mailed to be received. The aging is still
based on the date due before these additional days are added.

Statement:
Statement Address - should be entered for your store name and address you want to print at the top of the
statements. If you are using pre printed forms, leave this blank.

PREPRINTED FORMS: If you are interested in using pre-printed forms with your name and/or logo on
them contact, Moore Business Forms at 1-800-323-6230 to order 1-part form # 17889 or a 2-part form #
17897.
ENVELOPES: To use double window envelopes for pre-printed or plain paper forms order # K15438.

Statement Detail - refers to how much detail you want to print on the statements. The least detail, but
probably the most common option, is Ticket Totals. Choosing any of the other three options will include more
detail to display to the customer individual departments, categories or SKUs that were purchased.

Messages:
Statement Messages - allows each user to enter their own wording to print on their statements for payments
and dunning notices. The oldest balance due for each customer will determine which dunning notice will print
at the bottom of their statement.

Message to print at the end of each statement - allows each user to enter a message that will appear at
the end of each statement. This could be used to tell customers about upcoming events.

                                                                                         209
Enter Customers in A/R

                                                Enter Customers for A/R Accounts
Account # - Enter the new account number (account number must be already in RICS Mail List, or you can
Lookup the customer's name. Their name and address will appear along with other account information. New
accounts can also be added at the POS computer for accounts using the default statement type.

Statement Type - Check either Balance Forward or Open Item option. The terms for any account can be
changed at a later date.

Apply Finance Charge - Check on to calculate finance charges. This can be changed for individual
accounts.

Enter A/R Payments

                                           Enter A/R Payments at the Main Computer
Batch Date is the date the payments are to be posted, even if it is a different than today's date. To change
the batch date click [Change Batch Date] or [Alt] + [B].

Account # - Enter the account number or Lookup the customer's name. Their name and address will appear
along with other account information.

Reference # - is a required field. Generally, the customer's check # is entered in this field. After a payment
has been entered and saved, you can enter a corrected payment by entering the previously used Reference
#. The system will assign a different Sequence # for each correction. You can also re-apply the payment to
different outstanding invoices by re-entering the previously used Reference #.

New Payment on balance forward accounts will automatically apply to the oldest balance. Payments on open
item accounts must be applied to specific invoices and the system will not allow you to save the payment until
it is fully applied.

[Reverse] or [Alt] + [R] - reverses a previous selected payment when the Reference # is entered.

[Auto Apply] or [Alt] + [A] - applies the payment(s) to the oldest open item ticket still open. If there are many
open invoices, it may be faster to press [Auto Apply] then override those invoice payments that are incorrect.

[Detail] or [Alt] + [D] - shows the ticket detail for the account entered. The detail screen has the following
options:

     · [Ticket Summary] or [Alt] + [T] - shows the ticket summary for the account entered.
     · [Ticket Detail] or [Alt] + [I] - shows the ticket detail for the account entered.
     · [Payment Summary] or [Alt] + [P] - shows the payment summary for the account entered.
     · [Payment Detail] or [Alt] + [A] - shows the payment detail for the account entered.

Enter A/R Adjustments

                                        Enter A/R Adjustments or Beginning Balances
Batch Date is the date the adjustments are to be posted, even if it is a different than today's date. To change
the batch date click [Change Batch Date] or [Alt] + [B].

Account # - Enter the account number or you can Lookup the customer's name. Their name and address will
appear along with other account information.

Enter any account adjustments by entering in a Description and the Amount. The amount can be either
positive or negative. If printing ticket totals on the statement, only the description on the first line above and
the total adjustment will print on the statement.

Entering Beginning Balances:

                                                                                         210
You will also use this screen to enter your beginning balances when implementing Accounts Receivable.
     · Balance Forward accounts will be entered with a description of BALANCE FORWARD and the current
          amount due.
     · Open Item accounts will be initially entered by inputting each open invoice. If you enter several open
          invoices on the same screen and you are printing ticket totals only on the statements, only the
          description from the first line and the total adjustment amount will print on the statement. Therefore, if
          you want each invoice listed individually on the statement, enter only one open invoice per adjustment
          screen and [Save]. Generally you would enter the invoice number as the description.
     [Detail] or [Alt] + [D] shows the ticket detail for the account entered. In the detail screen you will also
     have the option to select:
     · [Ticket Summary] or [Alt] + [T] shows the ticket summary for the account entered.
     · [Ticket Detail] or [Alt] + [I] shows the ticket detail for the account entered.
     · [Payment Summary] or [Alt] + [P] shows the payment summary for the account entered.
     · [Payment Detail] or [Alt] + [A] shows the payment detail for the account entered.

Print Aged Trial Balance

                                                      List of Aged Trial Balances
Aging dates in days is the number of days to increment for aging. Thirty day increments are most common.

Include Accounts with Balance Forward Statements - Check on or off.

Include Accounts with open Item Statements - Check on or off.

Include customers with no aging when unchecked omits customers with -0- balances. However, it does
include customers with an open invoice and an offsetting open credit, even if the total balance is zero.

Sort Report by: Option for Account#, Name or Current Balance

range. If you choose to list activity from last statement date, Open Item accounts will still print all open

Print A/R General Information when checked includes information such as YTD charges and payments,

Include Accounts with Balance Forward Statements - Check on or off.

                                                                                         212
Print A/R Statements

                                                  Prints A/R Customer Statements
It is very important to make a current backup of your data before running statements because the A/R
files are being updated during this process. If your power goes off during statements, you would need to
restore data from the backup before running statements again.

Balance Forward accounts are updated with a new BALANCE FORWARD while printing statements. Also
finance charges are calculated for Balance Forward and Open Item accounts while printing statements.
Therefore, it is mandatory that statements are printed each month.

You can print a preview statement at any time during the middle of the month for a selected account. It will not
update the new BALANCE FORWARD for Balance Forward accounts nor compute finance charges for any
accounts. Their normal statement will print again at month end.

Because some users may experience a printer problem while printing statements, the system includes a
feature to automatically create a screen spool file, even if you are normally printing directly to a printer as set
up in Printer Setup. That way, if you have printer problems during statements, instead of restoring data from
the backup you can go to Look at Screen Spool Files and simply print the statements again.

Date Statements - is the date to print on the statement.

Print Statements For: You have one of four choices-
     Only Balance Forward Accounts
     Only Open Item Accounts
     All Accounts
     One Account with no updates

Have you made a backup of your data? You must make a current backup of your data before running
statements.

Purge A/R Detail

                                                     Deletes Closed A/R Activity
This option will purge (delete) the A/R detail for all closed activity from the entered date and earlier. The
system will keep A/R invoice detail history in the file even though the invoices have already been paid.
Retaining this detail allows the user to run Print A/R Detail for a selected date range and print the detail for as
far back as you want to keep it. You can also review this detail on the screen for selected accounts by
pressing [Detail] from A/R - Enter Customer, Enter Payments, or Enter Adjustments.

It is up to each user to determine when they want to clear the old detail from the system. Some users may
keep the last year's history and others may retain only the last several months. The paid or closed invoices
will not continue to print on Open Item Statements nor display on the Apply Payments screen once the -0-
balance invoice has printed on a statement.

Purge closed detail dated up to enter the date you want detail delete before.

Have you made a backup of your data?
You must make a current backup of your data before deleting A/R detail.

Roll Over A/R Current Year

                                                      Changes A/R Account year
This option will change the A/R current year to the next year and clear all YTD customer totals and reset the
totals for YTD to $ 0. NOTE: You must run this option before posting A/R sales to a new year.

Have you made a backup of your data? You must make a current backup of your data before rolling
over A/R Current Year

Company Setup

                                           Information on your company preferences
Enter the Year-ending Month for which your calendar year ends. The system will then know when to zero out
the yearly sales figures during the month/season/year end close. This month does not have to match your
accounting or tax year end. It could be your merchandising year end.

Enter both the Current month and Current year. You can only post sales for the current month. When you
run the Close Month/Season/Year, the current month (season and year, if necessary) will be incremented.
(You can, however, enter sales for any month.)

Click on each month in Season Ending Months that is the end of a season for your company. At the end of a
season, when you run Close Month/Season/Year this will zero out the season-to-date sales figures.

You can have RICS Automatically Generate Labels (or hang tags or jewelry tags) for each SKU, either
After orders (POs), or After receipts (PO or manual) are entered.

You can optionally have RICS Print retail price on Purchase Orders and/or Print cost on Purchase
Orders.

Sort SKUs on reports by: can be indexed either by the SKU#, by the Vendor SKU#, or by SKU
description. Because the SKU# is 15 characters, and the Vendor SKU#, or SKU Description is 20
characters, indexing by SKU# is faster and consumes less disk space.

Price to print on manual transfers journal: You may choose either Retail price, Average cost, or Neither
to print on the manual transfer journal.

Open-To-Buy entry Method: Use % of total store sales and fixed monthly percentages - this option is
used by new stores that have no sales, or who want to set up their own sales plan.
Use % change over last years sales for each category - use this plan if you have history in the system,
and want to do just % change over last years sales.

You can optionally Save posted sales transactions information when posting sales. Now, when printing the
Special Orders, Layaways, House pymt/chgs, Sales Person Summary or Sales by Time reports, you can print
either from unposted transactions or from previously posted information. This option should be checked on.

You can add a user-defined Sales Transaction Type 2. Use this to track sales by store and salesperson.

Communication Setup

                              Setup how you communicate with your stores or main office
There are 4 ways to communicate RICS data with computers. One way is by exchanging sales and backup
diskettes between the MAIN and POS computers. The other 3 ways are by modem, a direct connect cable,
and via the Internet.

Communications setup: Before communicating with a POS register, you will need to setup the register in
File Setup - Communications. For a list of registers setup for communications see Print Communications File.

                                                                                         214
Communicating via modem and Direct Connect Cable:

To communicate by modem:
You will need to tell RICS what communications port (COM port) your modem is located at. CSI strongly
recommends a Hayes, U.S. Robotics, or Zoom external (outside the computer) modem for
communications. If you are having communications issues and using an internal modem, CSI support staff
will require you to purchase an external modem. This is because the quality and reliability of the external
modems is higher than the internal modems. These modems are designed for direct computer-to-computer
connections and are it is easier for CSI to help you with any problems you encounter when you use these
modems.
Modems also need certain commands issued to setup the process of dialing, sending data, and receiving
data. These commands can be different for different modems. A default set of modem commands may be
entered by pressing the [Default Modem Commands] button.
To communicate by direct connect cable:
You will need to tell RICS what communications port (COM port) your direct connect cable located at. A direct
connect cable connects 2 computers and allows the computers to exchange data over the cable. When you
communicate via direct connect cable, the Communications record for the register should have a phone
number of 'DIRECT' and the registers Communicate with Main screen should answer on ring 'D'

Communicating via Internet:

In order to communicate via the Internet, you first need to tell RICS how you will be using the Internet to
communicate your data:

     · None - Use this option when you don't have an Internet connection to use with RICS
     · Have RICS Connect - Use this option if you want RICS to attempt to connect to your Internet Service

          Provider (ISP) when starting communications and disconnect when done communicating. This option

                                                                                         215
          will require you to fill in the fields ISP UserID, ISP Password, and ISP Phone Number. These are
          the parameters that RICS will need to connect to your ISP. To have RICS connect, you must have a
          Dial-Up Network Connection that can be accessed by windows. Not all Internet Service Providers
          offer this feature, preferring instead to control the connection via proprietary software.
     · Don't have RICS Connect - Use this option when you have a 24/7 Internet Connection (DSL/Cable)
          or must establish the Internet connection yourself.
     · Local Directory - Use this option when your POS registers can access your local network (via the
          internet or by other methods) directly as a local or network hard drive. In this case the only field that
          will need to be entered is the Directory the data is to be sent to. This field does not have to be same
          for the main as the registers.

Fields that may be needed for Internet file Transfers:
Host Site: The domain name or IP address of the web site (normally an FTP site) storing the files.
Host Logon Name: The user name you will be logging into the site as.
Host Logon Password: The password this user logs on as.
Account: The account name or number to logon to the web site, if required.
Port: The specific port number to communicate through, if required.

Firewall Type: The type of firewall you have
     0 = No firewall
     1 = Use Socks4 firewall
     2 = Use Socks5 firewall
     3 = Use Proxy USER command
     4 = Use Proxy SITE command
     5 = Use Proxy PROXY command
     6 = Use Proxy OPEN command
     7 = Use simple Pipe

Firewall Port: The specific port number to the firewall through.
Firewall Host: The name of the firewall host.
Firewall Logon Name: The user name you will be logging into the firewall with, if required.
Firewall Password: The password this user logs onto the firewall with, if required.

Printer Setup

                                             Information on your printer preferences

Printers are setup for each user. The Printer Setup screen allows you to setup a printer to print wide reports,
narrow reports, mailing labels, and a receipt printer. Here you specify which printer handles RICS print jobs.
You only need to setup your printer once for each of the four options, unless you change printers.

To setup a printer:

     1. Click the tab of the printer you want to change (Wide, Narrow, Mailing Labels, or Receipt)
     2. Click the [Change Printer] button
     3. Select from the list of Printers Setup in Windows. (Printers must be setup in Windows before they will

          be listed here.
     4. In the Print Setup window, select the paper size (letter or legal) and orientation (portrait or landscape)

          and the paper source (automatic, first available, manual, tray 1, or tray 2). Changing a printer here will
          then make the new printer the default printer in Windows. Click OK to save your settings.
     5. Use the printer (wide, narrow, mailing label, or receipt) specific options listed below to complete the
          Printer Setup.
     6. Click the [Save] button.

                                                                                         216
NOTE: For printing bar codes, RICS supports laser printers (NOT ink jet, desk jet, or bubble jet printers)
made by HP (Hewlett Packard). Many laser printers claim to be HP compatible, but are NOT 100%
compatible. Therefore, CSI only guarantees RICS to work with HP laser printers.

CSI recommends an Zebra* LP2722 or TLP2722 bar code printer for printing bar code labels. If using two
printers, we recommend having a second parallel printer port installed in the main computer to attach the
second printer instead of using an A/B switch box.

Wide Reports:

     · Dot Matrix/Text-Only Printer ­ check this option if you are using a Dot Matrix Printer
     · Print reports to screen spool file option prints to a file which can be viewed at a later time. If this

          option is not checked, the wide reports print directly to the printer. See Look at screen spool file for
          more information.
     · Print journals to a screen spool file option always print journals to a screen spool file preventing a
          lost journal if the printer jams. See Look at screen spool file for more information.
     · Lines per page - how many lines are printed before going to a new page. Laser Printers reports are
          required to print on legal size paper (8˝" X 14") in landscape mode and the lines per page are 41.
          Dot Matrix Printers reports are printed on 14" X 11" continuous paper and the lines per page are 56.
     · Print to receipt printer when possible is only used for a 40 column receipt printer at a POS.
     · Select the font to use. The fonts listed are the fonts that you have in your computer. Recommended
          fonts in both Compressed and Un-compressed are Courier New, Line Printer or Lucida
          Console. You may want to experiment with some of the other fonts to get a different look to your
          reports.
     · Top Margin and Left Margin ­ number of inches to from the top and left to start printing

Narrow Reports:
     · Dot Matrix/Text-Only Printer ­ check this option if you are using a Dot Matrix Printer
     · Print reports to screen spool file option prints to a file which can be viewed at a later time. If this
          option is not checked, the wide reports print directly to the printer. See Look at screen spool file for
          more information.
     · Lines per page - how many lines are printed before going to a new page. Laser Printers are
          required to print on letter size paper (8˝" X 11") in portrait mode and the lines per page is 56. Dot
          Matrix Printers reports are printed on 8 ˝" X 11" continuous paper and the lines per page is also 56.
     · Print Purchase Orders to a screen spool file is an option to always print a Purchase Order to a
          screen spool file preventing a lost PO if the printer jams.
     · Print to receipt printer when possible is only used for a 40 column receipt printer at a POS.
     · Select the font to use. The fonts listed are the fonts that you have in your computer. Recommended
          fonts in both Compressed and Un-compressed are Courier New, Line Printer or Lucida
          Console. You may want to experiment with some of the other fonts to get a different look to your
          reports.
     · Top Margin and Left Margin ­ number of inches to from the top and left to start printing

Mailing Labels:
     · Dot Matrix/Text-Only Printer ­ check this option if you are using a Dot Matrix Printer
     · Select the type/size labels you are using for your printer.
                o Dot Matrix Printers: Select either the 1 across labels or 4 across labels.
                o Laser Printers: Select either laser sheets (2X10) or laser sheets (3X10)
                o Zebra (LP/TLP) Printers: Select Zebra (LP/TLP) Labels
     · Select the font to use. The fonts listed are the fonts that you have in your computer. Recommended
          fonts in both Compressed and Un-compressed are Courier, or Line Printer. You may want to
          experiment with some of the other fonts to get a different look to your labels.
     · If you want your labels to printer larger or smaller than the default size, enter a Font Size. The default
          size is 10. The larger the number, the bigger the font will print.
     · Top Margin and Left Margin ­ number of inches to from the top and left to start printing

                                                                                         217
Receipt Printer:
     · If using a thermal or Dot Matrix printer, check Dot Matrix/Text-Only Printer option. Select the font to
          use. The fonts listed are the fonts that you have in your computer. Recommended fonts are: Un-
          compressed: Roman 10cpi and Compressed: Roman 17cpi.

*PLEASE NOTE: Zebra printers were formerly manufactured under the name Eltron. All settings and
instructions under either name are interchangeable with regards to appropriate model number.

Mail List Setup

                                            Information on your mail list preferences

This option is used to set up the additional information you might want to keep about customers in the Mailing
List file. Up to six additional items can be entered. You do not have to set up any additional items. You can

                                                                               add or change these entries at a later time.

                                                                               Description: Can be up to 15 characters for each
                                                                               item, and its Length (up to 24 characters). In the
                                                                               above example Gender only needs to be 1 length
                                                                               because you only want an M of F to be entered,
                                                                               where as Shoe Size needs to be a length of 3 to fit
                                                                               sizes such as 110.

                                                                               Save Mail Detail: You can, optionally, also Save
                                                                               Mail Detail information (information about each
                                                                               SKU purchased). Then, when printing the mailing
                                                                               list, you could select customers that have
                                                                               purchased a specific SKU, or purchased from a
                                                                               particular vendor, category, or purchased an item
                                                                               on a specific date. This information, however,
                                                                               does consume extra disk space.

                                                                               Omit these categories from posting to Mail
Detail: Assume you have categories for accessories (shoe strings, polish, etc.), and you do not want to keep
sales of these items in the customer detail. Enter these category numbers or ranges in the Omit these
categories from posting to Mail Detail field. These categories are still posted to the sales and inventory
files, they are just not added the mailing list detail file (customer detail).

Prevent these categories from adding quantities to purchase totals: Assume you have SKUs in
categories to track coupons, promotions or special discounts, and you do not want to have these added to the
customer purchase quantity totals. Enter these category numbers or ranges in the Prevent these categories
from adding quantities to purchase totals field. These categories are still posted to the sales and inventory
files. They are just not added to the customer purchase quantity totals.

Season Setup

              Define your seasons

              218
When entering a SKU, assign a season code to each SKU. When printing reports you may then choose to
print only selected seasons. Using this menu option, you can assign a description (up to 8 characters) for up
to 20 different seasons.
You may want to create one season for Old, Hashed, Past, or Previous seasons. When you have used all 20
seasons and you need to create a new season, move your oldest season(s) to this season. See Change
Seasons.
You may also want to create another season for All Year round or Basic merchandise and then run reports on
just your Basic merchandise, new season, or any combination of seasons.

System Status Report

                             Information on your job history, files, and system information
Print Job history - is a list of options that were selected from the menu for up to the last 2 months. You can
enter a date range to use this option to determine if a particular option was done, and if so, by whom and
when.
Print File Statistics - is a list of each of the data files in RICS showing the number of records and the size of
each file in kilo-bytes.
Print RICS System Information - is a list of information setup in RICS which includes Company, Mail List
and Season Setups, along with the RICS.CFG and Vendor.CFG files.
